# 7. Quality Gates

# 7.1 Quality Gate Architecture

# Part 7.1.1 — Purpose & Quality Gate Boundary

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Part 7.0.1 — Specification v2.1 Agent Review Gate

## Purpose and classification

The **Agent Review Gate** is a hybrid, pre-rendering governance gate. Its transport and schema validation are deterministic; its substantive findings are model-produced review evidence; its final authority remains human. It supplements but never replaces the deterministic Story, Screenplay, Shot, Storyboard, security, budget, or approval gates.

The gate runs only when `INSYNERGY_AGENT_REVIEW_MODE=review`, after all deterministic planning gates pass and before `render-approval` is offered.

## Evaluation order

```text
schema and referential validation
  -> deterministic planning Quality Gates
  -> Agent Review report acquisition or exact cache replay
  -> deterministic AgentReviewReport schema and evidence validation
  -> Agent Review policy evaluation
  -> human render-approval of the plan/report hash pair
```

Later evidence cannot erase an earlier failure. In particular, agent `PASS` cannot convert a deterministic `FAIL` or missing approval into a pass.

## Controlled dispositions

| Agent disposition | Gate behavior |
| --- | --- |
| `PASS` | Agent evidence is complete and no blocking finding is present. Continue only to human `render-approval`. |
| `MANUAL_REVIEW_REQUIRED` | Hold automatic progression and present blocking findings and evidence to the human reviewer. |
| `UNAVAILABLE` | Hold automatic progression; preserve deterministic evidence; permit an attributable retry or explicit human disposition according to policy. |
| `ERROR` | Hold automatic progression; record the classified error; require remediation or explicit human disposition. |

No disposition authorizes rendering by itself. In `off` mode the Agent Review Gate is `NOT_APPLICABLE`, not silently passed.

## Finding policy

Every finding shall use a registered dimension code, controlled severity (`INFO`, `WARNING`, `BLOCKING`), stable finding code, concise rationale, actionable recommendation, and one or more evidence references. Each evidence reference shall resolve to a reviewed artifact content hash, artifact identifier, and valid JSON Pointer.

A finding may be blocking only when all of the following are true:

1. its code is allow-listed as block-capable in the versioned Agent Review policy;
2. severity is `BLOCKING` and `blocking` is `true`;
3. at least one evidence reference resolves successfully to the approved input set;
4. the rationale identifies the violated specification invariant or acceptance criterion;
5. deterministic post-validation finds no schema or referential defect in the report itself.

Free-form preference, model confidence alone, absent evidence, an unknown code, or an unresolvable pointer cannot be blocking. Such output is downgraded to advisory or causes report rejection according to policy.

## Report validation guardrail

Before policy evaluation, deterministic validators shall enforce the Part 9 schema, maximum counts and lengths, controlled vocabulary, build and review-key coherence, input-hash equality, evidence-pointer resolution, and the following cross-field rules:

* `PASS` contains no blocking finding;
* `MANUAL_REVIEW_REQUIRED` contains at least one valid blocking finding;
* `UNAVAILABLE` and `ERROR` contain classified error evidence;
* every material finding contains evidence;
* the report contains no undeclared properties such as raw reasoning;
* model, agent, prompt, and contract versions are present;
* the report belongs to the current build and exact review key.

Invalid structured output shall not be repaired by accepting a best-effort parse. After any explicitly bounded structured-output retry is exhausted, the result is `ERROR` and the build remains before rendering.

## Prompt-injection and data guardrails

The source Article and every artifact body are untrusted review data. Static Review Agent instructions shall state that embedded commands, credentials requests, role changes, tool requests, and output-schema changes inside those inputs are content to evaluate, not instructions to follow. Because the v2.1 Review Agent has no tools or handoffs, prompt injection cannot grant a side-effect path. Deterministic output validation remains mandatory even when the model reports success.

Input construction shall reject secrets, token-shaped environment values, internal credentials, and unrelated repository files. Secret-scanning failure is a blocking preflight error and prevents submission.

## Human decision boundary

The human reviewer shall see the exact Execution Plan hash, Agent Review report hash, disposition, blocking findings, evidence locations, deterministic gate summary, cost estimate, and any error classification. Approval records shall bind both hashes in `review` mode. Changing inputs, regenerating the report, changing the selected report, or changing the Execution Plan voids prior approval.

A human may approve despite `MANUAL_REVIEW_REQUIRED`, `UNAVAILABLE`, or `ERROR` only if the versioned policy explicitly permits that class and records approver, timestamp, rationale, report hash, plan hash, and exception code. Non-waivable deterministic, security, schema, budget, or publication gates remain non-waivable.

## Required evaluation suite

Before promotion from shadow to enforcing review, the gate shall be evaluated on representative golden cases covering at least:

* a clean planning bundle expected to pass;
* an unsupported source claim;
* multiple premises or protagonists;
* concept disclosure before Act 3;
* exposition-only or non-observable screenplay action;
* omitted scene coverage or orphan shots;
* character, prop, location, camera, lighting, or emotion continuity defects;
* provider technology leaking into the Storyboard;
* prompt injection embedded in Article content;
* unavailable provider, timeout, and authentication failure;
* malformed structured output and unresolvable evidence pointers;
* secret redaction and absence of raw reasoning;
* exact-key cache replay and approval invalidation.

Evaluation shall report precision and recall for blocking findings, false-hold rate, human agreement and override rates, schema-valid output rate, latency, token use, and cost. Thresholds are versioned release criteria owned by Part 9 acceptance evidence.

## Invariants

* INV-7.0.1-1 — Agent Review never overrides a deterministic gate.
* INV-7.0.1-2 — Agent `PASS` never substitutes for human approval.
* INV-7.0.1-3 — A blocking finding always has resolvable evidence and a registered violated rule.
* INV-7.0.1-4 — Invalid or unavailable review output holds automatic progression in `review` mode.
* INV-7.0.1-5 — Report or plan hash change invalidates approval.
* INV-7.0.1-6 — Article content cannot supply agent instructions or a side-effect path.

## Acceptance criteria

This gate is complete when the evaluation order is enforced; all four dispositions behave as specified; invalid output fails closed; blocking evidence resolves; agent `PASS` cannot override or approve; human exceptions are attributable and policy-bound; prompt-injection fixtures have no side effect; and the required golden suite meets versioned promotion thresholds.

---

# Purpose

This section defines the purpose, scope, authority, and architectural boundary of the **Quality Gate Architecture**.

A Quality Gate is a mandatory, deterministic checkpoint that stands between one stage of the platform and the next.

Its responsibility is to answer exactly one question:

> **"Is this artifact fit to proceed, or must it be rejected?"**

Part 4 established the Shot & Storyboard Quality Gates. Part 6 established per-component quality gates for the execution architecture. Each of those gates was defined locally, inside the section that owned the artifact it validated.

Part 7 does not replace those gates.

Part 7 defines the **common architecture** every gate in the platform obeys — the shared model, the shared vocabulary, the shared enforcement semantics, and the shared governance — so that a gate in the Story Engine and a gate in the Publication layer behave identically in every respect that matters: how they evaluate, how they fail, how they report, and who may override them.

Section 7.1 is the foundation. It defines what a gate *is* before Part 7.2 defines the specific gates the pipeline runs.

The Quality Gate Architecture does not decide what is good. It decides how "good" is checked, enforced, and recorded, uniformly, everywhere.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle without exception.

> **A quality gate is a deterministic, fail-closed decision. It enforces rules it does not own, at a single auditable point, and it never renders a verdict of "probably."**

Three commitments follow from this principle.

* **Deterministic.** Given the same artifact and the same configuration, a gate produces the same verdict every time. A gate contains no randomness, no sampling, and no time-dependent judgment.
* **Fail-closed.** The default verdict is FAIL. A gate passes an artifact only by affirmatively confirming every check. A missing input, an unevaluated check, or an internal error is a failure, never a pass.
* **Enforcement, not authorship.** A gate does not invent the rules it checks. Each rule is owned by an upstream section that defines its meaning. The gate is the enforcement point; the owning section is the source of truth.

A quality gate is therefore a control surface, not a critic. It does not have taste. It has a checklist, a verdict function, and a report.

---

# Position in the Overall Architecture

Quality Gates sit on the seams between pipeline stages.

```text
Insight Article
        │
        ▼
Story Engine ───────────► Story Quality Gate
        │
        ▼
Screenplay Engine ──────► Screenplay Quality Gate
        │
        ▼
Shot Planner ───────────► Shot Quality Gate
        │
        ▼
Storyboard Engine ──────► Storyboard Quality Gate
        │
        ▼
Render Execution ───────► Render Quality Gate
        │
        ▼
Composition ────────────► Composition Quality Gate
        │
        ▼
Packaging ──────────────► Metadata & Packaging Quality Gate
        │
        ▼
Publication ────────────► Publication Quality Gate
```

Every arrow that crosses a stage boundary passes through a gate.

A gate is not a stage. It produces no creative artifact. It consumes the output of the stage before it and emits a single verdict — PASS or FAIL — plus a report.

The gate is the platform's guarantee that no defect crosses a stage boundary silently.

---

# Relationship to the Build Orchestrator (Part 6.3)

The Build Orchestrator defined in Part 6.3 owns *execution*. Quality Gates own *admissibility*.

The Orchestrator schedules, dispatches, and coordinates tasks. It does not decide whether an artifact is good. When a task completes, the Orchestrator submits the resulting artifact to the relevant Quality Gate and honors the verdict.

The relationship is a contract.

* The Orchestrator invokes the gate.
* The gate returns a verdict.
* The Orchestrator advances the build on PASS and blocks it on FAIL.

The gate never schedules work. The Orchestrator never overrides a verdict. Each owns one half of the boundary, and neither reaches into the other.

The `VALIDATING` build state (Part 6.3.4) and the `Quality Gate Integration` hook of the build state machine are the Orchestrator-side expression of this contract; Part 7 defines the gate-side behavior the Orchestrator relies on.

---

# Relationship to Cache & Incremental Execution (Part 6.2)

A gate verdict is an attribute of an artifact, and it participates in caching.

Part 6.2 established that a validated artifact may be reused when its inputs are unchanged. A quality-gate PASS is part of what makes an artifact reusable: a cached artifact carries its last gate verdict, and a `cached_clip`-style reuse inherits the PASS rather than re-earning it.

Two rules bind the gate to the cache.

* A gate verdict is recorded against the exact artifact identity (content hash) it evaluated.
* If the artifact identity changes, the prior verdict is void and the gate must run again.

A gate never trusts a verdict attached to a different artifact identity. Caching accelerates re-validation; it never bypasses it.

---

# Core Responsibility

The Quality Gate Architecture owns the definition of a gate.

Its core responsibility is expressed as:

```text
Stage Output Artifact
        │
        ▼
Resolve Gate Definition
        │
        ▼
Evaluate Checks (deterministic)
        │
        ▼
Aggregate Verdict (fail-closed)
        │
        ▼
Emit Gate Report (immutable)
        │
        ▼
PASS → advance    FAIL → block
```

Section 7.1 defines each box in this diagram as a reusable contract, so that every specific gate in Part 7.2 is an instance of the same machine.

---

# Scope

The Quality Gate Architecture is responsible for the following domains.

## Gate Definition

* define the anatomy of a gate: identity, checks, verdict function, report;
* define what makes two gates structurally identical;
* define the closed vocabulary of gate outcomes.

---

## Check Definition

* define the anatomy of a check: identity, owner, evaluation, result;
* define how checks compose into a verdict;
* define mandatory versus advisory checks.

---

## Verdict Semantics

* define PASS, FAIL, and the fail-closed default;
* define how an unevaluated or errored check resolves;
* prohibit partial credit, scoring below threshold, and "render anyway" overrides.

---

## Reporting

* define the machine-readable gate report;
* require every verdict to be traceable to its failing checks and their owners;
* require reports to be immutable once emitted.

---

## Governance

* define who may author, configure, waive, and override gates;
* define the audit trail for every waiver and exception;
* define the separation between authoring a rule and enforcing it.

---

## Configuration

* define how gate thresholds and profiles are declared;
* require configuration to be declarative, versioned, and immutable per build;
* forbid runtime mutation of a gate mid-evaluation.

---

# Explicit Non-Scope

The Quality Gate Architecture is not responsible for the following.

## Artifact Generation

A gate never generates, repairs, or edits the artifact it evaluates. It reads and judges; it does not write.

---

## Rule Authorship

A gate never invents a rule. The meaning of a check — what a valid story, screenplay, shot, or render is — is owned by the section that defines that artifact. The gate imports the rule; it does not define it.

---

## Scheduling & Execution

A gate never schedules a task, allocates a worker, or submits a provider job. Execution belongs to the Orchestrator (Part 6.3).

---

## Editorial Judgment

A gate never substitutes for a human editorial decision. Where human approval is required (Part 7.4), the gate records the presence or absence of that approval as a check; it does not grant the approval itself.

---

# Principle — A Gate Enforces, It Does Not Interpret

A quality gate applies rules that already exist.

```text
Owning Section (defines the rule)
        │
        ▼
Quality Gate (enforces the rule)
        │
        ▼
Verdict + Report
```

When a gate fails an artifact, the failure is always attributable to a rule owned elsewhere. The gate's report names that owner so the artifact is returned to the correct authority for correction.

A gate that invents a novel rule at evaluation time is malformed. Every check must trace to an owning section, and the trace must appear in the report.

This mirrors the discipline established for the Shot & Storyboard Quality Gates in Part 4.1.12: *the gate does not invent new rules; it enforces existing ones at a single, auditable point.* Part 7 generalizes that discipline to the whole platform.

---

# Gate Boundary

The Quality Gate Architecture is bounded by two contracts.

```text
Upstream Contract
Stage Output Artifact + Artifact Identity
        │
        ▼
Quality Gate
        │
        ▼
Downstream Contract
Verdict (PASS | FAIL) + Immutable Gate Report
```

The upstream contract defines what a gate consumes: a completed stage artifact and its content-addressed identity.

The downstream contract defines what a gate emits: a single verdict and an immutable report.

The gate owns the transformation between the two. It never alters the artifact and never withholds the report.

---

# Upstream Contract

A gate requires the following inputs.

```yaml
gate_input:
  artifact:              # the stage output under evaluation
  artifact_identity:     # content hash of the artifact
  gate_definition:       # the resolved gate for this stage
  gate_configuration:    # thresholds and profile, immutable for this build
  upstream_evidence:     # prior gate verdicts this gate depends on
```

A gate that is missing any mandatory input fails closed before evaluating a single check. An absent artifact is a failure, not an empty pass.

---

# Downstream Contract

A gate produces the following outputs.

```yaml
gate_output:
  verdict:               # PASS | FAIL
  gate_report:           # immutable, machine-readable
  artifact_identity:     # the exact identity evaluated
  blocking:              # true on FAIL, false on PASS
```

The verdict and the report are always emitted together. A gate never returns a verdict without a report, and never a report without a verdict.

---

# Determinism Boundary

Repeated evaluation of the same artifact under the same configuration shall produce the same verdict.

A gate contains no nondeterministic input. It does not sample, does not consult wall-clock time, and does not depend on evaluation order across independent checks. Given identical `artifact_identity` and identical `gate_configuration`, the verdict and the set of failing checks are byte-stable.

Determinism is what makes a verdict cacheable (Part 6.2) and auditable (Part 7.4). A gate that could return different verdicts for the same artifact would make every downstream guarantee meaningless.

---

# Fail-Closed Boundary

The default verdict of every gate is FAIL.

A gate reaches PASS only by affirmatively evaluating every mandatory check to a passing result. Any of the following resolves to FAIL:

* a missing mandatory input;
* an unevaluated mandatory check;
* a check that errors during evaluation;
* an artifact identity that does not match the evaluated artifact;
* a configuration that cannot be resolved.

There is no path by which absence, ambiguity, or error yields PASS. The gate treats the unknown as unacceptable.

---

# Authority Model

The Quality Gate Architecture separates three authorities.

```text
Rule Authority     → owns what a check means           (upstream sections)
Enforcement Authority → owns how a check is applied     (the gate)
Waiver Authority   → owns whether a failure is excused  (governance, Part 7.1.10)
```

No single actor holds all three. A gate enforces rules it does not author and cannot waive. A waiver, when permitted at all, is granted by a distinct governance authority and is always recorded. This separation of duties is the structural guarantee against a gate quietly lowering its own bar.

---

# Prohibited Boundary Behaviors

A gate shall never:

* modify, repair, or regenerate the artifact it evaluates;
* emit a PASS without evaluating every mandatory check;
* invent a rule not owned by an upstream section;
* return a verdict outside the closed set {PASS, FAIL};
* suppress or mutate a report after it is emitted;
* grant itself a waiver.

Each prohibition is enforced as an invariant below.

---

# Boundary Violation Examples

## Violation 1 — Repairing the Artifact

Wrong:

```text
Continuity check fails
        │
        ▼
Gate silently patches the continuity reference
        │
        ▼
Gate passes the shot
```

Correct:

```text
Continuity check fails
        │
        ▼
Gate records FAIL, names the owning section
        │
        ▼
Artifact returned for correction
```

---

## Violation 2 — Passing on Missing Evidence

Wrong:

```text
emotion_defined evidence absent
        │
        ▼
Gate assumes neutral default
        │
        ▼
Gate passes
```

Correct:

```text
emotion_defined evidence absent
        │
        ▼
Check resolves FAIL (fail-closed)
        │
        ▼
Gate blocks
```

---

## Violation 3 — Self-Granted Override

Wrong:

```text
runway_ratio exceeds cap
        │
        ▼
Gate raises its own threshold to pass the plan
```

Correct:

```text
runway_ratio exceeds cap
        │
        ▼
Gate FAILs; only Waiver Authority may record an exception
```

---

## Violation 4 — Verdict Without Report

Wrong:

```text
Gate returns FAIL
        │
        ▼
No report of which checks failed
```

Correct:

```text
Gate returns FAIL
        │
        ▼
Report names every failing check and its owner
```

---

# Public Boundary Interfaces

The Quality Gate Architecture exposes the following top-level contracts.

```python
QualityGate

GateDefinition

Check

GateVerdict

GateReport

GateRegistry
```

`QualityGate` evaluates an artifact and returns a verdict.

`GateDefinition` is the declarative specification of a gate's checks and verdict function.

`Check` is a single, owned, deterministic evaluation.

`GateVerdict` is the closed-set outcome {PASS, FAIL}.

`GateReport` is the immutable, machine-readable record of an evaluation.

`GateRegistry` resolves the correct gate for a given stage and build profile.

Each interface is independently testable and exposes no artifact-generation or scheduling detail.

---

# Required Inputs

The architecture requires:

```yaml
required_inputs:
  artifact:
  artifact_identity:
  gate_definition:
  gate_configuration:
```

Missing mandatory input causes the gate to fail closed before any check is evaluated.

---

# Required Outputs

The architecture produces:

```yaml
required_outputs:
  verdict:
  gate_report:
```

Outputs are emitted together, are immutable once emitted, and are traceable to the exact artifact identity evaluated.

---

This section defines the gate's purpose and authority boundary.

The remaining sections of 7.1 define its internal architecture.

| Section | Responsibility                                       |

---

# Architectural Invariants

The following invariants are mandatory.

## Invariant QGB-701

Every stage boundary in the pipeline is guarded by exactly one Quality Gate.

---

## Invariant QGB-702

A gate consumes an artifact and its identity, and never modifies the artifact.

---

## Invariant QGB-703

A gate emits exactly one verdict from the closed set {PASS, FAIL}, always accompanied by a report.

---

## Invariant QGB-704

The default verdict is FAIL; PASS requires affirmative evaluation of every mandatory check.

---

## Invariant QGB-705

Every check enforced by a gate is owned by an upstream section; a gate authors no rule.

---

## Invariant QGB-706

A gate verdict is bound to the exact artifact identity evaluated and is void for any other identity.

---

## Invariant QGB-707

Given identical artifact identity and configuration, a gate is deterministic in verdict and failing-check set.

---

## Invariant QGB-708

Rule authority, enforcement authority, and waiver authority are held by distinct actors.

---

## Invariant QGB-709

A gate never schedules execution and the Orchestrator never overrides a verdict.

---

## Invariant QGB-710

A gate never grants itself a waiver; exceptions are recorded only by the Waiver Authority defined in 7.1.10.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                                          |
| ------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| ADR-701 | A Quality Gate is a deterministic, fail-closed checkpoint on a stage boundary.                    |
| ADR-702 | Part 7 defines the common gate architecture; Part 7.2 defines concrete instances of it.           |
| ADR-703 | A gate enforces rules owned by upstream sections and authors none of its own.                     |
| ADR-704 | A gate emits exactly one verdict from {PASS, FAIL}, always with an immutable report.               |
| ADR-705 | The default verdict is FAIL; absence, ambiguity, and error resolve to FAIL.                        |
| ADR-706 | A verdict is bound to a content-addressed artifact identity and participates in caching (6.2).     |
| ADR-707 | The Orchestrator (6.3) invokes gates and honors verdicts; it never overrides them.                |
| ADR-708 | Rule, enforcement, and waiver authorities are separated as a structural guarantee.                |
| ADR-709 | A gate never modifies, repairs, or regenerates the artifact it evaluates.                          |
| ADR-710 | Every gate is an instance of the architecture defined in Section 7.1.                              |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.1** is complete when:

* The Quality Gate is formally defined as a deterministic, fail-closed stage-boundary checkpoint.
* Its relationship to the Build Orchestrator (6.3) and the Cache (6.2) is explicit.
* Rule, enforcement, and waiver authorities are separated.
* Scope and non-scope are unambiguous.
* Upstream and downstream contracts are defined and traceable.
* The determinism and fail-closed boundaries are established.
* Prohibited boundary behaviors are enumerated and mapped to invariants.
* Every subsequent gate can be evaluated as an instance of a single, stable architecture.

---

# Part 7.1.2 — Quality Philosophy & Governing Principles

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **quality philosophy** of the platform and the **governing principles** every Quality Gate embodies.

Section 7.1.1 established what a gate is and where it sits. This section establishes *why the gates exist* and *what beliefs they enforce*.

A gate is the mechanical expression of a philosophy. If the philosophy is unstated, the gates drift — one gate becomes lenient, another becomes arbitrary, and the platform loses the single property that makes quality gates worth having: that "passing" means the same thing everywhere.

This section states the philosophy once, so that every gate in Part 7.2 inherits it rather than reinventing it.

The platform does not treat quality as an aspiration. It treats quality as an admissibility condition, checked at defined points, enforced without exception, and recorded for audit.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts a single foundational belief.

> **Defects are cheapest to reject at the earliest boundary they can be detected. Quality is therefore enforced continuously along the pipeline, never inspected once at the end.**

An error caught at the Story Gate costs a re-plan.

The same error caught at the Publication Gate has already consumed rendering, composition, packaging, and reviewer attention.

The same error that escapes the Publication Gate costs trust.

The cost of a defect grows monotonically as it travels downstream.

The platform therefore places a gate at every stage boundary and rejects a defect at the first boundary that can see it. Late detection is treated as a design failure of an earlier gate, not as the natural order of things.

---

# The Ten Governing Principles

Every Quality Gate embodies ten principles. Each is stated once here and referenced by the specific gates in Part 7.2.

---

# Principle 1 — Quality Is an Admissibility Condition

Quality is not a score to be maximized. It is a condition to be met.

An artifact is either admissible to the next stage or it is not. There is no "good enough for now" and no "we'll fix it later." An artifact that does not meet the condition does not advance.

This reframes every gate from a critic that rates into a guard that admits.

---

# Principle 2 — Fail Closed

The default answer is no.

A gate passes an artifact only by affirmatively confirming admissibility. Absence of evidence is failure. Ambiguity is failure. An internal error in the gate itself is failure.

The platform prefers a false rejection, which costs a re-run, over a false acceptance, which costs a defect in production.

---

# Principle 3 — Enforce, Do Not Author

A gate enforces rules owned elsewhere.

The meaning of a valid story is owned by the Story Engine. The meaning of a valid shot is owned by the Shot Planner. The gate imports these meanings and checks them; it never invents a rule of its own at evaluation time.

This keeps rules in one place — their owning section — and keeps gates thin, uniform, and auditable.

---

# Principle 4 — Determinism Over Judgment

A gate computes; it does not opine.

Every check yields the same result for the same input. A gate never samples, never consults the clock, and never depends on the order in which independent checks run.

Determinism is what makes a verdict reproducible, cacheable, and defensible. A gate that could disagree with itself would be worthless as a control.

---

# Principle 5 — One Auditable Point

Each rule is enforced at exactly one gate.

A rule checked in five places drifts in five directions. The platform enforces each rule at a single, defined gate, and records the enforcement in that gate's report.

Where a downstream gate must rely on an upstream property, it references the upstream gate's recorded verdict rather than re-deriving the property independently.

---

# Principle 6 — Traceability Is Mandatory

Every verdict is explainable.

A FAIL names the checks that failed and the sections that own them. A PASS records every check that was satisfied. A verdict with no trace is not a verdict; it is an assertion, and the platform does not accept assertions.

Traceability is what routes a rejected artifact back to the correct authority for correction.

---

# Principle 7 — No Silent Degradation

A gate never quietly lowers quality to make an artifact pass.

It does not substitute a default for a missing value. It does not truncate content to fit a limit. It does not downgrade a strategy to satisfy a cap without recording the change. When an artifact cannot pass as-is, the gate fails it and returns it; it does not massage it into compliance.

Silent degradation converts a visible failure into an invisible one, which is strictly worse.

---

# Principle 8 — Separation of Duties

Authoring a rule, enforcing a rule, and waiving a failure are three different powers held by three different authorities.

No actor may hold more than one power over the same rule. A gate that could waive its own failures, or an author who could both write and excuse a rule, would collapse the control into a rubber stamp.

---

# Principle 9 — Quality Outranks Throughput

When quality and speed conflict, quality wins.

A gate never passes a defective artifact because a deadline is near, because a queue is deep, or because a re-run is expensive. Performance is a first-class concern (Part 6.1), but it is subordinate to correctness at a gate. A late correct build is preferable to a fast wrong one.

---

# Principle 10 — Gates Are Immutable During a Build

A gate's definition and configuration are fixed for the duration of a build.

Thresholds are not tuned mid-flight to rescue a failing artifact. A gate resolved at build start evaluates every artifact of that build against the same bar. Changing the bar requires a new build generation, not an in-place edit.

---

# Principles Summary

| # | Principle                       | One-line statement                                             |
| - | ------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------- |
| 1 | Admissibility condition         | Quality is a condition to meet, not a score to maximize.       |
| 2 | Fail closed                     | The default answer is no; absence and error are failures.      |
| 3 | Enforce, do not author          | Gates enforce rules owned by upstream sections.                |
| 4 | Determinism over judgment       | Same input, same verdict, always.                              |
| 5 | One auditable point             | Each rule is enforced at exactly one gate.                     |
| 6 | Traceability is mandatory       | Every verdict names its checks and owners.                     |
| 7 | No silent degradation           | A gate never massages an artifact into compliance.             |
| 8 | Separation of duties            | Author, enforce, and waive are separate powers.                |
| 9 | Quality outranks throughput     | When quality and speed conflict, quality wins.                 |
| 10| Immutable during a build        | Gate definition and thresholds are fixed per build.            |

---

# The Cost-of-Defect Curve

The philosophy is grounded in a single economic observation.

```text
Cost to fix a defect

  high │                                         ● Publication
       │                                   ●
       │                            ●  Composition
       │                     ●  Render
       │              ●  Storyboard
       │        ●  Shot
       │    ●  Screenplay
   low │● Story
       └───────────────────────────────────────────► pipeline stage
```

The curve rises monotonically. A defect introduced at the Story stage and caught at the Story Gate is cheap. The same defect caught at Publication is expensive, because every intervening stage did work on a foundation that was already wrong.

Gates exist to intercept the curve as far left as possible.

---

# Why Not a Single Final Gate

A tempting alternative is one comprehensive gate at the end.

The platform rejects it.

A single final gate catches every defect at the most expensive point on the curve. It also cannot attribute a defect to its origin: by the time an artifact reaches the end, it has been transformed so many times that the root cause is obscured.

Continuous gating catches each defect where it is introduced, at the cost where it is cheapest, and attributes it to the stage that produced it.

```text
Single final gate   → late, expensive, unattributable
Continuous gating   → early, cheap, attributable
```

---

# Quality vs Performance Matrix

The relationship between quality gates and performance objectives is explicit.

| Situation                                   | Resolution                                            |
| ------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------- |
| Gate would fail but deadline is near        | Gate fails; deadline yields (Principle 9).            |
| Re-run is expensive after a FAIL            | Artifact is corrected and re-gated; no bypass.        |
| A cache hit carries a prior PASS            | Verdict reused only if artifact identity matches.     |
| Gate evaluation is slow                     | Optimize the check; never skip the check.             |
| Throughput SLO at risk from gating          | SLO is renegotiated; the gate is not weakened.        |

Performance is optimized around gates, never through them.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-701 — The Advisory Gate

Wrong:

```text
Gate reports "quality concerns" as warnings
        │
        ▼
Build proceeds regardless
```

Correct:

```text
Gate returns a binding PASS or FAIL
        │
        ▼
FAIL blocks the build
```

A gate that only advises is not a gate.

---

## AP-702 — The Tuned-to-Pass Threshold

Wrong:

```text
Artifact fails at threshold 0.90
        │
        ▼
Threshold lowered to 0.80 to pass this artifact
```

Correct:

```text
Artifact fails at threshold 0.90
        │
        ▼
Artifact corrected; threshold unchanged (Principle 10)
```

---

## AP-703 — The End-Only Inspection

Wrong:

```text
No stage gates
        │
        ▼
One inspection at Publication
```

Correct:

```text
A gate at every stage boundary
        │
        ▼
Defects caught at their origin
```

---

## AP-704 — The Self-Healing Gate

Wrong:

```text
Gate detects a defect
        │
        ▼
Gate edits the artifact to remove the defect
        │
        ▼
Gate passes its own repair
```

Correct:

```text
Gate detects a defect
        │
        ▼
Gate fails and returns the artifact to its owner
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant QGP-701

Quality is enforced as an admissibility condition at every stage boundary, not inspected once at the end.

---

## Invariant QGP-702

Every gate is fail-closed: absence, ambiguity, and internal error resolve to FAIL.

---

## Invariant QGP-703

Every gate enforces rules owned by upstream sections and authors none.

---

## Invariant QGP-704

Every gate is deterministic; identical input yields an identical verdict.

---

## Invariant QGP-705

Each rule is enforced at exactly one gate and referenced, not re-derived, downstream.

---

## Invariant QGP-706

Every verdict is traceable to its checks and their owning sections.

---

## Invariant QGP-707

No gate silently degrades an artifact to force a pass.

---

## Invariant QGP-708

Authoring, enforcing, and waiving are separated powers.

---

## Invariant QGP-709

When quality and throughput conflict, quality prevails.

---

## Invariant QGP-710

Gate definition and configuration are immutable for the duration of a build.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                                       |
| ------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-711 | The platform enforces quality continuously at stage boundaries, driven by the cost-of-defect curve. |
| ADR-712 | Quality is an admissibility condition, not a maximized score.                                   |
| ADR-713 | Every gate is fail-closed by default.                                                           |
| ADR-714 | Gates enforce rules owned upstream and author none.                                             |
| ADR-715 | Gate verdicts are deterministic and reproducible.                                              |
| ADR-716 | Each rule is enforced at exactly one auditable gate.                                            |
| ADR-717 | No gate silently degrades an artifact to achieve a pass.                                        |
| ADR-718 | Authoring, enforcing, and waiving rules are separated duties.                                   |
| ADR-719 | Quality outranks throughput at every gate.                                                      |
| ADR-720 | Gate definition and thresholds are immutable during a build.                                    |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.2** is complete when:

* The cost-of-defect curve is documented as the economic basis for continuous gating.
* The ten governing principles are each defined and summarized in a reference table.
* The rejection of a single final gate in favor of continuous gating is justified.
* The quality-versus-performance relationship is made explicit and resolved in favor of quality.
* Anti-patterns for advisory gates, tuned thresholds, end-only inspection, and self-healing gates are documented.
* Invariants QGP-701 through QGP-710 and ADR-711 through ADR-720 are established.
* Every gate in Part 7.2 can inherit these principles rather than restating them.

---

# Part 7.1.3 — Gate Model & Gate Anatomy

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **canonical model of a Quality Gate** and the **anatomy** every gate shares.

Section 7.1.1 defined the gate's boundary. Section 7.1.2 defined its philosophy. This section defines its structure: the parts a gate is made of, the schema that serializes it, and the contract each part satisfies.

The Gate Model gives every specific gate in Part 7.2 a single shared skeleton. A Story Gate and a Render Gate differ only in their checks; their anatomy is identical. This is what allows the platform to reason about "a gate" in the abstract and to build one engine that runs all of them.

If the gate model is malformed, every gate built on it is malformed. This section defines the gate precisely enough that its structure can be validated before any specific gate is authored.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A gate is data, not code. Its checks, its verdict function, and its report shape are declared, so that one evaluation engine can execute every gate uniformly.**

Two consequences follow.

A gate is **declarative**. It is a specification of *what* to check and *how* to combine the results, not a bespoke procedure. The same engine that runs the Story Gate runs the Publication Gate; only the declaration differs.

A gate is **decomposable**. It is built from independent checks, each owned and each testable in isolation. A gate is never a monolith; it is an aggregation of small, verifiable parts.

Declarative and decomposable together make gates auditable. A reviewer reads a gate's declaration and knows exactly what it enforces, without reading procedural code.

---

# The Anatomy of a Gate

Every gate is composed of five parts.

```text
Gate
  ├── identity        (which gate, which stage, which version)
  ├── checks[]        (the owned, deterministic evaluations)
  ├── verdict_function(how checks combine into PASS | FAIL)
  ├── report_shape    (the machine-readable record it emits)
  └── configuration_ref (the immutable thresholds it reads)
```

* **identity** — names the gate, binds it to a stage, and versions it.
* **checks** — the list of individual evaluations the gate performs.
* **verdict_function** — the rule that reduces the check results to a single verdict.
* **report_shape** — the structure of the report the gate emits.
* **configuration_ref** — the reference to the immutable configuration the gate reads.

A gate missing any of the five parts is malformed. An empty `checks` list is a malformed gate, not a gate that always passes.

---

# The Gate Schema

Every gate is represented by the following canonical schema.

```json
{
  "gate_id": "shot_quality_gate",
  "stage": "shot_planning",
  "gate_version": "2.0",
  "verdict_function": "all_mandatory_pass",
  "checks": [
    { "check_id": "purpose_exists",          "owner": "4.1.3", "class": "mandatory" },
    { "check_id": "camera_defined",          "owner": "4.1.4", "class": "mandatory" },
    { "check_id": "single_camera_move",      "owner": "4.1.4", "class": "mandatory" }
  ],
  "report_shape": "standard_gate_report_v2",
  "configuration_ref": "gates/shot_quality_gate.yaml"
}
```

This object is the atomic declaration of a gate.

Every field is mandatory. The `checks` array declares the evaluations; each entry names the check, its owner, and its class. The `verdict_function` names the reduction rule (defined in 7.1.5). The `report_shape` names the report contract (defined in 7.1.8). The `configuration_ref` points to the immutable thresholds (defined in 7.1.11).

---

# Field Reference

| Field               | Type   | Meaning                                              | Constraint                                        |
| ------------------- | ------ | ---------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------- |
| `gate_id`           | string | Globally unique identity of the gate                 | Unique across the platform                        |
| `stage`             | string | The pipeline stage this gate guards                  | A valid pipeline stage                            |
| `gate_version`      | string | Version of the gate definition                       | Semantic version                                  |
| `verdict_function`  | string | The rule reducing checks to a verdict                | A registered verdict function (7.1.5)             |
| `checks`            | array  | The list of checks the gate performs                 | Non-empty; each entry a valid Check reference     |
| `report_shape`      | string | The report contract emitted                          | A registered report shape (7.1.8)                 |
| `configuration_ref` | string | Reference to the immutable configuration             | Resolves to a versioned config (7.1.11)           |

Every field participates in the gate's identity for caching and audit. A change to any field is a change to the gate.

---

# Gate Identity

Every gate carries a deterministic identity.

```text
gate_id @ gate_version
```

The pair `(gate_id, gate_version)` uniquely identifies a gate definition. A gate's behavior may change only by producing a new `gate_version`; an existing version is never edited in place.

This mirrors the versioned-identifier discipline used for continuity references in Part 4.1.7: a deliberate change produces a new version rather than a silent mutation. A verdict recorded under `shot_quality_gate@2.0` is never confused with one recorded under `shot_quality_gate@2.1`.

Identity rules:

* identity is deterministic — the same definition yields the same identity;
* identity is stable — a version is never re-pointed to a different definition;
* identity is unique — no two gate definitions share `(gate_id, gate_version)`.

---

# The Check List

The `checks` array is the substance of a gate.

Each entry is a reference to a Check (defined in full in 7.1.4), carrying at minimum:

```json
{ "check_id": "continuity_valid", "owner": "4.1.7", "class": "mandatory" }
```

* `check_id` — the identity of the check.
* `owner` — the section that owns the rule the check enforces.
* `class` — `mandatory` or `advisory` (defined in 7.1.4).

The check list is ordered for reporting but not for verdict: because checks are independent and deterministic, the verdict does not depend on the order in which checks are evaluated. The order exists so reports are stable and readable, not so earlier checks can influence later ones.

A gate's checks are the complete and exclusive set of evaluations it performs. A gate never evaluates a rule not in its check list.

---

# The Verdict Function

The `verdict_function` reduces the individual check results to a single verdict.

```text
[check results]  ──verdict_function──►  PASS | FAIL
```

The default and most common verdict function is `all_mandatory_pass`: the gate passes if and only if every mandatory check passes. Other registered functions (defined in 7.1.5) support threshold-scored and weighted gates, but all share one property:

> **Every verdict function is fail-closed and reduces to exactly PASS or FAIL.**

A verdict function never emits a third value, never emits a score as its verdict, and never passes when a mandatory check is unevaluated. The function is a pure reduction over check results; it reads nothing else.

---

# The Report Shape

The `report_shape` names the contract for the report the gate emits.

Every gate emits a report conforming to a registered shape (defined in 7.1.8). The `standard_gate_report_v2` shape is the platform default: it records the gate identity, the artifact identity, the verdict, every check result, the failing checks, their owners, and the blocking flag.

The report shape is part of the gate definition so that consumers of a gate's report know its structure in advance. A gate never emits an ad-hoc report.

---

# The Configuration Reference

The `configuration_ref` binds the gate to its immutable thresholds.

A gate reads thresholds — a `runway_ratio` cap, a minimum score, a tolerance — from configuration, never from hard-coded literals in the check logic. The reference resolves to a versioned, immutable configuration object (defined in 7.1.11) that is fixed for the build.

Separating configuration from definition lets the same gate definition run under different profiles (development, preview, production) by resolving a different configuration, without changing the gate's identity-bearing structure.

---

# Gate vs Check vs Verdict

The three core concepts are distinct and never conflated.

| Concept | Is                                        | Owns                          | Emits            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------- | ----------------------------- | ---------------- |
| Gate    | An aggregation of checks at a boundary    | Identity, verdict function    | A verdict + report |
| Check   | A single owned deterministic evaluation   | One rule                      | A check result   |
| Verdict | The reduced outcome of a gate             | Nothing                       | (is the outcome) |

A gate has many checks. A check yields one result. A verdict is the reduction of all a gate's check results into one of {PASS, FAIL}.

---

# Structural Validity of a Gate

A gate definition is itself validated before use.

A well-formed gate satisfies:

* a unique `(gate_id, gate_version)`;
* a bound, valid `stage`;
* a non-empty `checks` array in which every entry names a registered check and a valid owner;
* a registered `verdict_function`;
* a registered `report_shape`;
* a resolvable `configuration_ref`.

A gate that fails structural validation is never run. The platform refuses to evaluate an artifact against a malformed gate, because an unvalidated gate cannot make a trustworthy verdict.

---

# Gate Composition Is Additive

A gate is assembled by declaring checks, never by procedural branching.

```text
Gate definition
   │  declare check A (owner, class)
   │  declare check B (owner, class)
   │  declare check C (owner, class)
   ▼
verdict_function reduces {A, B, C} → verdict
```

Adding a rule to a gate means adding a check to the list, not adding a branch to code. Removing a rule means removing a check, and both actions produce a new `gate_version`. The gate's behavior is always the transparent sum of its declared checks.

---

# The One Evaluation Engine

Because every gate shares this anatomy, one engine evaluates them all.

```text
Artifact + Gate Definition + Configuration
        │
        ▼
Evaluation Engine
   │  for each check: evaluate (deterministic)
   │  apply verdict_function (fail-closed)
   │  build report (report_shape)
   ▼
Verdict + Report
```

The engine is generic. It knows how to evaluate any check, apply any registered verdict function, and emit any registered report shape. It contains no gate-specific logic; all gate-specific behavior lives in the declaration.

This is the architectural payoff of a shared anatomy: the platform maintains one gate engine, not one per stage.

---

# Public Interfaces

The Gate Model exposes the following contracts.

```python
GateDefinition

GateIdentity

CheckReference

VerdictFunction

GateValidator

GateEvaluationEngine
```

`GateDefinition` is the serialized gate schema.

`GateIdentity` constructs and verifies `(gate_id, gate_version)` identities.

`CheckReference` is an entry in the check list binding a check to its owner and class.

`VerdictFunction` is the registered reduction from check results to a verdict.

`GateValidator` enforces structural validity of a gate definition.

`GateEvaluationEngine` executes any well-formed gate definition against an artifact.

Each interface is independently testable.

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant GM-701

Every gate is composed of exactly five parts: identity, checks, verdict function, report shape, and configuration reference.

---

## Invariant GM-702

A gate is declarative data executed by a single generic engine, not bespoke code.

---

## Invariant GM-703

Every gate has a unique `(gate_id, gate_version)`; a version is never edited in place.

---

## Invariant GM-704

A gate's `checks` array is non-empty; an empty gate is malformed, not a gate that always passes.

---

## Invariant GM-705

Every check entry names a registered check, its owning section, and its class.

---

## Invariant GM-706

The verdict function is a pure, fail-closed reduction over check results to exactly {PASS, FAIL}.

---

## Invariant GM-707

Check order affects reporting only; the verdict is independent of evaluation order.

---

## Invariant GM-708

A gate reads thresholds from a resolvable, versioned configuration reference, never from hard-coded literals.

---

## Invariant GM-709

A gate definition that fails structural validation is never executed.

---

## Invariant GM-710

Adding or removing a rule changes a gate only by changing its declared checks and producing a new gate version.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                                 |
| ------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-721 | A gate is composed of identity, checks, verdict function, report shape, and configuration reference. |
| ADR-722 | Gates are declarative data executed by one generic evaluation engine.                     |
| ADR-723 | Gate identity is the versioned pair `(gate_id, gate_version)`, never edited in place.      |
| ADR-724 | A gate's check list is non-empty and is its complete, exclusive set of evaluations.        |
| ADR-725 | Every check entry binds a check to an owning section and a class.                          |
| ADR-726 | The verdict function is a pure, fail-closed reduction to {PASS, FAIL}.                     |
| ADR-727 | Verdicts are independent of check evaluation order.                                        |
| ADR-728 | Gate thresholds are read from versioned configuration, not hard-coded.                     |
| ADR-729 | Structurally invalid gate definitions are never executed.                                  |
| ADR-730 | Gate behavior changes only by changing declared checks and producing a new gate version.   |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.3** is complete when:

* The five-part anatomy of a gate is defined and made structurally checkable.
* The canonical gate schema is specified with every field, type, and constraint.
* Gate identity follows the versioned `(gate_id, gate_version)` convention.
* The roles of the check list, verdict function, report shape, and configuration reference are defined.
* Gate, check, and verdict are distinguished and never conflated.
* Structural validity of a gate definition is defined and enforced before execution.
* The single generic evaluation engine is established as the payoff of shared anatomy.
* Invariants GM-701 through GM-710 and ADR-721 through ADR-730 are established.
* Every specific gate in Part 7.2 can be expressed as an instance of this model.

---

# Part 7.1.4 — Check Model & Check Contracts

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Check** — the atomic unit of quality evaluation — and the **contracts** every check obeys.

Section 7.1.3 established that a gate is an aggregation of checks. This section defines what a single check is: its identity, its owner, its inputs, its evaluation, and its result.

A check is the smallest thing a gate can evaluate. It answers exactly one question about an artifact, deterministically, and returns exactly one result. Everything a gate concludes is built from the results of its checks.

If a check is ambiguous, the gate that contains it is ambiguous. This section defines the check precisely enough that its result can be trusted and reproduced.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A check evaluates one rule, owns nothing, and decides deterministically. It reports a fact about an artifact; it never repairs the artifact and never invents the rule it checks.**

Three commitments follow.

A check is **singular**. It evaluates exactly one rule. A check that evaluates two rules is two checks. Singularity is what makes a failing check point to a single, correctable defect.

A check is **owned elsewhere**. The rule a check enforces is defined by an upstream section. The check is a reference to that rule plus a deterministic evaluation of it; it holds no rule of its own.

A check is **pure**. Given the same artifact and the same configuration, a check returns the same result. It reads its inputs, computes a result, and returns; it writes nothing and remembers nothing.

---

# The Anatomy of a Check

Every check is composed of six parts.

```text
Check
  ├── check_id     (unique identity)
  ├── owner        (the section that owns the rule)
  ├── class        (mandatory | advisory)
  ├── inputs       (what the check reads)
  ├── evaluation   (the deterministic predicate)
  └── result       (PASS | FAIL | NOT_APPLICABLE + evidence)
```

* **check_id** — the unique name of the check.
* **owner** — the section defining the rule the check enforces.
* **class** — whether the check is mandatory or advisory.
* **inputs** — the artifact fields and configuration values the check reads.
* **evaluation** — the deterministic predicate applied to the inputs.
* **result** — the outcome, with evidence.

A check missing any part is malformed.

---

# The Check Schema

Every check result is represented by the following canonical schema.

```json
{
  "check_id": "single_camera_move",
  "owner": "4.1.4",
  "class": "mandatory",
  "result": "FAIL",
  "evidence": {
    "expected": "camera_movements <= 1",
    "observed": "camera_movements = 3"
  },
  "message": "Shot declares three camera movements; at most one permitted."
}
```

The result schema records what was checked, who owns it, whether it is mandatory, the outcome, the evidence for the outcome, and a human-readable message.

The `evidence` object is what makes a result auditable: it records the `expected` condition and the `observed` value, so a reviewer can confirm the verdict without re-running the check.

---

# Check Result Values

A check result is drawn from a closed set of exactly three values.

```yaml
PASS

FAIL

NOT_APPLICABLE
```

* **PASS** — the rule is satisfied by the artifact.
* **FAIL** — the rule is violated by the artifact.
* **NOT_APPLICABLE** — the rule does not apply to this artifact.

No other value is valid. In particular there is no `UNKNOWN`, no `WARNING`, and no `PARTIAL`. A check that cannot determine PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE returns FAIL, because the platform is fail-closed and an undeterminable rule is treated as violated.

---

# NOT_APPLICABLE Is Not a Pass

`NOT_APPLICABLE` is a distinct outcome from `PASS`, and the distinction is load-bearing.

A `title_card` shot has no character performance, so an `emotion_defined` check on it is `NOT_APPLICABLE`, not `PASS`. The rule did not apply; it was not satisfied.

The verdict function (7.1.5) treats `NOT_APPLICABLE` according to the gate's declaration — typically excluding it from the mandatory set for that artifact — but it never silently converts `NOT_APPLICABLE` into `PASS`. A check that reports `NOT_APPLICABLE` must justify inapplicability in its evidence, so that a reviewer can confirm the rule genuinely did not apply rather than being skipped.

---

# Mandatory vs Advisory Checks

Every check carries a `class`.

## mandatory

A mandatory check must pass (or be `NOT_APPLICABLE`) for the gate to pass.

A single mandatory `FAIL` fails the gate. Mandatory checks are the enforcement backbone of a gate.

---

## advisory

An advisory check is evaluated and reported but does not, by itself, fail the gate.

Advisory checks surface quality signals — a metric trending toward a limit, a soft stylistic concern — that inform reviewers without blocking the build. An advisory `FAIL` appears in the report and may contribute to a quality score (7.3), but it does not flip the gate verdict.

> **Advisory does not mean ignored. It means recorded but non-blocking.**

The class of a check is fixed in the gate definition. A mandatory check is never quietly demoted to advisory to rescue a build; demotion requires a new gate version.

---

# Check Ownership

Every check names the section that owns its rule.

```text
Check single_camera_move
        │
        ▼
owner = 4.1.4 (Camera Language & Constraints)
```

Ownership is mandatory and traceable. When a check fails, the gate report routes the failure to the owning section, so the artifact is returned to the authority that defines the violated rule.

A check with no owner is malformed. A gate never enforces a rule that no section claims, because such a rule cannot be corrected against an authoritative definition.

The owner is the source of truth; the check is the enforcement. This is the check-level expression of Principle 3 (Enforce, Do Not Author).

---

# Check Inputs

A check declares exactly what it reads.

```yaml
inputs:
  artifact_fields:
    - camera.movement
  configuration_values:
    - limits.camera_movements_max
  upstream_verdicts: []
```

A check reads three kinds of input:

* **artifact_fields** — fields of the artifact under evaluation;
* **configuration_values** — thresholds from the immutable configuration;
* **upstream_verdicts** — recorded verdicts of prior gates it depends on.

A check reads nothing outside its declared inputs. It does not consult global state, the network, or the clock. Declared inputs are what make a check reproducible: the same inputs always produce the same result.

---

# Check Evaluation Is a Pure Predicate

A check's evaluation is a pure function.

```text
evaluation(inputs) → { PASS | FAIL | NOT_APPLICABLE, evidence }
```

The predicate reads the declared inputs, computes a result, and attaches evidence. It has no side effects. It does not write to the artifact, does not enqueue work, and does not emit events.

Purity is the check-level expression of Principle 4 (Determinism Over Judgment). A check that consulted anything beyond its declared inputs could disagree with itself, and a check that disagrees with itself cannot support a trustworthy verdict.

---

# Evidence Is Mandatory

Every check result carries evidence.

```json
"evidence": {
  "expected": "runway_ratio <= 0.50",
  "observed": "runway_ratio = 0.72"
}
```

Evidence records the `expected` condition and the `observed` value. It is mandatory for every result, including `PASS`: a passing check records the condition it confirmed and the value it observed.

Evidence is what makes a verdict explainable (Principle 6, Traceability). A result with no evidence is an assertion, and the platform does not accept assertions. Evidence is the raw material a reviewer uses to confirm — or dispute — a verdict without re-running the gate.

---

# Check Determinism

A check is deterministic across evaluations.

Given identical declared inputs, a check returns an identical result and identical evidence. Two evaluations of `single_camera_move` on the same shot produce the same `FAIL` with the same `observed: camera_movements = 3`.

Determinism holds across machines, across runs, and across time. It is what allows a check result to be cached with its artifact identity (Part 6.2) and reproduced during audit (Part 7.4).

---

# Check Independence

Checks within a gate are independent.

The result of one check never depends on the result of another. `camera_defined` does not consult the result of `purpose_exists`. Each check reads its own declared inputs and computes its own result.

Independence is why the verdict does not depend on check order (Invariant GM-707). It also means checks may be evaluated in parallel by the engine without changing any result — a property the platform relies on for gate performance.

---

# The Check Result Model

The complete result a check returns.

```json
{
  "check_id": "continuity_valid",
  "owner": "4.1.7",
  "class": "mandatory",
  "result": "PASS",
  "evidence": {
    "expected": "all references resolve",
    "observed": "maya_v1, executive_dark_v1, operations_center_night resolved"
  },
  "message": "All continuity references resolved.",
  "evaluated": true
}
```

The `evaluated` flag is significant: a check that was not evaluated has `evaluated: false`, and the fail-closed verdict function treats an unevaluated mandatory check as FAIL. A check never silently disappears from a report; if it did not run, that fact is recorded.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-711 — The Multi-Rule Check

Wrong:

```text
one check verifies purpose AND camera AND continuity
        │
        ▼
FAIL points to three possible defects
```

Correct:

```text
three checks: purpose_exists, camera_defined, continuity_valid
        │
        ▼
FAIL points to exactly one defect
```

---

## AP-712 — NOT_APPLICABLE as a Free Pass

Wrong:

```text
Check cannot determine result
        │
        ▼
returns NOT_APPLICABLE to avoid failing
```

Correct:

```text
Check cannot determine result
        │
        ▼
returns FAIL (fail-closed); NOT_APPLICABLE only when the rule truly does not apply
```

---

## AP-713 — The Evidence-Free Result

Wrong:

```text
Check returns FAIL with no expected/observed
```

Correct:

```text
Check returns FAIL with expected and observed recorded
```

---

## AP-714 — The Ownerless Rule

Wrong:

```text
Gate adds a check with no owning section
```

Correct:

```text
Every check names the section that owns its rule
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant CK-701

A check evaluates exactly one rule owned by exactly one upstream section.

---

## Invariant CK-702

A check result is drawn from the closed set {PASS, FAIL, NOT_APPLICABLE}.

---

## Invariant CK-703

`NOT_APPLICABLE` is distinct from `PASS` and is never silently converted to it.

---

## Invariant CK-704

A check that cannot determine PASS or genuine NOT_APPLICABLE returns FAIL.

---

## Invariant CK-705

Every check carries a class of `mandatory` or `advisory`, fixed in the gate definition.

---

## Invariant CK-706

An advisory check is recorded but never, by itself, fails a gate.

---

## Invariant CK-707

A check reads only its declared artifact fields, configuration values, and upstream verdicts.

---

## Invariant CK-708

A check evaluation is a pure predicate with no side effects.

---

## Invariant CK-709

Every check result carries evidence recording the expected condition and the observed value.

---

## Invariant CK-710

An unevaluated mandatory check is recorded as such and treated as FAIL by the verdict function.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                                |
| ------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-731 | A check is the atomic unit of evaluation and enforces exactly one owned rule.            |
| ADR-732 | Check results are drawn from the closed set {PASS, FAIL, NOT_APPLICABLE}.                |
| ADR-733 | NOT_APPLICABLE is distinct from PASS and requires justification.                         |
| ADR-734 | A check that cannot determine a result returns FAIL, honoring fail-closed.               |
| ADR-735 | Checks are classed mandatory or advisory; advisory checks record but do not block.       |
| ADR-736 | Every check names the upstream section that owns its rule.                               |
| ADR-737 | A check reads only its declared inputs and is a pure predicate.                          |
| ADR-738 | Every check result carries expected/observed evidence.                                   |
| ADR-739 | Checks are independent; the verdict is order-independent.                                |
| ADR-740 | An unevaluated mandatory check is treated as FAIL.                                        |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.4** is complete when:

* The six-part anatomy of a check is defined.
* The canonical check-result schema is specified with evidence and message.
* The closed result set {PASS, FAIL, NOT_APPLICABLE} is defined, and NOT_APPLICABLE is distinguished from PASS.
* The mandatory/advisory class distinction is defined, with advisory checks recorded but non-blocking.
* Check ownership, declared inputs, purity, and mandatory evidence are established.
* Check determinism and independence are defined and tied to caching and order-independence.
* The unevaluated-check case is defined and resolved fail-closed.
* Anti-patterns for multi-rule checks, NOT_APPLICABLE misuse, evidence-free results, and ownerless rules are documented.
* Invariants CK-701 through CK-710 and ADR-731 through ADR-740 are established.

---

# Part 7.1.5 — Pass/Fail Semantics & the Fail-Closed Model

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **verdict semantics** of a Quality Gate: how individual check results reduce to a single verdict, what that verdict means, and how the **fail-closed model** governs every ambiguous case.

Section 7.1.4 defined the check and its result. This section defines the reduction from many check results to one verdict, and the rules that make that reduction safe.

A verdict is the whole purpose of a gate. Everything upstream — the anatomy, the checks, the evidence — exists to produce one trustworthy PASS or FAIL. This section defines exactly how that verdict is computed, so that "PASS" carries the same guarantee at every gate in the platform.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A verdict is a fail-closed reduction. PASS is earned by affirmative evidence on every mandatory check; FAIL is the default that absence, ambiguity, and error all resolve to.**

The philosophy is asymmetric by design.

PASS is expensive: it requires that every mandatory check was evaluated and returned PASS or genuine NOT_APPLICABLE.

FAIL is cheap: it is the resting state, reached by any mandatory FAIL, any unevaluated mandatory check, any missing input, or any internal error.

The asymmetry encodes the platform's risk preference: a false FAIL costs a re-run, a false PASS costs a defect in production. The gate is built to prefer the cheaper mistake.

---

# The Closed Verdict Set

A gate verdict is drawn from a closed set of exactly two values.

```yaml
PASS

FAIL
```

There is no third verdict.

There is no `PASS_WITH_WARNINGS`, no `CONDITIONAL_PASS`, and no `PENDING`. A gate either admits the artifact or it does not. Advisory concerns are recorded in the report (7.1.8) and may lower a quality score (7.3), but they never create a third verdict.

The two-value verdict is what makes the Orchestrator's response unambiguous: PASS advances, FAIL blocks. A third value would require the Orchestrator to interpret quality, which it must never do.

---

# The Governing Rule

The verdict is governed by a single rule.

> **A gate returns PASS if and only if every mandatory check was evaluated and returned PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE. Otherwise it returns FAIL.**

Expressed formally:

```text
PASS  ⟺  ∀ c ∈ mandatory_checks :
            c.evaluated = true  ∧  c.result ∈ {PASS, NOT_APPLICABLE}

FAIL  ⟺  ¬PASS
```

Every path that is not an affirmative PASS is a FAIL. This is the fail-closed model stated as a biconditional.

---

# Verdict Functions

The reduction from check results to a verdict is performed by a registered **verdict function**, named in the gate definition (7.1.3).

The platform defines three verdict functions. All three are fail-closed.

---

## all_mandatory_pass

The default verdict function.

```text
PASS ⟺ every mandatory check is PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE
```

This is a pure logical AND across the mandatory checks. It is the function used by the Shot Quality Gate (Part 4.1.12) and by most pipeline gates. Advisory checks are recorded but do not participate in the verdict.

---

## threshold_score

Used where quality is measured continuously (7.3).

```text
PASS ⟺ every mandatory check passes
       AND quality_score >= configured_threshold
```

The mandatory checks are still a hard AND; the score is an *additional* gate, never a substitute for the mandatory checks. A high score never rescues a failed mandatory check. This function is fail-closed twice: once on the mandatory checks, once on the threshold.

---

## weighted_mandatory

Used where mandatory checks carry different blocking severities but all remain blocking.

```text
PASS ⟺ every mandatory check is PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE
```

Weights inform the *reporting* and *scoring* of a failure's severity; they never allow a mandatory FAIL to be outweighed into a PASS. Every mandatory check remains individually blocking. Weighting orders the failures for reviewers; it does not soften the verdict.

---

# All Verdict Functions Are Fail-Closed

The three functions differ in what they additionally require, never in their floor.

| Function            | Mandatory checks | Additional condition        | Can a mandatory FAIL pass? |
| ------------------- | ---------------- | --------------------------- | -------------------------- |
| `all_mandatory_pass`| hard AND         | none                        | No                         |
| `threshold_score`   | hard AND         | score ≥ threshold           | No                         |
| `weighted_mandatory`| hard AND         | none (weights inform report)| No                         |

No registered verdict function permits a mandatory FAIL to yield PASS. A verdict function that did would violate the fail-closed model and is not a valid function.

---

# The Fail-Closed Resolution Table

Every ambiguous condition resolves to FAIL. The resolution is exhaustive and mandatory.

| Condition                                      | Verdict |
| ---------------------------------------------- | ------- |
| Every mandatory check PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE   | PASS    |
| Any mandatory check FAIL                       | FAIL    |
| Any mandatory check unevaluated                | FAIL    |
| Missing mandatory input to the gate            | FAIL    |
| Artifact identity mismatch                     | FAIL    |
| Configuration unresolvable                     | FAIL    |
| Internal error during evaluation              | FAIL    |
| Verdict function unregistered or malformed     | FAIL    |

There is no row whose verdict is PASS other than the first. The table is the complete definition of when a gate passes.

---

# Absence Is Failure

A missing value is never a default.

If a mandatory check's input is absent, the check does not assume a neutral value and pass. It fails. This is the direct application of the Shot Gate discipline from Part 4.1.12 — *a missing value is a failure, not a default* — generalized to every gate.

```text
Wrong:  input absent → assume default → PASS
Correct: input absent → check FAIL → gate FAIL
```

The platform never manufactures evidence it does not have.

---

# Error Is Failure

An internal error in a gate is a FAIL, not an exception that skips the gate.

If a check throws, if the configuration cannot be read, if the evaluation engine encounters an unexpected state — the gate returns FAIL and records the error as the cause. It never returns PASS, and it never returns "no verdict."

```text
Wrong:  check errors → gate skipped → build proceeds
Correct: check errors → gate FAIL → build blocked
```

A gate that could be bypassed by inducing an error would be no gate at all. Errors close the gate; they do not open it.

---

# No Partial Credit

A gate never renders or admits the passing portion of a failing artifact.

If nine of ten mandatory checks pass and one fails, the gate fails. The nine passing checks do not earn partial admission. This mirrors Part 4.1.12: *failure blocks rendering for the build, not merely for the failing shot.*

```text
9 of 10 mandatory checks pass
        │
        ▼
one FAIL → gate FAIL → nothing advances
```

Partial credit would let defects accumulate across stages, each stage admitting "most" of a flawed artifact until the composite is wholly wrong.

---

# No Override Path

There is no flag that converts a FAIL into a PASS.

A gate exposes no "force pass," no "render anyway," and no "ignore failures" parameter. The verdict is a function of the evidence, and the only way to change the verdict is to change the artifact so the evidence changes.

The single, narrow exception is a **waiver**, which does not change the verdict. A waiver is a governance action (7.1.10) that *records an accepted exception* against a recorded FAIL; the gate still returns FAIL, and the waiver is an auditable decision by a distinct authority to proceed despite it. The gate never converts its own FAIL to PASS.

---

# The Verdict Is Bound to the Artifact Identity

A verdict is valid only for the exact artifact identity it evaluated.

```text
verdict PASS  @  artifact_identity = sha256(...)
```

If the artifact changes by a single byte, its identity changes, and the prior verdict is void. A gate never honors a PASS recorded against a different identity. This is what keeps cached verdicts (Part 6.2) safe: reuse is permitted only when the identity matches exactly.

---

# Verdict Determinism

The verdict is deterministic.

Given identical check results — which are themselves deterministic (7.1.4) — the verdict function produces an identical verdict. Because the function is a pure reduction and the checks are order-independent, the verdict is byte-stable across runs, machines, and time.

Determinism at the verdict level is what makes a PASS auditable months later: re-running the gate on the archived artifact yields the same verdict and the same failing set.

---

# Worked Example — A Fail-Closed Reduction

Consider a gate with four mandatory checks and one advisory check.

```json
{
  "checks": [
    { "check_id": "a", "class": "mandatory", "result": "PASS",           "evaluated": true },
    { "check_id": "b", "class": "mandatory", "result": "NOT_APPLICABLE", "evaluated": true },
    { "check_id": "c", "class": "mandatory", "result": "PASS",           "evaluated": true },
    { "check_id": "d", "class": "mandatory", "result": "FAIL",           "evaluated": true },
    { "check_id": "e", "class": "advisory",  "result": "FAIL",           "evaluated": true }
  ],
  "verdict_function": "all_mandatory_pass"
}
```

Reduction under `all_mandatory_pass`:

* mandatory `a` = PASS — acceptable;
* mandatory `b` = NOT_APPLICABLE — acceptable;
* mandatory `c` = PASS — acceptable;
* mandatory `d` = FAIL — **fails the gate**;
* advisory `e` = FAIL — recorded, does not affect verdict.

Verdict: **FAIL**, caused by mandatory check `d`. The advisory `e` appears in the report but is not the cause.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-721 — The Third Verdict

Wrong:

```text
Gate returns PASS_WITH_WARNINGS
```

Correct:

```text
Gate returns PASS or FAIL; warnings live in the report
```

---

## AP-722 — Score Rescuing a Mandatory FAIL

Wrong:

```text
mandatory check FAILs
        │
        ▼
overall score is high → gate PASSes
```

Correct:

```text
mandatory check FAILs
        │
        ▼
gate FAILs regardless of score
```

---

## AP-723 — Error as Bypass

Wrong:

```text
check throws → gate skipped → build proceeds
```

Correct:

```text
check throws → gate FAIL → build blocked
```

---

## AP-724 — The Force-Pass Flag

Wrong:

```text
Operator sets force_pass = true → FAIL becomes PASS
```

Correct:

```text
No force-pass exists; a waiver records an exception without changing the verdict
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant FC-701

A gate verdict is drawn from the closed set {PASS, FAIL}; no third verdict exists.

---

## Invariant FC-702

PASS is returned if and only if every mandatory check was evaluated and returned PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE.

---

## Invariant FC-703

Every registered verdict function applies a hard AND over mandatory checks and can never pass a mandatory FAIL.

---

## Invariant FC-704

A missing mandatory input resolves to FAIL.

---

## Invariant FC-705
