An unevaluated mandatory check resolves to FAIL.

---

## Invariant FC-706

An internal gate error resolves to FAIL and never bypasses the gate.

---

## Invariant FC-707

No partial credit: a gate admits nothing of a failing artifact.

---

## Invariant FC-708

No override path converts a FAIL to a PASS; a waiver records an exception without altering the verdict.

---

## Invariant FC-709

A verdict is valid only for the exact artifact identity evaluated and is void for any other.

---

## Invariant FC-710

The verdict is deterministic given deterministic, order-independent check results.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-741 | The verdict set is closed at {PASS, FAIL}; no third verdict exists.                  |
| ADR-742 | PASS requires affirmative evaluation of every mandatory check.                       |
| ADR-743 | All verdict functions apply a hard AND over mandatory checks.                        |
| ADR-744 | A score or weight may add a condition but never rescue a mandatory FAIL.             |
| ADR-745 | Missing input, unevaluated check, and internal error all resolve to FAIL.            |
| ADR-746 | No partial credit and no override path exist.                                        |
| ADR-747 | A waiver records an exception without converting the verdict from FAIL to PASS.       |
| ADR-748 | A verdict is bound to the exact artifact identity evaluated.                         |
| ADR-749 | The verdict is deterministic and reproducible.                                       |
| ADR-750 | The fail-closed resolution table is the complete definition of when a gate passes.   |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.5** is complete when:

* The closed verdict set {PASS, FAIL} is defined and the absence of a third verdict is enforced.
* The governing biconditional for PASS is stated formally.
* The three registered verdict functions are defined and shown to be uniformly fail-closed.
* The exhaustive fail-closed resolution table is provided.
* Absence, error, partial credit, and override are each defined and resolved to FAIL or prohibited.
* The waiver is distinguished from an override: it records an exception without changing the verdict.
* Verdict binding to artifact identity and verdict determinism are established.
* A worked reduction example is provided.
* Invariants FC-701 through FC-710 and ADR-741 through ADR-750 are established.

---

# Part 7.1.6 — Gate Types & Classification

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **classification of Quality Gates** — the closed taxonomy of gate types the platform recognizes, and the properties that distinguish them.

Sections 7.1.3 through 7.1.5 defined the shared anatomy and semantics every gate obeys. This section defines how gates differ: by scale, by trigger, by blocking authority, and by the kind of judgment they encode.

A classification matters because it tells the Orchestrator (Part 6.3) how to schedule a gate, tells reviewers how to interpret a verdict, and tells the configuration layer (7.1.11) which knobs a gate exposes. Two gates with identical anatomy may still be scheduled and interpreted differently because they are different types.

The taxonomy is closed. Every gate in Part 7.2 is exactly one type along each classification axis.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **Every gate shares one anatomy but occupies a defined position in a small, closed taxonomy. Classification is descriptive of scale and trigger; it never weakens the fail-closed guarantee.**

Classification is orthogonal to enforcement. A gate's type describes *what it spans* and *when it runs*, not *how strictly it judges*. An advisory-influence gate is still fail-closed on its mandatory checks; a sequence-level gate still returns exactly {PASS, FAIL}.

The taxonomy exists to organize gates, not to create tiers of leniency.

---

# The Four Classification Axes

Every gate is classified along four independent axes.

```text
Gate
  ├── Scope Axis     → element | sequence | cross-stage
  ├── Trigger Axis   → stage-exit | on-demand | continuous
  ├── Blocking Axis  → blocking | advisory-influence
  └── Judgment Axis  → structural | semantic | human-approval
```

A gate's full type is the tuple of its position on all four axes. The axes are independent: a gate may be, for example, sequence-scope, stage-exit-trigger, blocking, and semantic-judgment.

---

# Scope Axis

The scope axis classifies what an artifact set a gate spans.

## element

An **element gate** validates a single artifact unit in isolation.

The Shot Quality Gate (Part 4.1.12) validating one shot is an element gate. It reads one shot and returns one verdict for that shot.

---

## sequence

A **sequence gate** validates a collection of elements as a whole.

The Storyboard Quality Gate validating an ordered sequence of shots is a sequence gate. A sequence gate can fail a set of individually valid elements because the *composition* is invalid — a property no element gate can see.

---

## cross-stage

A **cross-stage gate** validates coherence across the outputs of more than one stage.

A gate confirming that the rendered assets match the approved storyboard spans two stages. Cross-stage gates enforce that transformations preserved meaning; they are defined in Part 7.2.11.

---

# Scope Axis Summary

| Scope       | Spans                        | Can detect                                   | Example              |
| ----------- | ---------------------------- | -------------------------------------------- | -------------------- |
| element     | one artifact unit            | defects internal to a unit                   | Shot Quality Gate    |
| sequence    | a collection of units        | composition, ordering, aggregate defects     | Storyboard Gate      |
| cross-stage | outputs of multiple stages   | drift between what was planned and produced  | Render↔Storyboard    |

The narrow gate runs before the wide gate: element gates precede sequence gates precede cross-stage gates, as established in 7.1.7.

---

# Trigger Axis

The trigger axis classifies when a gate runs.

## stage-exit

A **stage-exit gate** runs automatically when a stage completes, before the artifact may advance.

Stage-exit gates are the default. Every pipeline stage boundary has a stage-exit gate. The Orchestrator invokes it as part of the `VALIDATING` transition (Part 6.3.4).

---

## on-demand

An **on-demand gate** runs when explicitly invoked, outside the automatic stage flow.

On-demand gates support re-validation after a correction, audit re-runs (Part 7.4), and benchmark builds (Part 6.1.7). An on-demand run is identical in semantics to a stage-exit run; only its trigger differs.

---

## continuous

A **continuous gate** runs repeatedly during a long-running stage, not only at its exit.

A continuous gate monitors an in-progress render or composition and can block early when a defect is certain, rather than waiting for stage completion. Continuous gates are advisory-influence by default (below) unless declared blocking.

---

# Blocking Axis

The blocking axis classifies a gate's authority over the build.

## blocking

A **blocking gate** fails the build on a FAIL verdict.

Blocking gates are the enforcement backbone. A FAIL halts advancement; the artifact must be corrected and re-gated. Every stage-exit gate is blocking.

---

## advisory-influence

An **advisory-influence gate** records a verdict and contributes to quality scoring, but a FAIL does not, by itself, halt the build.

An advisory-influence gate is composed predominantly of advisory checks (7.1.4). Its verdict informs reviewers and the quality score (7.3); it does not block. An advisory-influence gate is still fail-closed and still deterministic; it simply lacks blocking authority.

> **Advisory-influence is a property of the gate's authority, not a relaxation of its rigor.**

The distinction between a blocking gate and an advisory-influence gate is fixed in the gate definition and versioned. A blocking gate is never quietly demoted.

---

# Judgment Axis

The judgment axis classifies the kind of rule a gate predominantly enforces.

## structural

A **structural gate** enforces well-formedness: schema conformance, required fields, enumerations, cardinality limits, reference resolution.

Structural checks are fully mechanical. `single_camera_move` and `render_strategy_defined` are structural. Structural judgment is the most objective and the cheapest to evaluate.

---

## semantic

A **semantic gate** enforces meaning-level coherence: continuity across a sequence, emotional arc, narrative consistency, temporal monotonicity.

Semantic checks are still deterministic — they reduce meaning to explicit, checkable predicates — but they evaluate relationships rather than isolated fields. The Time Continuity check (Part 4.1.8) is semantic.

---

## human-approval

A **human-approval gate** enforces the presence of a recorded human decision.

A human-approval gate does not judge the artifact's content; it checks that a required editorial approval exists, is scoped correctly, and has not been revoked. Human-approval gates are defined in Part 7.4. The gate mechanizes the *presence* of approval; the human owns the *substance* of it.

---

# The Full Type of a Gate

A gate's type is the tuple across all four axes.

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    sequence
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: semantic
```

The example describes a gate like the Storyboard Quality Gate: it spans a sequence, runs at stage exit, blocks on failure, and enforces semantic coherence.

Every gate in Part 7.2 declares its full type. The type determines scheduling, interpretation, and configuration surface, but never the fail-closed floor.

---

# Classification Does Not Alter Semantics

No position on any axis changes the core guarantees.

| Guarantee                        | Holds for every type? |
| -------------------------------- | --------------------- |
| Verdict ∈ {PASS, FAIL}           | Yes                   |
| Fail-closed on mandatory checks  | Yes                   |
| Deterministic verdict            | Yes                   |
| Traceable report                 | Yes                   |
| Enforces owned rules only        | Yes                   |

An advisory-influence, continuous, structural, element gate obeys every guarantee that a blocking, stage-exit, semantic, cross-stage gate does. The taxonomy organizes gates; it never exempts one from the architecture.

---

# The Gate Registry

Gates are resolved by type and stage through the **Gate Registry**.

```text
(stage, build_profile)
        │
        ▼
Gate Registry
        │
        ▼
resolved gate definition(s) + type
```

The registry maps each stage and build profile to the gate definitions that apply, and records each gate's full type. The Orchestrator queries the registry to learn which gates to run and how to schedule them (a continuous gate is scheduled differently from a stage-exit gate).

The registry is the single source of truth for which gates exist and where they apply. A gate not in the registry is never run.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-731 — Type as an Excuse

Wrong:

```text
"It's only a structural gate, so a FAIL is a warning"
```

Correct:

```text
Judgment type does not change blocking authority; a blocking structural gate still blocks
```

---

## AP-732 — Sequence Logic in an Element Gate

Wrong:

```text
Element gate tries to validate ordering across shots
```

Correct:

```text
Ordering is validated by the sequence gate that spans the shots
```

---

## AP-733 — Silent Demotion to Advisory

Wrong:

```text
Blocking gate keeps failing → redefine it as advisory-influence to unblock
```

Correct:

```text
Blocking authority is versioned; demotion requires a new gate version and governance approval
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant GT-701

Every gate is classified along four independent axes: scope, trigger, blocking, and judgment.

---

## Invariant GT-702

The scope axis is closed at {element, sequence, cross-stage}.

---

## Invariant GT-703

The trigger axis is closed at {stage-exit, on-demand, continuous}.

---

## Invariant GT-704

The blocking axis is closed at {blocking, advisory-influence}.

---

## Invariant GT-705

The judgment axis is closed at {structural, semantic, human-approval}.

---

## Invariant GT-706

A gate declares its full type as the tuple across all four axes.

---

## Invariant GT-707

Classification never alters the fail-closed, deterministic, traceable guarantees.

---

## Invariant GT-708

Blocking authority is fixed in the gate definition and versioned; demotion requires a new gate version.

---

## Invariant GT-709

Element gates precede sequence gates precede cross-stage gates.

---

## Invariant GT-710

A gate not registered in the Gate Registry is never run.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-751 | Gates are classified along four independent, closed axes.                            |
| ADR-752 | The scope axis is {element, sequence, cross-stage}.                                  |
| ADR-753 | The trigger axis is {stage-exit, on-demand, continuous}.                             |
| ADR-754 | The blocking axis is {blocking, advisory-influence}.                                 |
| ADR-755 | The judgment axis is {structural, semantic, human-approval}.                         |
| ADR-756 | A gate's full type is the tuple across all four axes and is declared explicitly.     |
| ADR-757 | Classification is descriptive; it never weakens fail-closed guarantees.              |
| ADR-758 | Blocking authority is versioned; advisory demotion requires a new version and governance. |
| ADR-759 | Narrow-scope gates precede wide-scope gates.                                         |
| ADR-760 | The Gate Registry resolves gates by stage and profile; unregistered gates never run. |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.6** is complete when:

* The four classification axes — scope, trigger, blocking, judgment — are defined as independent and closed.
* Each axis's values are enumerated and defined with examples.
* The full type of a gate is defined as the tuple across all axes.
* It is established that classification never alters the core semantic guarantees.
* The advisory-influence type is defined as an authority property, not a relaxation of rigor.
* The Gate Registry is defined as the resolution point for gates by stage and profile.
* Anti-patterns for type-as-excuse, misplaced sequence logic, and silent demotion are documented.
* Invariants GT-701 through GT-710 and ADR-751 through ADR-760 are established.

---

# Part 7.1.7 — Gate Ordering, Composition & the Gate Chain

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines how Quality Gates **compose** across the pipeline: the order in which they run, how one gate's verdict feeds another, and the guarantees the resulting **gate chain** provides.

Sections 7.1.3 through 7.1.6 defined a gate in isolation. This section defines the relationships *between* gates — the chain that runs from the Story Gate to the Publication Gate — and the invariants that hold over the chain as a whole.

A single gate guarantees that one artifact is admissible. The gate chain guarantees that a published trailer passed every admissibility condition, in order, with no boundary skipped and no verdict fabricated.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **Gates compose as a monotone chain: each gate depends only on verdicts already earned upstream, no gate re-derives an upstream property, and a break anywhere halts everything downstream.**

Two properties define the chain.

The chain is **monotone**: an artifact only moves forward, from a narrower, earlier admissibility condition to a wider, later one. It never re-enters an earlier gate to have a property re-judged.

The chain is **non-bypassable**: reaching a downstream gate is proof that every upstream gate passed. There is no path to the Publication Gate that skips the Render Gate.

---

# The Canonical Gate Chain

The platform runs the following ordered chain of stage-exit gates.

```text
Story Quality Gate
        │  PASS
        ▼
Screenplay Quality Gate
        │  PASS
        ▼
Shot Quality Gate
        │  PASS
        ▼
Storyboard Quality Gate
        │  PASS
        ▼
Render Quality Gate
        │  PASS
        ▼
Composition Quality Gate
        │  PASS
        ▼
Narration & Audio Quality Gate
        │  PASS
        ▼
Metadata & Packaging Quality Gate
        │  PASS
        ▼
Publication Quality Gate
        │  PASS
        ▼
Published Trailer
```

Each gate runs only after the one before it has returned PASS. A FAIL at any gate halts the chain at that point.

The specific gates are defined in Part 7.2; this section defines the chain that connects them.

---

# Ordering Within a Stage

Within a single stage boundary, gates are ordered by scope.

```text
Element gates
        │  all PASS
        ▼
Sequence gates
        │  all PASS
        ▼
Cross-stage gates
```

The narrow gate precedes the wide gate. Every element must individually pass before the sequence they form is evaluated, and the sequence must pass before any cross-stage coherence is checked.

This is the generalization of the Part 4.1.12 rule: *the Storyboard Quality Gate runs only after every shot has individually passed the Shot Quality Gate.* A collection is judged as a whole only once its parts are each admissible.

---

# The Gate Dependency Graph

Gate ordering is expressed as an explicit dependency graph.

```text
StoryGate ──► ScreenplayGate ──► ShotGate ──► StoryboardGate ──► RenderGate
                                                                    │
                                                                    ▼
                                        PublicationGate ◄── PackagingGate ◄── CompositionGate
```

Each edge is a dependency: the target gate runs only after the source gate has returned PASS. The graph is a directed acyclic graph — a gate never depends, directly or transitively, on a gate downstream of it.

The dependency graph is declarative and registered alongside the gates (7.1.6). The Orchestrator reads it to determine gate order; it never infers order procedurally.

---

# Verdict Feed-Forward

A downstream gate may depend on an upstream verdict, and it consumes that verdict rather than re-deriving the property.

```text
StoryboardGate PASS
        │  recorded verdict
        ▼
RenderGate reads "storyboard approved & valid"
        │  as an upstream_verdict input
        ▼
RenderGate checks render fidelity, not storyboard validity
```

This is the chain-level expression of Principle 5 (One Auditable Point). The Render Gate does not re-check that the storyboard is structurally valid; that was settled at the Storyboard Gate, and the Render Gate references the recorded verdict. Each property is enforced once and referenced thereafter.

A check that reads an upstream verdict declares it in its `upstream_verdicts` inputs (7.1.4). If the referenced upstream verdict is absent or is not PASS, the dependent check fails closed.

---

# No Re-Derivation

A gate never re-computes a property another gate owns.

```text
Wrong:  RenderGate re-validates shot continuity from scratch
Correct: RenderGate trusts the ShotGate/StoryboardGate recorded verdict
```

Re-derivation is prohibited for two reasons. It duplicates enforcement, creating a second place a rule can drift. And it is wasteful, re-doing settled work. The chain relies on each gate trusting the recorded verdicts of the gates before it, exactly.

The trust is safe because verdicts are bound to artifact identity (7.1.5): a downstream gate trusts an upstream verdict only when the upstream artifact identity it was earned against is unchanged.

---

# Chain Halting

A FAIL halts the chain immediately.

```text
For each gate in chain order:
    verdict = evaluate(gate, artifact)
    if verdict == FAIL:
        halt chain
        block build
        return report
Advance only when the current gate PASSes
```

When a gate fails, no downstream gate runs. The build stops at the failing gate, the artifact is returned to the owning stage for correction, and the chain resumes from the corrected gate — not from the beginning — once the correction is re-gated.

Halting on first FAIL is deliberate: running downstream gates against an artifact that already failed upstream would waste work and produce misleading downstream verdicts.

---

# Chain Resumption After Correction

When a failed artifact is corrected, the chain resumes at the gate that failed.

```text
ShotGate FAIL
        │
        ▼
Shot corrected (artifact identity changes)
        │
        ▼
ShotGate re-run on new identity
        │  PASS
        ▼
Chain resumes: StoryboardGate, RenderGate, ...
```

Gates upstream of the failure are not re-run *unless* the correction changed an artifact they had validated. Because verdicts are bound to artifact identity, the platform re-runs exactly the gates whose upstream artifact identity changed, and no more. This is the gate-chain application of the incremental principle from Part 6.2.

---

# The Chain Is Non-Bypassable

Reaching a gate is proof that every upstream gate passed.

```text
Artifact at RenderGate
        │
        ▼
implies StoryGate, ScreenplayGate, ShotGate, StoryboardGate all PASSed
```

There is no entry point into the middle of the chain that skips earlier gates. An artifact cannot be injected at the Render stage without having passed the Storyboard Gate, because the Orchestrator advances an artifact to a stage only after the prior stage's gate returned PASS.

Non-bypassability is what lets the Publication Gate assume, without re-checking, that the entire upstream chain succeeded.

---

# Chain Invariants Hold Globally

Certain guarantees hold over the chain as a whole, not merely per gate.

* **Completeness** — every stage boundary in the pipeline has a gate in the chain.
* **Ordering** — gates run in dependency-graph order, narrow scope before wide.
* **Monotonicity** — an artifact advances forward only; it never re-enters an earlier gate to have a settled property re-judged.
* **Attribution** — a chain halt is always attributed to a single failing gate and its owning section.

These are properties of the chain, verified over the dependency graph, not of any individual gate.

---

# Composition Report

The chain emits a composition report summarizing the whole traversal.

```yaml
chain_report:
  build_id:
  chain_version:
  gates:
    - gate: story_quality_gate,      verdict: PASS
    - gate: screenplay_quality_gate, verdict: PASS
    - gate: shot_quality_gate,       verdict: PASS
    - gate: storyboard_quality_gate, verdict: FAIL
  halted_at: storyboard_quality_gate
  halted_reason: "render balance exceeded hybrid cap"
  owning_section: "4.1.10"
  gates_not_run:
    - render_quality_gate
    - composition_quality_gate
    - narration_quality_gate
    - packaging_quality_gate
    - publication_quality_gate
```

The chain report records the verdict of every gate that ran, the gate where the chain halted, the reason, the owning section, and every gate that did not run because of the halt. It never presents a partial traversal as a complete one — gates that did not run are explicitly listed as such.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-741 — Re-Deriving an Upstream Property

Wrong:

```text
RenderGate re-validates storyboard continuity
```

Correct:

```text
RenderGate references the StoryboardGate verdict
```

---

## AP-742 — Running Past a Failure

Wrong:

```text
ShotGate FAIL → run StoryboardGate and RenderGate anyway
```

Correct:

```text
ShotGate FAIL → halt chain; run no downstream gate
```

---

## AP-743 — Mid-Chain Injection

Wrong:

```text
Artifact enters at RenderGate without upstream gates
```

Correct:

```text
Every artifact enters at the chain head and advances only on PASS
```

---

## AP-744 — Silent Partial Traversal

Wrong:

```text
Chain report shows only the gates that ran, implying completion
```

Correct:

```text
Chain report lists gates not run and the halt point
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant GO-701

Gates compose as a directed acyclic dependency graph; no gate depends on a downstream gate.

---

## Invariant GO-702

A gate runs only after every gate it depends on has returned PASS.

---

## Invariant GO-703

Within a stage, element gates precede sequence gates precede cross-stage gates.

---

## Invariant GO-704

A downstream gate consumes upstream verdicts and never re-derives an upstream property.

---

## Invariant GO-705

A dependent check that references an absent or non-PASS upstream verdict fails closed.

---

## Invariant GO-706

A FAIL halts the chain immediately; no downstream gate runs.

---

## Invariant GO-707

The chain resumes at the corrected gate, re-running exactly the gates whose upstream artifact identity changed.

---

## Invariant GO-708

Reaching a gate proves every upstream gate passed; the chain is non-bypassable.

---

## Invariant GO-709

Every stage boundary in the pipeline is covered by a gate in the chain.

---

## Invariant GO-710

The chain report lists gates run, the halt point and reason, and gates not run; it never presents a partial traversal as complete.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-761 | Gates compose as a registered directed acyclic dependency graph.                     |
| ADR-762 | A gate runs only after every upstream gate it depends on has passed.                 |
| ADR-763 | Within a stage, narrow-scope gates precede wide-scope gates.                          |
| ADR-764 | Downstream gates consume upstream verdicts and never re-derive upstream properties.  |
| ADR-765 | A dependent check on an absent or non-PASS upstream verdict fails closed.             |
| ADR-766 | A FAIL halts the chain immediately; downstream gates do not run.                      |
| ADR-767 | The chain resumes at the corrected gate, re-running only affected gates.              |
| ADR-768 | The chain is non-bypassable; reaching a gate proves upstream success.                 |
| ADR-769 | Every pipeline stage boundary is covered by a gate in the chain.                      |
| ADR-770 | The chain report distinguishes gates run from gates not run and names the halt point. |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.7** is complete when:

* The canonical gate chain from Story to Publication is defined.
* Intra-stage ordering by scope (element → sequence → cross-stage) is defined.
* The gate dependency graph is defined as a registered DAG read by the Orchestrator.
* Verdict feed-forward and the prohibition on re-derivation are established and tied to Principle 5.
* Chain halting on first FAIL and resumption at the corrected gate are defined.
* Non-bypassability is established: reaching a gate proves upstream success.
* Global chain invariants — completeness, ordering, monotonicity, attribution — are defined.
* The chain report is specified, distinguishing gates run from gates not run.
* Invariants GO-701 through GO-710 and ADR-761 through ADR-770 are established.

---

# Part 7.1.8 — Gate Result & Reporting

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Gate Report** — the machine-readable record every gate emits — and the reporting contract every gate obeys.

Sections 7.1.4 and 7.1.5 defined the check result and the verdict. This section defines how they are serialized into a durable, immutable, traceable artifact that outlives the evaluation.

A verdict without a report is an assertion. The report is what makes a verdict explainable, auditable, and actionable: it names what was checked, what failed, who owns the failure, and where the artifact must go for correction. The report is the gate's only durable output besides the verdict itself, and the two are always emitted together.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **Every verdict is accompanied by an immutable report that fully explains it. A report is a first-class artifact, not a log line: it is structured, addressed, retained, and traceable to the exact artifact and gate that produced it.**

Two commitments follow.

A report is **complete**: it records every check result, not only the failures, so that a PASS is as explainable as a FAIL. A reader can reconstruct the verdict entirely from the report.

A report is **immutable**: once emitted, it is never edited. A correction produces a new report against a new artifact identity; it never overwrites the prior report. The history of verdicts is append-only.

---

# The Gate Report Schema

Every gate emits a report conforming to the `standard_gate_report_v2` shape.

```json
{
  "report_id": "gr-2026-07-20-shot-014-03",
  "gate_id": "shot_quality_gate",
  "gate_version": "2.0",
  "stage": "shot_planning",
  "artifact_identity": "sha256:9f2c...e41a",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "blocking": true,
  "verdict_function": "all_mandatory_pass",
  "checks": [
    {
      "check_id": "purpose_exists",
      "owner": "4.1.3",
      "class": "mandatory",
      "result": "PASS",
      "evidence": { "expected": "purpose non-empty", "observed": "\"Reveal realization\"" },
      "evaluated": true
    },
    {
      "check_id": "emotion_defined",
      "owner": "4.1.5",
      "class": "mandatory",
      "result": "FAIL",
      "evidence": { "expected": "emotion.before and emotion.after present", "observed": "emotion absent" },
      "evaluated": true
    }
  ],
  "failed_checks": ["emotion_defined"],
  "owning_sections": { "emotion_defined": "4.1.5" },
  "advisory_failures": [],
  "created_at_ref": "build_clock:tick-4821"
}
```

Every field is mandatory. The report records the gate, its version, the exact artifact identity, the verdict, the blocking flag, every check result with evidence, the failing checks, their owners, and any advisory failures.

---

# Report Field Reference

| Field              | Meaning                                                           |
| ------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `report_id`        | Unique identity of this report                                    |
| `gate_id`          | The gate that produced the report                                |
| `gate_version`     | The version of the gate definition                               |
| `stage`            | The pipeline stage guarded                                       |
| `artifact_identity`| The content hash of the evaluated artifact                       |
| `verdict`          | PASS or FAIL                                                      |
| `blocking`         | true on FAIL for a blocking gate, false on PASS                  |
| `verdict_function` | The reduction applied                                            |
| `checks`           | Every check result, with evidence and evaluated flag             |
| `failed_checks`    | The mandatory checks that failed                                 |
| `owning_sections`  | Map from failed check to owning section                          |
| `advisory_failures`| Advisory checks that failed, recorded but non-blocking           |
| `created_at_ref`   | A build-clock reference, not wall-clock time                     |

The report is self-contained: nothing outside it is needed to understand the verdict.

---

# No Wall-Clock in Reports

A report records a build-clock reference, never wall-clock time.

```text
created_at_ref: build_clock:tick-4821
```

Wall-clock timestamps would make a report non-deterministic — the same artifact evaluated twice would produce two different reports. The platform uses a monotonic build-clock reference so that re-evaluating an artifact yields a byte-identical report. Wall-clock time, where needed for human display, is attached externally by the reporting layer and is never part of the report's identity.

This mirrors the workflow-determinism discipline of Part 6: identity-bearing artifacts never embed wall-clock time.

---

# Complete Recording

A report records every check, not only failures.

A PASS report lists every mandatory check as PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE, each with its confirming evidence. This is what makes a PASS auditable: a reviewer can confirm not merely *that* the gate passed but *what* it confirmed.

```text
Wrong:  PASS report is empty or lists only "OK"
Correct: PASS report lists every check, result, and evidence
```

A report that omits passing checks cannot support an audit that asks "was rule X actually checked?" — and that question is exactly what audit exists to answer.

---

# Traceability to the Owning Section

Every failure in a report names the section that owns the violated rule.

```json
"owning_sections": { "emotion_defined": "4.1.5" }
```

The `owning_sections` map routes each failure to the authority responsible for the rule. When the report is returned to the pipeline, the failing artifact goes to the owning stage for correction, not to a generic error handler.

Traceability is the report's actionable payload. A FAIL that names no owner cannot be corrected against an authoritative definition; the report guarantees every FAIL is attributable.

---

# Advisory Failures Are Recorded Separately

Advisory failures appear in a distinct `advisory_failures` field.

```json
"advisory_failures": [
  { "check_id": "pacing_variance", "owner": "4.1.6", "message": "cut rhythm nearing monotony" }
]
```

Advisory failures are recorded because they carry quality signal (7.3), but they are segregated from `failed_checks` so that a reader never mistakes an advisory concern for a blocking failure. An advisory failure never appears in `failed_checks`, and its presence never sets `blocking: true`.

The segregation enforces the 7.1.4 distinction at the report level: advisory means recorded but non-blocking, visibly so.

---

# Report Immutability

A report is immutable once emitted.

```text
Report emitted
        │
        ▼
Never edited, never deleted, never overwritten
        │
        ▼
A correction produces a NEW report against a NEW artifact identity
```

Immutability makes the report a durable record of what the gate concluded at a moment in the build. If the artifact is corrected, the new evaluation emits a new report with a new `artifact_identity`; the old report remains as the record of the prior state.

This is the reporting-layer expression of the artifact-immutability boundary established across the specification: validated records are not mutated in place.

---

# Report Retention

Reports are retained according to the retention policy of the build.

Every gate report produced during a build is retained at least for the life of the build's manifest (Part 6). Reports for a published trailer are retained for the audit horizon defined by governance (7.1.10), because a published artifact must remain explainable long after it shipped.

A report is never discarded while the artifact it describes is still reachable — cached, published, or referenced by a later build.

---

# The Report Is Attached to the Artifact

A gate report is attached to the artifact it describes as planning metadata.

```text
Artifact
   ├── content
   └── gate_reports[]
         ├── shot_quality_gate report
         └── ...
```

The report travels with the artifact through the pipeline and into the cache (Part 6.2). A cached artifact carries the report that last passed it, so a reuse inherits both the PASS verdict and its full explanation. The report is never separated from the artifact identity it was earned against.

---

# Report Aggregation

Individual gate reports aggregate into higher-level reports.

```text
Check results
        │
        ▼
Gate Report          (per gate, this section)
        │
        ▼
Chain Report         (per traversal, 7.1.7)
        │
        ▼
Build Quality Report (per build, 7.3.6)
```

Each level is a faithful aggregation of the level below, never a summary that loses attribution. The Build Quality Report can always be drilled down to the individual check result and evidence that caused any failure. Aggregation adds structure; it never discards the underlying evidence.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-751 — The Log-Line Report

Wrong:

```text
Gate writes "shot 14 failed" to a log
```

Correct:

```text
Gate emits a structured report naming the check, evidence, and owner
```

---

## AP-752 — Overwriting a Report

Wrong:

```text
Artifact corrected → old report edited to PASS
```

Correct:

```text
Artifact corrected → new report emitted under new identity; old report retained
```

---

## AP-753 — PASS Without Detail

Wrong:

```text
PASS report records only "verdict: PASS"
```

Correct:

```text
PASS report records every check, result, and confirming evidence
```

---

## AP-754 — Advisory Mixed Into Failures

Wrong:

```text
advisory failure listed in failed_checks, setting blocking: true
```

Correct:

```text
advisory failure listed in advisory_failures; blocking stays false
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant GR-701

Every verdict is emitted with an immutable, structured Gate Report.

---

## Invariant GR-702

A report records every check result with evidence, not only failures.

---

## Invariant GR-703

A report records the exact artifact identity and the gate identity and version.

---

## Invariant GR-704

A report uses a build-clock reference and embeds no wall-clock time in its identity.

---

## Invariant GR-705

Every failed check is mapped to its owning section in the report.

---

## Invariant GR-706

Advisory failures are recorded in a segregated field and never set the blocking flag.

---

## Invariant GR-707

A report is immutable; corrections produce new reports under new identities.

---

## Invariant GR-708

A report is retained at least as long as the artifact it describes is reachable.

---

## Invariant GR-709

A report is attached to the artifact identity it evaluated and travels with it into the cache.

---

## Invariant GR-710

Aggregated reports preserve full drill-down to the underlying check result and evidence.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-771 | Every verdict is accompanied by an immutable, structured Gate Report.                |
| ADR-772 | Reports record every check result with evidence, including passes.                   |
| ADR-773 | Reports bind to the exact artifact identity and gate identity/version.               |
| ADR-774 | Reports use a build-clock reference, not wall-clock time, for determinism.           |
| ADR-775 | Every failed check is attributed to its owning section in the report.                |
| ADR-776 | Advisory failures are recorded separately and never block.                           |
| ADR-777 | Reports are immutable; corrections emit new reports, never overwrite.                |
| ADR-778 | Reports are retained while their artifact is reachable and for the audit horizon.    |
| ADR-779 | Reports travel with the artifact into the cache and inherit on reuse.                |
| ADR-780 | Aggregated reports preserve full drill-down to check-level evidence.                 |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.8** is complete when:

* The `standard_gate_report_v2` schema is specified with every field defined.
* Reports are shown to record every check with evidence, not only failures.
* The prohibition on wall-clock time in report identity is established for determinism.
* Failure attribution to owning sections is mandatory and defined.
* Advisory failures are segregated from blocking failures in the report.
* Report immutability, retention, and attachment to artifact identity are defined.
* Report aggregation into chain and build reports preserves drill-down.
* Anti-patterns for log-line reports, overwriting, detail-free passes, and advisory mixing are documented.
* Invariants GR-701 through GR-710 and ADR-771 through ADR-780 are established.

---

# Part 7.1.9 — Gate Lifecycle & State Model

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **lifecycle** of a single gate evaluation and the **state model** that governs it.

Sections 7.1.3 through 7.1.8 defined a gate's structure, semantics, and outputs. This section defines the states a gate evaluation moves through, from invocation to verdict, and the rules that govern each transition.

A gate is not instantaneous. It is invoked, it resolves its inputs, it evaluates its checks, it reduces to a verdict, and it emits a report. Each step is a state, and each transition has preconditions. Defining the lifecycle makes gate evaluation observable, recoverable, and idempotent — the same guarantees the platform demands of every long-running operation (Part 6.3).

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A gate evaluation is a state machine with a single terminal verdict. Every state is observable, every transition is guarded, and interruption at any point resolves fail-closed on recovery.**

Two commitments follow.

A gate evaluation is **observable**: at any moment its state is known — resolving inputs, evaluating, reducing, or terminal. The Orchestrator (Part 6.3) can observe and reason about an in-flight gate.

A gate evaluation is **idempotent**: re-invoking a gate on the same artifact identity produces the same verdict and report. A gate that was interrupted mid-evaluation is simply re-run; there is no partial verdict to reconcile.

---

# The Gate Evaluation States

A gate evaluation moves through the following canonical states.

```yaml
INVOKED

RESOLVING

EVALUATING

REDUCING

REPORTING

TERMINAL
```

* **INVOKED** — the gate has been called with an artifact and identity.
* **RESOLVING** — the gate is resolving its definition, configuration, and upstream verdicts.
* **EVALUATING** — the gate is evaluating its checks.
* **REDUCING** — the gate is applying the verdict function to the check results.
* **REPORTING** — the gate is emitting its immutable report.
* **TERMINAL** — the gate has produced a verdict and report and is complete.

The states are ordered. A gate never skips a state and never moves backward.

---

# The Gate State Diagram

```text
INVOKED
   │  inputs present
   ▼
RESOLVING ──── input missing / config unresolvable ──► TERMINAL (FAIL)
   │  resolved
   ▼
EVALUATING ─── check errors ──► TERMINAL (FAIL)
   │  all checks evaluated
   ▼
REDUCING
   │  verdict computed
   ▼
REPORTING
   │  report emitted
   ▼
TERMINAL (PASS | FAIL)
```

Every failure path leads to `TERMINAL (FAIL)`. There is no path from an error state to `TERMINAL (PASS)`. This is the lifecycle expression of the fail-closed model (7.1.5).

---

# State Definitions

## INVOKED

The gate has been invoked with an artifact and its identity.

Entry condition: the Orchestrator has called the gate for a specific stage artifact.

Permitted transition: to `RESOLVING` when the invocation carries an artifact and identity; to `TERMINAL (FAIL)` if the invocation itself is malformed.

---

## RESOLVING

The gate resolves everything it needs before evaluating.

Activities: resolve the gate definition from the registry (7.1.6), resolve the immutable configuration (7.1.11), resolve declared upstream verdicts (7.1.7), and confirm the artifact identity matches the artifact.

Permitted transitions: to `EVALUATING` when all inputs resolve; to `TERMINAL (FAIL)` when any mandatory input is missing, the configuration is unresolvable, or the artifact identity mismatches.

Invariant: a gate never evaluates a check until every input is resolved.

---

## EVALUATING

The gate evaluates its checks.

Activities: run each check as a pure predicate (7.1.4), collecting results and evidence. Checks are independent and may be evaluated in parallel.

Permitted transitions: to `REDUCING` when every check has an evaluated result; to `TERMINAL (FAIL)` when a check errors irrecoverably.

Invariant: an unevaluated mandatory check at the end of `EVALUATING` is recorded and treated as FAIL in reduction.

---

## REDUCING

The gate reduces check results to a verdict.

Activities: apply the declared verdict function (7.1.5) over the check results.

Permitted transition: to `REPORTING` with a computed verdict of PASS or FAIL.

Invariant: the reduction is a pure, deterministic function of the check results.

---

## REPORTING

The gate emits its immutable report.

Activities: serialize the report per the declared report shape (7.1.8), bind it to the artifact identity, and persist it.

Permitted transition: to `TERMINAL` once the report is durably emitted.

Invariant: the verdict is not considered final until its report is durably emitted; verdict and report terminalize together.

---

## TERMINAL

The gate has produced a verdict and report.

Characteristics: the verdict is PASS or FAIL, the report is immutable and persisted, and the evaluation is complete. A terminal gate evaluation is never re-opened; re-validation is a new evaluation with its own lifecycle.

---

# Terminal States

A gate evaluation has exactly one terminal outcome, carrying one of two verdicts.

```text
TERMINAL (PASS)
TERMINAL (FAIL)
```

Both terminal states carry an immutable report. There is no terminal state without a report, and no non-terminal state that yields a durable verdict. The verdict exists only once the evaluation reaches `TERMINAL`.

---

# Interruption and Recovery

A gate evaluation interrupted before `TERMINAL` has produced no verdict.

```text
Interruption in RESOLVING / EVALUATING / REDUCING / REPORTING
        │
        ▼
No durable verdict was emitted
        │
        ▼
Recovery re-invokes the gate from INVOKED
        │
        ▼
Deterministic re-evaluation yields the same verdict
```

Because a verdict terminalizes only with its report, an interruption before `REPORTING` completes leaves no half-verdict to reconcile. Recovery simply re-runs the gate. Because evaluation is deterministic (7.1.5), the re-run produces the identical verdict and report.

This is the gate-level application of the resume-by-default and idempotency principles of Part 6.3: an interrupted operation is safely re-executed, never partially committed.

---

# Idempotent Re-Invocation

Re-invoking a gate on the same artifact identity is idempotent.

```text
evaluate(gate, artifact_identity = X)  →  verdict V, report R
evaluate(gate, artifact_identity = X)  →  verdict V, report R   (identical)
```

A second invocation on an unchanged artifact yields the same verdict and a byte-identical report (7.1.8). The platform may serve the cached report (Part 6.2) rather than re-evaluating, but the guarantee is that re-evaluation would produce the same result. Idempotence is what makes caching a gate verdict safe.

---

# State Ownership

Gate evaluation state is owned by the evaluation engine, recorded in the manifest.

The evaluation engine (7.1.3) drives the state machine. The current state of an in-flight gate is recorded in the runtime manifest (Part 6.3.11), so the Orchestrator can observe it and recovery can determine that no terminal verdict was reached. The gate's state is never held only in volatile memory; a crash loses at most the in-flight evaluation, never a committed verdict.

---

# State Metrics

The lifecycle emits observability metrics.

```yaml
gate_lifecycle_metrics:
  resolve_duration:
  evaluate_duration:
  reduce_duration:
  report_duration:
  total_duration:
  interrupted_count:
  re_evaluation_count:
```

These metrics feed the operational dashboards (7.3.6) and the performance telemetry of Part 6.1. A gate that spends excessive time in `EVALUATING` is a signal to optimize a check — never to skip it.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-761 — The Partial Verdict

Wrong:

```text
Evaluation interrupted in REDUCING
        │
        ▼
Emit a provisional PASS to be confirmed later
```

Correct:

```text
Evaluation interrupted before TERMINAL
        │
        ▼
No verdict exists; re-run from INVOKED
```

---

## AP-762 — Evaluating Before Resolving

Wrong:

```text
Start EVALUATING while configuration is still loading
```

Correct:

```text
Complete RESOLVING before any check runs
```

---

## AP-763 — Verdict Without Report

Wrong:

```text
Reach TERMINAL with a verdict but no persisted report
```

Correct:

```text
Verdict and report terminalize together
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant GL-701

A gate evaluation moves through the ordered states INVOKED, RESOLVING, EVALUATING, REDUCING, REPORTING, TERMINAL.

---

## Invariant GL-702

A gate never evaluates a check until all inputs are resolved.

---

## Invariant GL-703

Every error or missing-input path leads to TERMINAL (FAIL); no error path yields PASS.

---

## Invariant GL-704

A verdict exists only at TERMINAL and terminalizes together with its immutable report.

---

## Invariant GL-705

An interruption before TERMINAL produces no durable verdict.

---

## Invariant GL-706

Recovery re-invokes an interrupted gate from INVOKED and deterministically reproduces the verdict.

---

## Invariant GL-707

Re-invocation on the same artifact identity is idempotent in verdict and report.

---

## Invariant GL-708

Gate evaluation state is recorded in the manifest, never held only in volatile memory.

---

## Invariant GL-709

The reduction in REDUCING is a pure, deterministic function of the check results.

---

## Invariant GL-710

A terminal evaluation is never re-opened; re-validation is a new evaluation with its own lifecycle.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-781 | A gate evaluation is an ordered state machine ending in a single terminal verdict.   |
| ADR-782 | Inputs are fully resolved before any check is evaluated.                             |
| ADR-783 | Every error and missing-input path terminalizes as FAIL.                            |
| ADR-784 | A verdict and its immutable report terminalize together.                            |
| ADR-785 | Interruption before terminal produces no durable verdict.                           |
| ADR-786 | Recovery re-runs an interrupted gate deterministically from the start.               |
| ADR-787 | Re-invocation on an unchanged artifact is idempotent.                               |
| ADR-788 | Gate evaluation state is persisted in the manifest for observability and recovery.   |
| ADR-789 | The verdict reduction is a pure, deterministic function.                             |
| ADR-790 | Terminal evaluations are never re-opened; re-validation is a fresh evaluation.       |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.9** is complete when:

* The six-state gate evaluation lifecycle is defined with entry conditions and transitions.
* The state diagram routes every error path to TERMINAL (FAIL).
* Each state is defined with its activities, permitted transitions, and invariant.
* The terminal verdict is shown to terminalize together with its immutable report.
* Interruption and recovery are defined as fail-closed and deterministic.
* Idempotent re-invocation is established and tied to caching.
* State ownership in the manifest and lifecycle metrics are defined.
* Anti-patterns for partial verdicts, premature evaluation, and verdict-without-report are documented.
* Invariants GL-701 through GL-710 and ADR-781 through ADR-790 are established.

---

# Part 7.1.10 — Gate Governance & Authority Model

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **governance** of Quality Gates: who may author, configure, waive, and retire gates, and the **authority model** that separates these powers.

Sections 7.1.1 through 7.1.9 defined how a gate works. This section defines who is allowed to change how a gate works, and under what recorded conditions a gate's verdict may be excused.

Governance is what prevents the fail-closed model from being quietly dismantled. A gate is only as strong as the rules about who can weaken it. Without governance, any operator under deadline pressure could lower a threshold, demote a blocking gate, or excuse a failure — and the entire quality architecture would become advisory in practice. This section makes every such action a distinct, authorized, recorded governance decision.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **The power to enforce a rule, the power to author it, and the power to excuse its failure are held by different authorities. Every governance action is explicit, authorized, and permanently recorded.**

Two commitments follow.

Governance is **separated**: no single actor can both write a rule and excuse its violation, nor both enforce a gate and waive its failures. Separation of duties is the structural defense against self-serving relaxation.

Governance is **auditable**: every authoring, configuration, waiver, and retirement decision is recorded in an append-only log with its authority, its justification, and its scope. A governance action that leaves no record did not happen.

---

# The Four Governance Powers

Governance distinguishes four powers over a gate.

```text
Author    → define the rule a check enforces
Configure → set the thresholds a gate reads
Enforce   → run the gate and produce verdicts
Waive     → record an accepted exception to a FAIL
```

* **Author** — belongs to the owning section's authority (e.g. the Story Engine authority owns story rules).
* **Configure** — belongs to a configuration authority that sets thresholds within a profile.
* **Enforce** — belongs to the gate engine, which is mechanical and holds no discretion.
* **Waive** — belongs to a distinct waiver authority, exercised only within strict limits.

The powers are held by distinct authorities. This is the concrete form of Principle 8 (Separation of Duties).

---

# The Authority Hierarchy

```text
Governance Authority
        │
        ├── Rule Authority        (per owning section)
        ├── Configuration Authority
        ├── Enforcement Authority (the gate engine — mechanical)
        └── Waiver Authority
```

Governance Authority sits above the four powers and defines the policies that bind them. It does not itself enforce or waive; it sets the rules under which the other authorities operate, and it owns the audit log.

No authority may assume another's power. The Configuration Authority cannot author a rule. The Waiver Authority cannot enforce a gate. The Enforcement Authority — being a mechanical engine — holds no discretionary power at all.

---

# Separation of Duties Matrix

| Power     | Held by                  | May also hold                     | May never also hold        |
| --------- | ------------------------ | --------------------------------- | -------------------------- |
| Author    | Rule Authority           | —                                 | Waive over the same rule   |
| Configure | Configuration Authority  | —                                 | Waive within same build    |
| Enforce   | Gate Engine (mechanical) | —                                 | Author, Configure, Waive   |
| Waive     | Waiver Authority         | —                                 | Author or Configure same rule |

The matrix is the structural guarantee against a single actor lowering the bar and then excusing the result.

---

# The Waiver

A waiver is the single, narrow mechanism for proceeding despite a recorded FAIL.

A waiver does **not** change a verdict. The gate still returns FAIL, the report still records the failure, and the chain still records the halt. A waiver is a separate, authorized decision — recorded alongside the FAIL — to proceed with the build despite the failure.

```text
Gate FAIL (recorded, immutable)
        │
        ▼
Waiver Authority records a waiver
   ├── references the exact report and failing checks
   ├── states an explicit justification
   ├── declares a bounded scope
   └── carries an expiry
        │
        ▼
Build may proceed under the recorded waiver
```

The waiver references the FAIL; it never erases it. Audit can always see both the failure and the decision to accept it.

---

# Waiver Constraints

A waiver is tightly bounded.

* A waiver references a specific gate report and specific failing checks; a blanket waiver over "all failures" is prohibited.
* A waiver carries an explicit written justification; an unjustified waiver is invalid.
* A waiver has a bounded scope — one build, or one artifact identity — and never applies globally.
* A waiver has an expiry; it is never permanent.
* A waiver over a **safety-critical** or **publication-integrity** check is prohibited outright; certain checks are non-waivable by policy.
* A waiver is granted by the Waiver Authority, never by the actor who authored or configured the rule.

A waiver that violates any constraint is itself invalid and is rejected.

---

# Non-Waivable Checks

Certain checks may never be waived.

```yaml
non_waivable:
  - publication_rights_cleared
  - child_safety_validated
  - continuity_no_backward_time
  - render_matches_approved_storyboard
```

Non-waivable checks encode guarantees the platform will not proceed without, regardless of authority or deadline. A FAIL on a non-waivable check halts the build absolutely; no waiver can release it. The list of non-waivable checks is itself governed and versioned.

This is the hard floor beneath the waiver mechanism: waivers create flexibility for judgment calls, never for integrity or safety.

---

# The Governance Audit Log

Every governance action is recorded in an append-only audit log.

```json
{
  "action": "waiver_granted",
  "authority": "editorial_lead",
  "gate_report_ref": "gr-2026-07-20-shot-014-03",
  "failing_checks": ["pacing_variance"],
  "justification": "Deliberate slow cadence approved for this narrative beat.",
  "scope": { "build_id": "build-2026-07-20-001" },
  "expiry_ref": "build_clock:end-of-build",
  "recorded_at_ref": "build_clock:tick-5210"
}
```

The log records what was done, by which authority, against which report, with what justification, in what scope, and until when. The log is append-only and immutable: a governance action, once recorded, is never edited or deleted.

The audit log is the evidentiary basis for reviewing whether the quality architecture was respected. A published trailer's full governance history — every waiver, every configuration change — is reconstructable from the log.

---

# Authoring and Retiring Gates

Creating, changing, or retiring a gate is a governed action.

* **Authoring a gate** produces a new gate definition with a new `(gate_id, gate_version)` and is recorded.
* **Changing a gate** produces a new version; the prior version is retained. A gate is never edited in place.
* **Demoting a blocking gate** to advisory-influence (7.1.6) requires Governance Authority approval and is recorded, because it removes blocking power.
* **Retiring a gate** is recorded with a justification; a stage boundary is never left ungated by retirement — a retirement must name the replacement gate or an explicit, approved decision to remove the boundary.

No gate appears, changes authority, or disappears without a recorded governance decision.

---

# Governance and Configuration

Configuration changes are governed but distinct from waivers.

A configuration change (7.1.11) sets thresholds for *future* builds; it never rescues a *current* failing artifact, because configuration is immutable within a build (Principle 10). Lowering a threshold to pass an in-flight artifact is prohibited; the only in-build mechanism for proceeding despite a FAIL is a waiver, with all its constraints.

```text
Wrong:  in-build FAIL → Configuration Authority lowers threshold → artifact passes
Correct: in-build FAIL → Waiver Authority records a bounded, justified waiver (if permitted)
         future builds → Configuration Authority may adjust threshold with governance record
```

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-771 — The Self-Waiver

Wrong:

```text
The author of a rule waives its own failure
```

Correct:

```text
A distinct Waiver Authority records the waiver; authors cannot waive their own rules
```

---

## AP-772 — The Blanket Waiver

Wrong:

```text
Waiver excuses "all quality failures" for a build
```

Correct:

```text
Waiver references specific checks in a specific report with justification and expiry
```

---

## AP-773 — Threshold Tuning to Pass

Wrong:

```text
In-build FAIL → lower the threshold in place → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
Configuration is immutable in-build; use a bounded waiver, or correct the artifact
```

---

## AP-774 — The Unrecorded Exception

Wrong:

```text
Operator proceeds past a FAIL with a verbal approval
```

Correct:

```text
Every exception is a recorded waiver in the append-only audit log
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant GG-701

The powers to author, configure, enforce, and waive are held by distinct authorities.

---

## Invariant GG-702

The Enforcement Authority is mechanical and holds no discretionary power.

---

## Invariant GG-703

A waiver records an accepted exception to a FAIL and never changes the verdict.

---

## Invariant GG-704

A waiver references specific checks in a specific report, carries a justification, a bounded scope, and an expiry.

---

## Invariant GG-705

A waiver is never granted by the actor who authored or configured the waived rule.

---

## Invariant GG-706

Non-waivable checks exist and cannot be released by any waiver.

---

## Invariant GG-707

Every governance action is recorded in an append-only, immutable audit log.

---

## Invariant GG-708

Creating, versioning, demoting, and retiring gates are recorded governance actions.

---

## Invariant GG-709

Configuration changes affect future builds only and never rescue an in-build failing artifact.

---

## Invariant GG-710

No gate appears, changes authority, or is retired without a recorded governance decision, and no stage boundary is left ungated by retirement.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-791 | Author, configure, enforce, and waive are separated governance powers.               |
| ADR-792 | The gate engine enforces mechanically and holds no discretion.                       |
| ADR-793 | A waiver records an exception without changing the verdict.                          |
| ADR-794 | Waivers are specific, justified, scoped, and expiring; blanket waivers are prohibited. |
| ADR-795 | Rule authors and configurers may not waive their own rules.                          |
| ADR-796 | Certain safety and publication-integrity checks are non-waivable.                    |
| ADR-797 | Every governance action is recorded in an append-only audit log.                     |
| ADR-798 | Gate creation, versioning, demotion, and retirement are governed and recorded.        |
| ADR-799 | Configuration changes apply to future builds and never rescue an in-build failure.    |
| ADR-800 | No stage boundary is left ungated by a gate retirement.                              |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.10** is complete when:

* The four governance powers — author, configure, enforce, waive — are defined and separated.
* The authority hierarchy and separation-of-duties matrix are specified.
* The waiver is defined as an exception that records, but never changes, a FAIL verdict.
* Waiver constraints — specificity, justification, scope, expiry, and non-self-waiver — are enumerated.
* Non-waivable checks are defined as a governed, versioned hard floor.
* The append-only governance audit log is specified.
* Gate authoring, versioning, demotion, and retirement are established as recorded governance actions.
* The distinction between in-build waivers and future-build configuration changes is defined.
* Anti-patterns for self-waiver, blanket waiver, threshold tuning, and unrecorded exceptions are documented.
* Invariants GG-701 through GG-710 and ADR-791 through ADR-800 are established.

---

# Part 7.1.11 — Gate Configuration Architecture

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **configuration architecture** of Quality Gates: how a gate's thresholds, profiles, and tolerances are declared, resolved, versioned, and frozen for a build.

Section 7.1.3 established that a gate reads its thresholds from a configuration reference rather than hard-coding them. This section defines what that configuration is, how it is structured, and the rules that keep it deterministic and immutable within a build.

Configuration is what lets one gate definition serve development, preview, and production builds by reading a different threshold under each profile — without changing the gate's identity-bearing structure. It is also where the platform is most tempted to cheat: lowering a threshold to pass a stubborn artifact. The configuration architecture makes that impossible within a build.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **Gate configuration is declarative, hierarchical, versioned, and immutable for the duration of a build. A gate resolves its configuration once, at build start, and evaluates every artifact of that build against the frozen values.**

Three commitments follow.

Configuration is **declarative**: thresholds are stated as data in versioned files, never computed at evaluation time. A gate reads a value; it does not derive one.

Configuration is **hierarchical**: values are layered — platform defaults, profile overrides, build-specific settings — with a defined precedence, so common values are stated once and specialized only where needed.

Configuration is **frozen per build**: once resolved at build start, configuration does not change until the build ends. This is Principle 10 (Immutable During a Build) expressed as an architecture.

---

# The Configuration Hierarchy

Gate configuration is layered.

```text
Platform Defaults          (lowest precedence)
        │
        ▼
Build Profile Overrides    (development | preview | production | benchmark)
        │
        ▼
Build-Specific Settings    (highest precedence)
        │
        ▼
Resolved Configuration     (frozen for the build)
```

Higher layers override lower layers for the values they specify. A value not specified at a higher layer inherits from the layer below. The resolution flattens the hierarchy into a single, complete, frozen configuration for the build.

This mirrors the configuration hierarchy of Part 6.1.8: a root default, profile overrides, and a runtime snapshot.

---

# The Gate Configuration Schema

A gate's configuration is a versioned object.

```yaml
gate_configuration:
  config_id: shot_quality_gate
  config_version: "2.0"
  applies_to_gate: shot_quality_gate
  thresholds:
    camera_movements_max: 1
    primary_subjects_max: 2
  scoring:
    threshold: 0.90
    weights:
      continuity_valid: 1.0
      emotion_defined: 0.8
  tolerances:
    duration_seconds_min: 1
  profile: production
```

The configuration declares the thresholds the gate's checks read, any scoring threshold and weights (7.3), tolerances, and the profile it belongs to. Every value a check reads as a `configuration_value` (7.1.4) is declared here.

---

# Configuration Field Reference

| Field             | Meaning                                                         |
| ----------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `config_id`       | Identity of the configuration object                           |
| `config_version`  | Version of the configuration                                   |
| `applies_to_gate` | The gate this configuration parameterizes                      |
| `thresholds`      | Named limits the gate's checks compare against                 |
| `scoring`         | Score threshold and per-check weights (7.3)                    |
| `tolerances`      | Permitted ranges for continuous values                        |
| `profile`         | The build profile this configuration belongs to               |

A gate reads only the configuration whose `applies_to_gate` matches its `gate_id`. A configuration never silently applies to a gate it was not declared for.

---

# Build Profiles

Configuration is specialized per build profile.

| Profile       | Intent                              | Threshold posture                          |
| ------------- | ----------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------ |
| `development` | Fast iteration                      | May relax advisory thresholds; mandatory checks unchanged |
| `preview`     | Structural validation, cheap        | Preview caps (e.g. lower hybrid ratio)     |
| `production`  | Final, shippable                    | Strictest thresholds                       |
| `benchmark`   | Reproducible measurement            | Fixed, never tuned                         |

A profile may relax **advisory** thresholds for speed, but it never weakens a **mandatory** check. The mandatory floor is identical across all profiles; only advisory and scoring thresholds vary. A development build and a production build enforce the same mandatory admissibility conditions.

This preserves the guarantee that "PASS" means the same mandatory thing everywhere, while allowing advisory strictness to scale with the build's purpose.

---

# Mandatory Floor Is Profile-Invariant

No profile lowers a mandatory check.

```text
mandatory checks      → identical across development, preview, production, benchmark
advisory thresholds   → may vary by profile
scoring threshold     → may vary by profile
```

A `production` build and a `development` build differ in advisory strictness and scoring, never in what makes an artifact fundamentally admissible. This is what allows a `development` PASS to be trusted as far as it goes: it guarantees the mandatory floor was met, even if advisory strictness was relaxed.

A configuration that attempted to relax a mandatory check under any profile is invalid and rejected at resolution.

---

# Configuration Resolution

Configuration is resolved once, at build start.

```text
Build starts
        │
        ▼
Resolve platform defaults
        │
        ▼
Apply profile overrides
        │
        ▼
Apply build-specific settings
        │
        ▼
Validate resolved configuration
        │
        ▼
Freeze as the Build Gate Configuration Snapshot
```

The resolution produces a single, complete, validated snapshot. Every gate in the build reads its thresholds from this snapshot. Resolution happens exactly once; a gate never re-resolves configuration mid-build.

---

# The Configuration Snapshot Is Immutable

The resolved snapshot is frozen for the build.

```text
Build Gate Configuration Snapshot
   ├── frozen at build start
   ├── read by every gate evaluation
   └── never mutated until the build ends
```

No gate, operator, or process changes a threshold after the snapshot is frozen. An artifact that fails at a frozen threshold is corrected or waived (7.1.10); the threshold is not lowered to accommodate it. Changing a threshold requires a new build with a newly resolved snapshot.

Immutability of the snapshot is the architectural enforcement of AP-702 (the tuned-to-pass threshold) and AP-773 (threshold tuning to pass).

---

# Configuration Validation

A configuration is validated before it is frozen.

Validation confirms:

* every threshold a gate's checks reference is present;
* no mandatory check is relaxed by any profile;
* scoring weights are well-formed and reference existing checks;
* the profile is a recognized profile;
* the configuration version is well-formed.

A configuration that fails validation is rejected, and the build fails closed at start rather than running against an invalid configuration. The platform never evaluates a gate against unvalidated thresholds.

---

# Configuration Versioning

Configuration is versioned independently of the gate definition.

```text
Gate definition   → (gate_id, gate_version)
Gate configuration → (config_id, config_version)
```

A configuration change produces a new `config_version`; the prior version is retained. A build records both the `gate_version` and the `config_version` it ran under, so a verdict is fully reproducible: re-running the gate requires the same definition *and* the same configuration.

A configuration version is never edited in place, consistent with the versioning discipline used throughout the specification.

---

# Configuration Is Recorded in the Report

The configuration a gate ran under is recorded in its report.

```json
"configuration": { "config_id": "shot_quality_gate", "config_version": "2.0", "profile": "production" }
```

A gate report (7.1.8) records the configuration identity and version it evaluated against, so a verdict can be reproduced exactly and audited against the thresholds that produced it. A verdict whose configuration is unknown is not reproducible, and the platform requires every verdict to be reproducible.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-781 — In-Build Threshold Mutation

Wrong:

```text
Artifact fails at threshold 0.90
        │
        ▼
Edit the snapshot to 0.80 mid-build
```

Correct:

```text
Snapshot is frozen; correct the artifact, or record a waiver, or adjust config for a future build
```

---

## AP-782 — Profile Relaxing a Mandatory Check

Wrong:

```text
development profile sets continuity_valid to advisory
```

Correct:

```text
Mandatory floor is profile-invariant; only advisory thresholds vary
```

---

## AP-783 — Hard-Coded Threshold

Wrong:

```text
Check compares against a literal 0.50 in code
```

Correct:

```text
Check reads runway_ratio_max from the resolved configuration
```

---

## AP-784 — Unrecorded Configuration

Wrong:

```text
Report omits the config version the gate ran under
```

Correct:

```text
Report records config_id, config_version, and profile
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant GC-701

Gate configuration is declarative data, never computed at evaluation time.

---

## Invariant GC-702

Configuration is hierarchical: platform defaults, profile overrides, and build-specific settings, with defined precedence.

---

## Invariant GC-703

Configuration is resolved exactly once at build start into a frozen snapshot.

---

## Invariant GC-704

The configuration snapshot is immutable for the duration of the build.

---

## Invariant GC-705

No build profile relaxes a mandatory check; the mandatory floor is profile-invariant.

---

## Invariant GC-706

A configuration is validated before it is frozen; an invalid configuration fails the build closed at start.

---

## Invariant GC-707

Configuration is versioned as `(config_id, config_version)` and never edited in place.

---

## Invariant GC-708

A gate reads only the configuration declared to apply to it.

---

## Invariant GC-709

A gate report records the configuration identity and version it evaluated against.

---

## Invariant GC-710

A threshold is never mutated in-build to rescue a failing artifact.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-801 | Gate configuration is declarative, versioned data read by gates, not hard-coded.     |
| ADR-802 | Configuration is hierarchical with defined precedence across defaults, profile, and build. |
| ADR-803 | Configuration is resolved once at build start into a frozen, immutable snapshot.      |
| ADR-804 | The mandatory floor is identical across all build profiles.                          |
| ADR-805 | Profiles may relax advisory and scoring thresholds only.                             |
| ADR-806 | Configuration is validated before freezing; invalid configuration fails the build closed. |
| ADR-807 | Configuration is versioned independently of the gate definition and never edited in place. |
| ADR-808 | A gate reads only its own applicable configuration.                                  |
| ADR-809 | The configuration identity and version are recorded in every gate report.            |
| ADR-810 | In-build threshold mutation to pass an artifact is prohibited.                        |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.11** is complete when:

* The configuration hierarchy — defaults, profile overrides, build-specific settings — is defined with precedence.
* The gate configuration schema is specified with thresholds, scoring, tolerances, and profile.
* The build profiles are defined, and the mandatory floor is established as profile-invariant.
* Configuration resolution into a frozen, immutable per-build snapshot is defined.
* Configuration validation before freezing is defined and fails closed on invalidity.
* Independent configuration versioning and its recording in reports are established.
* The prohibition on in-build threshold mutation is defined and tied to Principle 10.
* Anti-patterns for in-build mutation, mandatory relaxation, hard-coded thresholds, and unrecorded configuration are documented.
* Invariants GC-701 through GC-710 and ADR-801 through ADR-810 are established.

---

# Part 7.1.12 — Architecture Decision Records (Quality Gate Architecture)

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section consolidates the **Architecture Decision Records** of the Quality Gate Architecture into a single authoritative register.

Sections 7.1.1 through 7.1.11 each recorded the ADRs local to their subject. This section gathers the load-bearing decisions into one place, defines their relationships, and establishes the governance under which they may change.

An ADR is a durable record of a decision, its rationale, and its consequences. The register exists so that a reader can understand the whole architecture's decision structure without reassembling it from eleven subsections, and so that a proposed change can be evaluated against the decisions it would disturb.

---

# ADR Philosophy

The platform treats architectural decisions as versioned, referenced facts.

> **A decision that is not recorded is not a decision; it is an accident waiting to be re-litigated.**

Each ADR states a decision the architecture depends on. An ADR is never silently reversed. A change to an ADR is a new decision, recorded as a superseding ADR, with the prior ADR retained and marked superseded.

---
