# ADR Lifecycle

```text
PROPOSED
   │  accepted
   ▼
ACCEPTED ──── superseded ──► SUPERSEDED
   │
   ▼
(referenced by invariants, gates, and checks)
```

An ADR is `PROPOSED`, then `ACCEPTED`, and may later be `SUPERSEDED` by a newer ADR. An accepted ADR is immutable; it is never edited. Superseding an ADR requires the same governance authority that would author a gate rule (7.1.10).

---

# The Foundational Decisions

The Quality Gate Architecture rests on ten foundational decisions.

| ADR     | Foundational Decision                                                        | Established in |
| ------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------- |
| ADR-701 | A gate is a deterministic, fail-closed stage-boundary checkpoint.            | 7.1.1          |
| ADR-703 | A gate enforces rules owned upstream and authors none.                       | 7.1.1          |
| ADR-713 | Every gate is fail-closed by default.                                        | 7.1.2          |
| ADR-722 | Gates are declarative data executed by one generic engine.                  | 7.1.3          |
| ADR-731 | A check is the atomic unit and enforces exactly one owned rule.              | 7.1.4          |
| ADR-741 | The verdict set is closed at {PASS, FAIL}.                                   | 7.1.5          |
| ADR-756 | A gate's full type is a tuple across four independent axes.                  | 7.1.6          |
| ADR-761 | Gates compose as a registered directed acyclic dependency graph.            | 7.1.7          |
| ADR-771 | Every verdict is accompanied by an immutable, structured report.            | 7.1.8          |
| ADR-793 | A waiver records an exception without changing the verdict.                  | 7.1.10         |

These ten decisions are the ones from which the rest of the architecture derives. Disturbing any of them disturbs the whole.

---

# The Complete ADR Register

The Quality Gate Architecture defines ADR-701 through ADR-810.

| Range           | Subject                                        | Section |
| --------------- | ---------------------------------------------- | ------- |
| ADR-701–ADR-710 | Purpose & Quality Gate Boundary                | 7.1.1   |
| ADR-711–ADR-720 | Quality Philosophy & Governing Principles      | 7.1.2   |
| ADR-721–ADR-730 | Gate Model & Gate Anatomy                      | 7.1.3   |
| ADR-731–ADR-740 | Check Model & Check Contracts                  | 7.1.4   |
| ADR-741–ADR-750 | Pass/Fail Semantics & Fail-Closed Model        | 7.1.5   |
| ADR-751–ADR-760 | Gate Types & Classification                    | 7.1.6   |
| ADR-761–ADR-770 | Gate Ordering, Composition & the Gate Chain    | 7.1.7   |
| ADR-771–ADR-780 | Gate Result & Reporting                        | 7.1.8   |
| ADR-781–ADR-790 | Gate Lifecycle & State Model                   | 7.1.9   |
| ADR-791–ADR-800 | Gate Governance & Authority Model              | 7.1.10  |
| ADR-801–ADR-810 | Gate Configuration Architecture                | 7.1.11  |
| ADR-811–ADR-815 | Architecture Decision Records (this subsection)| 7.1.12  |
| ADR-816–ADR-820 | Section Summary & Interface to 7.2             | 7.1.13  |

The register is contiguous and gap-free across ADR-701 through ADR-820, inclusive of the decision records of this subsection (ADR-811–ADR-815) and of 7.1.13 (ADR-816–ADR-820). Part 7.2 continues the numbering from ADR-821.

---

# ADR Dependency Graph

The foundational decisions depend on one another in a fixed structure.

```text
ADR-701 (fail-closed checkpoint)
   │
   ├──► ADR-713 (fail-closed default)
   │        │
   │        └──► ADR-741 (closed verdict set)
   │                 │
   │                 └──► ADR-793 (waiver records, never changes verdict)
   │
   ├──► ADR-703 (enforce, not author)
   │        │
   │        └──► ADR-731 (check enforces one owned rule)
   │
   ├──► ADR-722 (declarative, one engine)
   │        │
   │        └──► ADR-756 (four-axis type)
   │
   └──► ADR-761 (DAG composition)
            │
            └──► ADR-771 (immutable report)
```

The graph is acyclic. A decision never depends, directly or transitively, on a decision that depends on it. This is what allows a change to be scoped: superseding a leaf decision disturbs less than superseding a root.

`ADR-701` is the root. Every other foundational decision is reachable from it. Reversing `ADR-701` would collapse the entire architecture, which is why it is the most heavily governed decision in Part 7.

---

# ADR Governance

An ADR is changed only through governance.

* An ADR is superseded, never edited.
* A superseding ADR references the ADR it supersedes and states why.
* Superseding a foundational ADR requires Governance Authority approval (7.1.10) and is recorded in the audit log.
* Every invariant, gate, and check that references a superseded ADR is re-evaluated against the superseding decision.

Because invariants and checks reference ADRs by number, the register is the anchor point for reasoning about the impact of any architectural change.

---

# ADR Repository Structure

ADRs are stored as versioned records alongside the gates they govern.

```text
gates/
  adr/
    ADR-701.md
    ADR-702.md
    ...
    ADR-810.md
  registry/
    gate_registry.yaml
    gate_dependency_graph.yaml
```

Each ADR is an individually addressable, immutable record. The registry references ADRs by number; the ADR repository is the source of truth for their content.

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant ADR7-701

Every load-bearing decision of the Quality Gate Architecture is recorded as an ADR in the range ADR-701 through ADR-810.

---

## Invariant ADR7-702

An accepted ADR is immutable and is superseded, never edited.

---

## Invariant ADR7-703

A superseding ADR references the ADR it supersedes and states its rationale.

---

## Invariant ADR7-704

The ADR dependency graph is acyclic.

---

## Invariant ADR7-705

Superseding a foundational ADR requires Governance Authority approval and an audit record.

---

## Invariant ADR7-706

Every invariant, gate, and check references the ADRs it depends on by number.

---

## Invariant ADR7-707

The ADR register is contiguous and gap-free across its declared range.

---

## Invariant ADR7-708

Part 7.2 continues ADR numbering from ADR-821 without reusing a number.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-811 | Architectural decisions are recorded as versioned, referenced ADRs.                 |
| ADR-812 | An accepted ADR is immutable and superseded, never edited.                          |
| ADR-813 | The ADR dependency graph is acyclic, with ADR-701 as its root.                      |
| ADR-814 | Superseding a foundational ADR is a governed, audited action.                       |
| ADR-815 | Invariants, gates, and checks reference their governing ADRs by number.             |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.12** is complete when:

* The ADR philosophy and lifecycle are defined.
* The ten foundational decisions are identified and traced to their sections.
* The complete ADR register (ADR-701–ADR-810) is presented and shown to be contiguous.
* The ADR dependency graph is defined as acyclic with ADR-701 as its root.
* ADR governance — superseding, not editing, under recorded authority — is defined.
* The ADR repository structure is specified.
* Invariants ADR7-701 through ADR7-708 and ADR-811 through ADR-815 are established.

# Part 7.1.13 — Section Summary & Interface to 7.2

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section summarizes the **Quality Gate Architecture** established across Section 7.1 and defines its **interface** to the concrete pipeline-stage gates of Section 7.2.

Section 7.1 defined what a gate is. Section 7.2 defines the specific gates the platform runs. This section is the seam between them: it states the stable contracts every gate in 7.2 inherits, and it hands the architecture forward.

The interface is a promise. Every gate in Part 7.2 is an instance of the architecture defined here, and this section makes explicit exactly what "an instance" is required to satisfy.

---

# Quality Gate Architecture Overview

Section 7.1 established a complete, reusable gate architecture.

```text
7.1.1  → Purpose & Quality Gate Boundary
7.1.2  → Quality Philosophy & Governing Principles
7.1.3  → Gate Model & Gate Anatomy
7.1.4  → Check Model & Check Contracts
7.1.5  → Pass/Fail Semantics & the Fail-Closed Model
7.1.6  → Gate Types & Classification
7.1.7  → Gate Ordering, Composition & the Gate Chain
7.1.8  → Gate Result & Reporting
7.1.9  → Gate Lifecycle & State Model
7.1.10 → Gate Governance & Authority Model
7.1.11 → Gate Configuration Architecture
7.1.12 → Architecture Decision Records
7.1.13 → Section Summary & Interface to 7.2
```

Together these subsections define a gate as a deterministic, fail-closed, declarative, governed, and configurable checkpoint — one that any specific gate in the platform can be built as an instance of.

---

# Responsibilities Established by Section 7.1

Section 7.1 established the following responsibilities.

* the **boundary** a gate occupies and the contracts it consumes and produces;
* the **philosophy** every gate embodies, grounded in the cost-of-defect curve;
* the **anatomy** of a gate and the single engine that executes all gates;
* the **check** as the atomic, owned, deterministic unit of evaluation;
* the **verdict semantics** and the fail-closed reduction to {PASS, FAIL};
* the **classification** of gates along four independent axes;
* the **composition** of gates into a non-bypassable chain;
* the **report** every gate emits, immutable and traceable;
* the **lifecycle** of a single evaluation and its recovery semantics;
* the **governance** that separates authoring, enforcing, and waiving;
* the **configuration** that is frozen and profile-invariant at the mandatory floor.

---

# The Canonical Gate Contract

Every gate in the platform satisfies one contract.

```text
Input:  artifact + artifact_identity + gate_definition + frozen configuration + upstream verdicts
Process: RESOLVE → EVALUATE checks → REDUCE (fail-closed) → REPORT
Output: verdict ∈ {PASS, FAIL} + immutable Gate Report
```

This contract is the whole of what 7.2 inherits. A gate that satisfies it is a valid instance of the architecture; a gate that violates it is not a gate.

---

# Stable Architectural Invariants

Ten invariants hold for every gate in the platform, regardless of stage.

## Invariant 1

Every gate is deterministic: identical artifact identity and configuration yield an identical verdict and report.

---

## Invariant 2

Every gate is fail-closed: absence, ambiguity, and error resolve to FAIL.

---

## Invariant 3

Every gate returns exactly one verdict from {PASS, FAIL}, always with an immutable report.

---

## Invariant 4

Every check enforces exactly one rule owned by an upstream section.

---

## Invariant 5

Every verdict is bound to the exact artifact identity evaluated.

---

## Invariant 6

Every gate is an instance of the shared anatomy, executed by one engine.

---

## Invariant 7

Gates compose as a non-bypassable, acyclic chain; reaching a gate proves upstream success.

---

## Invariant 8

Every verdict is traceable to its failing checks and their owning sections.

---

## Invariant 9

Authoring, enforcing, and waiving are separated powers, and every governance action is recorded.

---

## Invariant 10

Gate definition and configuration are immutable for the duration of a build; the mandatory floor is profile-invariant.

---

# Architectural Contracts

Section 7.1 exposes five contracts to downstream sections.

## Definition Contract

A gate is a declarative `GateDefinition` — identity, checks, verdict function, report shape, configuration reference — validated before execution.

---

## Evaluation Contract

A gate is executed by the single `GateEvaluationEngine`, which resolves inputs, evaluates checks, reduces fail-closed, and emits a report.

---

## Verdict Contract

A gate returns exactly one verdict from {PASS, FAIL}, bound to the artifact identity, accompanied by an immutable report.

---

## Governance Contract

A gate's rules, thresholds, and waivers are governed by separated authorities with an append-only audit log.

---

## Configuration Contract

A gate reads thresholds from a frozen, profile-resolved snapshot whose mandatory floor is identical across profiles.

---

# Interfaces to Downstream Sections

Section 7.1 hands specific responsibilities to the remaining sections of Part 7.

## Interface to Section 7.2

Section 7.2 defines the concrete pipeline-stage gates — Story, Screenplay, Shot, Storyboard, Render, Composition, Narration, Packaging, Publication, and cross-stage — each as an instance of the architecture defined here. Section 7.2 supplies each gate's specific checks and owners; it inherits anatomy, semantics, reporting, lifecycle, governance, and configuration unchanged.

---

## Interface to Section 7.3

Section 7.3 defines quality metrics, scoring, and enforcement. It builds on the advisory-check class (7.1.4), the `threshold_score` verdict function (7.1.5), the scoring configuration (7.1.11), and the report aggregation (7.1.8) established here.

---

## Interface to Section 7.4

Section 7.4 defines human approval and editorial gates. It builds on the `human-approval` judgment type (7.1.6), the waiver and governance model (7.1.10), and the audit log established here.

---

## Interface to Section 7.5

Section 7.5 defines Part 7 acceptance and transition. It aggregates the invariants and guarantees established across 7.1 through 7.4 into the platform's overall quality-gate acceptance criteria.

---

# Traceability Matrix

Each architectural concern traces to the subsection that owns it.

| Concern                     | Owning Subsection |
| --------------------------- | ----------------- |
| Boundary & authority        | 7.1.1             |
| Philosophy & principles     | 7.1.2             |
| Gate anatomy & engine       | 7.1.3             |
| Check model                 | 7.1.4             |
| Verdict & fail-closed       | 7.1.5             |
| Classification              | 7.1.6             |
| Composition & chain         | 7.1.7             |
| Reporting                   | 7.1.8             |
| Lifecycle & recovery        | 7.1.9             |
| Governance & waivers        | 7.1.10            |
| Configuration               | 7.1.11            |
| Decision records            | 7.1.12            |

---

# Quality Gate Architecture Maturity Model

The architecture supports staged adoption.

| Level | Name             | Characteristic                                                        |
| ----- | ---------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| L0    | Ad hoc           | Gates exist per stage with inconsistent semantics.                   |
| L1    | Unified anatomy  | Every gate is an instance of the shared model and one engine.        |
| L2    | Composed chain   | Gates compose as a non-bypassable, attributable chain.               |
| L3    | Governed         | Authoring, enforcing, and waiving are separated and audited.         |
| L4    | Reproducible     | Every verdict is deterministic, configured, and re-runnable.         |

The architecture defined in Section 7.1 targets L4: every gate is unified, composed, governed, and reproducible.

---

# Compliance Checklist

Section 7.1 is compliant when a gate built to it satisfies:

* the canonical gate contract (input, process, output);
* the ten stable architectural invariants;
* the five architectural contracts;
* the fail-closed resolution table (7.1.5);
* the reporting and traceability requirements (7.1.8);
* the governance and configuration constraints (7.1.10, 7.1.11).

---

# Section Completion Statement

Section 7.1 defined the Quality Gate Architecture in full.

Every gate the platform runs — from the Story Gate to the Publication Gate — is an instance of this architecture. The architecture guarantees that "PASS" means the same deterministic, fail-closed, governed thing at every stage boundary, and that every verdict is explainable, reproducible, and attributable.

The architecture is defined. The specific gates remain.

---

# Transition to Section 7.2

Section 7.1 ends where the concrete gates begin.

```text
Section 7.1
Quality Gate Architecture (the reusable model)
        │
        ▼
Section 7.2
Pipeline Stage Quality Gates (instances at each boundary)
```

Section 7.2 consumes this architecture and instantiates it at each pipeline stage. It defines the specific checks, owners, and types of the Story, Screenplay, Shot, Storyboard, Render, Composition, Narration, Packaging, Publication, and cross-stage gates.

Section 7.2 may not redefine gate anatomy, verdict semantics, reporting, lifecycle, governance, or configuration. Those are settled here and inherited there.

Section 7.1 is complete. The pipeline gates begin in Section 7.2.

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant QGS-701

Every gate in the platform satisfies the canonical gate contract defined in 7.1.13.

---

## Invariant QGS-702

Every gate in Part 7.2 is an instance of the architecture defined in Part 7.1 and redefines none of its foundations.

---

## Invariant QGS-703

The ten stable architectural invariants hold for every gate regardless of stage.

---

## Invariant QGS-704

The five architectural contracts — definition, evaluation, verdict, governance, configuration — are inherited unchanged by every gate.

---

## Invariant QGS-705

Every downstream section of Part 7 builds on 7.1 and never contradicts it.

---

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |

| ADR-817 | Part 7.2 instantiates, and never redefines, the Part 7.1 architecture.              |
| ADR-818 | The ten stable invariants hold for every gate at every stage.                       |
| ADR-819 | The five architectural contracts are inherited unchanged by all gates.              |
| ADR-820 | Part 7.1 targets maturity level L4: unified, composed, governed, reproducible.       |

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.1.13** is complete when:

* The Quality Gate Architecture of Section 7.1 is summarized across its subsections.
* The canonical gate contract every gate satisfies is stated.
* The ten stable architectural invariants and five architectural contracts are consolidated.
* Interfaces to Sections 7.2, 7.3, 7.4, and 7.5 are defined.
* A traceability matrix maps each concern to its owning subsection.
* The maturity model and compliance checklist are defined.
* The transition to Section 7.2 is defined, with the prohibition on redefining the architecture.
* Invariants QGS-701 through QGS-705 and ADR-816 through ADR-820 are established.

---

# Section 7.1 Completion Statement

Section **7.1 — Quality Gate Architecture** is complete.

It defines the reusable model, semantics, composition, reporting, lifecycle, governance, and configuration of every Quality Gate in the platform. Sections 7.2 through 7.5 instantiate and extend this architecture; they do not redefine it.

The Quality Gate Architecture is established. The pipeline-stage gates follow in Section 7.2.

---

# 7.2 Pipeline Stage Quality Gates

# Part 7.2.1 — Purpose & Stage Gate Taxonomy

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **taxonomy of pipeline-stage Quality Gates** and the shared template every stage gate obeys.

Section 7.1 defined the gate architecture in the abstract. Section 7.2 instantiates it: it defines the specific gates that guard each boundary of the platform pipeline, from the Story Engine to Publication.

This subsection is the map. It enumerates the stage gates, fixes their order in the chain, defines the template each one follows, and establishes what every stage gate inherits from Section 7.1 and what it supplies itself.

Every gate defined in 7.2.2 through 7.2.11 is an instance of the architecture established in 7.1. This subsection makes the instancing explicit so the individual gates need not repeat it.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **Each pipeline stage is guarded by exactly one stage-exit gate. The gate inherits its entire mechanism from Section 7.1 and supplies only its stage, its checks, and their owners.**

A stage gate is not a new kind of thing. It is the Section 7.1 gate, parameterized for one boundary. It inherits anatomy, verdict semantics, fail-closed reduction, reporting, lifecycle, governance, and configuration unchanged. It contributes only the list of checks appropriate to its stage, the owners of those checks, and its declared type.

This is what keeps the pipeline's gates uniform: they differ in *what* they check, never in *how* they check.

---

# The Pipeline Stage Gates

The platform defines the following stage gates, in chain order.

| # | Gate                              | Stage guarded             | Primary owner    | Section |
| - | --------------------------------- | ------------------------- | ---------------- | ------- |
| 1 | Story Quality Gate                | Story generation          | Part 2           | 7.2.2   |
| 2 | Screenplay Quality Gate           | Screenplay generation     | Part 3           | 7.2.3   |
| 3 | Shot Quality Gate                 | Shot planning             | Part 4           | 7.2.4   |
| 4 | Storyboard Quality Gate           | Storyboard generation     | Part 4           | 7.2.5   |
| 5 | Render Quality Gate               | Render execution          | Part 5           | 7.2.6   |
| 6 | Composition Quality Gate          | Composition               | Part 5 / Part 6  | 7.2.7   |
| 7 | Narration & Audio Quality Gate    | Narration & audio         | Part 3 / Part 5  | 7.2.8   |
| 8 | Metadata & Packaging Quality Gate | Packaging                 | Part 6           | 7.2.9   |
| 9 | Publication Quality Gate          | Publication               | Part 6 / Part 7.4| 7.2.10  |
| — | Cross-Stage Coherence Gate        | Inter-stage fidelity      | Part 7           | 7.2.11  |

The first nine are stage-exit gates on the linear pipeline. The Cross-Stage Coherence Gate (7.2.11) is a family of cross-stage gates that verify a transformation preserved meaning across a boundary.

---

# The Stage Gate Chain

The stage gates compose into the canonical chain defined in 7.1.7.

```text
Story ─► Screenplay ─► Shot ─► Storyboard ─► Render ─► Composition ─► Narration/Audio ─► Packaging ─► Publication
   │          │          │         │            │           │               │               │            │
  SQG        SCG        SHG       SBG          RQG         CQG             NQG             MQG          PQG
```

Each gate runs at its stage's exit, before the artifact may advance. A FAIL halts the chain at that gate (7.1.7). Cross-stage coherence gates (7.2.11) run at the boundaries where a transformation must be verified — most importantly, that rendered assets match the approved storyboard.

---

# The Stage Gate Template

Every stage gate in 7.2 is specified using one template.

```text
Stage Gate Specification
  ├── Stage Boundary      (which stage, which input artifact, which output)
  ├── Gate Type           (the 7.1.6 four-axis tuple)
  ├── Mandatory Checks     (id, owner, class = mandatory)
  ├── Advisory Checks      (id, owner, class = advisory)
  ├── Verdict Function     (a 7.1.5 registered function)
  ├── Upstream Dependencies(the 7.1.7 verdicts it consumes)
  └── Gate Report          (a 7.1.8 standard report)
```

A stage gate specification is complete when every field of the template is populated. The template guarantees that any two stage gates are directly comparable and that each is a valid instance of Section 7.1.

---

# What a Stage Gate Inherits

Every stage gate inherits the following from Section 7.1, unchanged.

| Inherited                     | From    |
| ----------------------------- | ------- |
| Gate anatomy and engine       | 7.1.3   |
| Check model and evidence      | 7.1.4   |
| Verdict semantics, fail-closed| 7.1.5   |
| Type classification           | 7.1.6   |
| Chain composition             | 7.1.7   |
| Report shape                  | 7.1.8   |
| Lifecycle and recovery        | 7.1.9   |
| Governance and waivers        | 7.1.10  |
| Configuration and profiles    | 7.1.11  |

A stage gate never redefines any inherited property. If a gate appears to need different verdict semantics or a different report shape, that is a signal to extend Section 7.1, not to special-case the gate.

---

# What a Stage Gate Supplies

Every stage gate supplies only the following.

* its **stage** and the artifact it guards;
* its **mandatory checks**, each with an owner;
* its **advisory checks**, each with an owner;
* its declared **type** (the four-axis tuple);
* its **upstream verdict dependencies**;
* the thresholds it reads, declared in configuration (7.1.11).

Everything else is inherited. This is the whole of a stage gate's originality: a stage, a check list, a type, and its dependencies.

---

# Stage Gate Ownership

Each stage gate's checks are owned by the sections that define the stage's rules.

```text
Story Quality Gate checks     → owned by Part 2 (Story Engine)
Screenplay Quality Gate checks→ owned by Part 3 (Screenplay Engine)
Shot Quality Gate checks      → owned by Part 4 (Shot Planner)
Storyboard Quality Gate checks→ owned by Part 4 (Storyboard Engine)
Render Quality Gate checks    → owned by Part 5 (Rendering Platform)
...
```

A stage gate enforces rules owned by the stage it guards. It never authors a rule (Principle 3). This is why the Story Gate's checks are owned by Part 2 and the Render Gate's checks by Part 5: the gate is the enforcement point; the stage's defining Part is the source of truth.

The Shot Quality Gate (7.2.4) and Storyboard Quality Gate (7.2.5) are the canonical worked examples, because Part 4.1.12 already defined their checks; Section 7.2 re-expresses them as instances of the 7.1 architecture without changing a single check.

---

# Element vs Sequence Stage Gates

Stage gates differ in scope (7.1.6).

| Gate                    | Scope     | Reason                                             |
| ----------------------- | --------- | -------------------------------------------------- |
| Shot Quality Gate       | element   | validates one shot                                 |
| Storyboard Quality Gate | sequence  | validates the ordered set of shots                 |
| Render Quality Gate     | element   | validates one rendered asset                       |
| Composition Quality Gate| sequence  | validates the assembled timeline                   |
| Publication Quality Gate| sequence  | validates the complete publishable package         |

Element gates run per unit; sequence gates run once the units have each passed (7.1.7). A stage may have both: shots pass the element Shot Gate individually before the sequence Storyboard Gate evaluates their composition.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-791 — The Bespoke Stage Gate

Wrong:

```text
Render Gate invents its own verdict semantics and report format
```

Correct:

```text
Render Gate inherits 7.1 semantics and report; supplies only its checks
```

---

## AP-792 — The Ungated Stage

Wrong:

```text
Composition advances to Packaging with no gate between them
```

Correct:

```text
Every stage boundary has exactly one stage-exit gate
```

---

## AP-793 — Cross-Stage Logic in a Stage Gate

Wrong:

```text
Render Gate re-validates the storyboard sequence
```

Correct:

```text
Storyboard validity is settled by the Storyboard Gate; render↔storyboard fidelity is a cross-stage gate (7.2.11)
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant SGT-701

Every pipeline stage is guarded by exactly one stage-exit Quality Gate.

---

## Invariant SGT-702

Every stage gate is an instance of the Section 7.1 architecture and redefines none of it.

---

## Invariant SGT-703

A stage gate supplies only its stage, checks, owners, type, and dependencies.

---

## Invariant SGT-704

Every stage gate check is owned by the section that defines the stage's rules.

---

## Invariant SGT-705

Stage gates compose into the canonical chain defined in 7.1.7.

---

## Invariant SGT-706

A stage gate's scope (element or sequence) is declared and determines its ordering within the stage.

---

## Invariant SGT-707

Cross-stage fidelity is enforced by cross-stage gates (7.2.11), never by a single-stage gate.

---

## Invariant SGT-708

Every stage gate is specified by the complete stage gate template.

---

## Invariant SGT-709

No stage boundary is left ungated.

---

## Invariant SGT-710

A stage gate that appears to need new mechanism extends Section 7.1 rather than special-casing itself.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-821 | Each pipeline stage is guarded by exactly one stage-exit gate.                       |
| ADR-822 | Every stage gate is an instance of the Section 7.1 architecture.                    |
| ADR-823 | A stage gate supplies only its stage, checks, owners, type, and dependencies.        |
| ADR-824 | Stage gate checks are owned by the sections defining the stage's rules.              |
| ADR-825 | Stage gates compose into the canonical Story-to-Publication chain.                   |
| ADR-826 | Stage gates declare element or sequence scope, ordering the intra-stage evaluation.  |
| ADR-827 | Cross-stage fidelity is enforced by dedicated cross-stage gates.                     |
| ADR-828 | Every stage gate is specified via the shared stage gate template.                   |
| ADR-829 | No stage boundary is left ungated.                                                   |
| ADR-830 | New mechanism extends Section 7.1; stage gates are never special-cased.              |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.1** is complete when:

* The full set of pipeline stage gates is enumerated in chain order with owners.
* The stage gate chain is defined and tied to 7.1.7.
* The shared stage gate template is defined.
* What every stage gate inherits from 7.1 and supplies itself is made explicit.
* Stage gate ownership is established, with Shot and Storyboard gates as canonical worked examples.
* Element versus sequence scope is defined for stage gates.
* Anti-patterns for bespoke gates, ungated stages, and misplaced cross-stage logic are documented.
* Invariants SGT-701 through SGT-710 and ADR-821 through ADR-830 are established.

---

# Part 7.2.2 — Story Quality Gate

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Story Quality Gate**: the checkpoint that stands between the Story Engine (Part 2) and the Screenplay Engine (Part 3).

The Story Quality Gate answers exactly one question:

> **"Is this story a sound dramatic foundation, or must it be rejected before a screenplay is written on it?"**

The Story Engine converts an insight article into a dramatic structure — a premise, a protagonist, stakes, a three-act shape, and an emotional arc. The Story Quality Gate confirms that this structure is complete and coherent before any downstream stage builds on it.

A defect admitted here propagates into the screenplay, the shots, the storyboard, and the render — at rising cost (7.1.2). The Story Gate is the earliest and cheapest place to catch a structural story defect, and it is therefore the first gate in the chain.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A story is admissible only when its dramatic foundation is complete: a defined premise, a defined protagonist, defined stakes, a valid three-act structure, and a coherent emotional arc. Missing or incoherent foundation is rejected, never inferred downstream.**

The Story Gate enforces the boundary the whole pipeline depends on: story meaning is settled here, and no downstream stage may reopen it (as established in Part 4.1.1). For that boundary to hold, the story must be *sound* when it passes. The gate is what makes soundness a precondition rather than a hope.

---

# The Stage Boundary

```text
Insight Article
        │
        ▼
Story Engine (Part 2)  ──► story.json (premise, protagonist, stakes, acts, arc)
        │
        ▼
Story Quality Gate  ◄── this section
        │  PASS
        ▼
Screenplay Engine (Part 3)
```

* **Input artifact:** the story structure emitted by the Story Engine.
* **Output on PASS:** the same artifact, admitted to screenplay generation.
* **Owner of checks:** Part 2 — Story Engine.

---

# Gate Type

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    element        # one story structure
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: semantic       # dramatic coherence, not mere schema
```

The Story Gate is an element, stage-exit, blocking, semantic gate. It evaluates one story structure at the exit of the Story stage, blocks on failure, and judges dramatic coherence — a semantic property — in addition to structural completeness.

---

# Mandatory Checks

The Story Gate performs the following mandatory checks. Each is owned by Part 2.

| Check                         | Owner  | Enforces                                                        |
| ----------------------------- | ------ | -------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `premise_defined`             | Part 2 | A non-empty dramatic premise is present.                       |
| `protagonist_defined`         | Part 2 | A single protagonist is identified.                            |
| `stakes_defined`              | Part 2 | The stakes of the story are explicit.                          |
| `three_act_structure_valid`   | Part 2 | The story declares a valid three-act structure.                |
| `emotional_arc_coherent`      | Part 2 | The emotional arc progresses coherently across the acts.       |
| `single_dramatic_question`    | Part 2 | The story poses exactly one central dramatic question.         |
| `human_grounded`              | Part 2 | The story is grounded in a human experience, not an abstraction.|
| `article_traceable`           | Part 2 | Every dramatic element traces to the source insight article.   |

Each mandatory check must return PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE for the gate to pass. A single mandatory FAIL fails the gate (7.1.5).

---

# Mandatory Check Detail

## premise_defined

The story declares a non-empty dramatic premise.

Evidence records the premise text; an empty or absent premise is a FAIL. A story with no premise has no dramatic reason to exist and cannot be built upon.

---

## protagonist_defined

The story identifies exactly one protagonist.

Evidence records the protagonist identity. Zero protagonists fails; multiple competing protagonists fails, because the downstream pipeline (shots, continuity) assumes a single focal human.

---

## stakes_defined

The story declares explicit stakes — what is at risk.

A story without stakes has no tension, and the emotional arc cannot be validated against it. Absent stakes are a FAIL.

---

## three_act_structure_valid

The story declares a valid three-act structure with a beginning, middle, and resolution.

This underpins the act-based constraints downstream, including the concept-scene restriction to Act 3 (Part 4.1.11). A malformed or missing act structure fails.

---

## emotional_arc_coherent

The emotional arc progresses coherently across the three acts.

Evidence records the arc's beat-to-beat progression. An arc that is flat, contradictory, or discontinuous fails. This is a semantic check: it evaluates the *relationship* between beats, not a single field.

---

## single_dramatic_question

The story poses exactly one central dramatic question.

Multiple competing dramatic questions fracture the trailer's focus. Evidence records the identified question; zero or multiple questions fail.

---

## human_grounded

The story is grounded in a human experience rather than an abstract thesis.

This enforces, at the story level, the platform's cinematic discipline that ideas are felt through a human before they are named (Part 4.1.11). A story that is purely conceptual fails.

---

## article_traceable

Every dramatic element traces to the source insight article.

The Story Engine dramatizes an article; it does not invent facts. A dramatic element with no traceable origin in the article fails, guarding against fabrication.

---

# Advisory Checks

The Story Gate performs the following advisory checks. An advisory FAIL is recorded but does not block (7.1.4).

| Check                     | Owner  | Signals                                             |
| ------------------------- | ------ | -------------------------------------------------- |
| `premise_distinctiveness` | Part 2 | The premise is distinctive rather than generic.    |
| `stakes_escalation`       | Part 2 | The stakes escalate across the acts.               |
| `arc_intensity`           | Part 2 | The emotional arc reaches sufficient intensity.    |

Advisory results contribute to the story quality score (7.3) and appear in the report's `advisory_failures`, but never flip the verdict.

---

# Verdict Function

```yaml
verdict_function: all_mandatory_pass
```

The Story Gate uses `all_mandatory_pass` (7.1.5): it passes if and only if every mandatory check is PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE. Advisory checks are recorded but excluded from the verdict.

---

# Upstream Verdict Dependencies

The Story Gate is the first gate in the chain. It has no upstream gate dependencies.

```yaml
upstream_verdicts: []
```

It depends only on the Story Engine having emitted a story artifact. Its verdict becomes the upstream dependency of the Screenplay Gate (7.2.3).

---

# The Gate Report

```json
{
  "gate_id": "story_quality_gate",
  "gate_version": "2.0",
  "stage": "story_generation",
  "artifact_identity": "sha256:...",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "blocking": true,
  "verdict_function": "all_mandatory_pass",
  "failed_checks": ["stakes_defined"],
  "owning_sections": { "stakes_defined": "Part 2" },
  "advisory_failures": [
    { "check_id": "premise_distinctiveness", "owner": "Part 2", "message": "premise reads as generic" }
  ]
}
```

The report names the failing mandatory check and routes it to Part 2 for correction. On correction, the story's identity changes and the gate re-runs (7.1.9), and the chain resumes at the Story Gate (7.1.7).

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-801 — Inferring a Missing Stake

Wrong:

```text
stakes absent → gate infers a plausible stake → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
stakes absent → stakes_defined FAIL → return to Story Engine
```

---

## AP-802 — Passing Multiple Protagonists

Wrong:

```text
two protagonists → gate picks one → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
two protagonists → protagonist_defined FAIL → single protagonist required
```

---

## AP-803 — Advisory Treated as Blocking

Wrong:

```text
premise_distinctiveness FAIL → gate blocks
```

Correct:

```text
premise_distinctiveness is advisory → recorded, non-blocking
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant SQG-701

The Story Quality Gate guards the boundary between the Story Engine and the Screenplay Engine.

---

## Invariant SQG-702

The gate passes only when premise, protagonist, stakes, three-act structure, and emotional arc are all present and coherent.

---

## Invariant SQG-703

Every Story Gate check is owned by Part 2 and enforces a rule the gate does not author.

---

## Invariant SQG-704

Missing story foundation is rejected, never inferred downstream.

---

## Invariant SQG-705

The gate enforces exactly one protagonist and exactly one central dramatic question.

---

## Invariant SQG-706

The gate enforces that every dramatic element traces to the source article.

---

## Invariant SQG-707

Advisory checks contribute to scoring but never flip the verdict.

---

## Invariant SQG-708

The gate is element-scope, stage-exit, blocking, and semantic.

---

## Invariant SQG-709

The Story Gate has no upstream verdict dependency and is the chain head.

---

## Invariant SQG-710

A Story Gate PASS is the upstream dependency consumed by the Screenplay Gate.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-831 | The Story Quality Gate guards the Story→Screenplay boundary.                         |
| ADR-832 | A story passes only with a complete, coherent dramatic foundation.                   |
| ADR-833 | Story Gate checks are owned by Part 2 and authored by the gate none.                 |
| ADR-834 | Missing story foundation is rejected, never inferred.                                |
| ADR-835 | The gate enforces a single protagonist and a single dramatic question.               |
| ADR-836 | The gate enforces article traceability, guarding against fabrication.                |
| ADR-837 | Advisory story checks inform scoring but never block.                                |
| ADR-838 | The Story Gate is element, stage-exit, blocking, semantic.                           |
| ADR-839 | The Story Gate is the chain head with no upstream dependency.                        |
| ADR-840 | A Story Gate PASS is consumed as an upstream dependency by the Screenplay Gate.       |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.2** is complete when:

* The Story Quality Gate is defined as the Story→Screenplay boundary gate.
* Its stage boundary, input artifact, and output are explicit.
* Its four-axis type is declared.
* Its mandatory checks are enumerated with owners in Part 2 and detailed.
* Its advisory checks are enumerated and shown to be non-blocking.
* Its verdict function and empty upstream dependency are defined.
* A representative gate report is provided.
* Anti-patterns for inference, multiple protagonists, and advisory-as-blocking are documented.
* Invariants SQG-701 through SQG-710 and ADR-831 through ADR-840 are established.

---

# Part 7.2.3 — Screenplay Quality Gate

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Screenplay Quality Gate**: the checkpoint between the Screenplay Engine (Part 3) and the Shot Planner (Part 4).

The Screenplay Quality Gate answers exactly one question:

> **"Is this screenplay a sound, scene-by-scene realization of the approved story, or must it be rejected before shot planning begins?"**

The Screenplay Engine converts the approved story into scenes — each with a purpose, dialogue, emotional progression, and narration timing. The Screenplay Gate confirms that these scenes faithfully realize the story and are well-formed enough to decompose into shots.

The gate guards a critical boundary: the Shot Planner consumes only screenplay artifacts and must never re-read the article or reopen story meaning (Part 4.1.1). For that boundary to be safe, the screenplay must be sound when it passes.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A screenplay is admissible only when every scene has a defined purpose, dialogue is well-formed, emotional progression is coherent, and the whole faithfully realizes the approved story without reopening it. Deviation from the approved story is rejected.**

The Screenplay Gate enforces fidelity to the story above it and well-formedness for the shots below it. It is the point at which "the screenplay realizes the story" becomes a checked fact rather than an assumption.

---

# The Stage Boundary

```text
Approved Story (passed Story Gate)
        │
        ▼
Screenplay Engine (Part 3)  ──► screenplay.json + screenplay.fountain
        │
        ▼
Screenplay Quality Gate  ◄── this section
        │  PASS
        ▼
Shot Planner (Part 4)
```

* **Input artifact:** the screenplay emitted by the Screenplay Engine.
* **Output on PASS:** the screenplay, admitted to shot planning.
* **Owner of checks:** Part 3 — Screenplay Engine.

---

# Gate Type

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    sequence       # the ordered set of scenes
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: semantic
```

The Screenplay Gate is a sequence, stage-exit, blocking, semantic gate. It validates the ordered set of scenes as a whole — a screenplay is more than its scenes individually, because progression across scenes carries meaning.

---

# Mandatory Checks

| Check                          | Owner  | Enforces                                                       |
| ------------------------------ | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `every_scene_has_purpose`      | Part 3 | Every scene declares an explicit scene purpose.               |
| `dialogue_well_formed`         | Part 3 | Dialogue is present and well-formed where required.           |
| `emotional_progression_coherent`| Part 3| Emotional progression across scenes is coherent.              |
| `narration_timing_valid`       | Part 3 | Narration timing is defined and consistent.                   |
| `scene_order_valid`            | Part 3 | Scenes are ordered consistently with the story structure.     |
| `story_fidelity`               | Part 3 | The screenplay realizes the approved story without reopening it.|
| `act_assignment_valid`         | Part 3 | Every scene is assigned to a valid act.                       |
| `no_article_leakage`           | Part 3 | The screenplay adds no detail absent from the approved story. |

---

# Mandatory Check Detail

## every_scene_has_purpose

Every scene declares an explicit, non-empty purpose.

A purposeless scene cannot be decomposed into purposeful shots (Part 4.1.3). Evidence records each scene's purpose; any scene with an empty purpose fails.

---

## dialogue_well_formed

Dialogue, where present, is well-formed and attributed.

The Shot Planner separates performance from dialogue and never rewrites it (Part 4.1.5). Malformed or unattributed dialogue fails here so the Shot Planner receives clean input.

---

## emotional_progression_coherent

The emotional progression across scenes is coherent and consistent with the story's emotional arc.

This is a sequence-level semantic check: it evaluates the arc across scenes, not within one scene. A progression that contradicts the approved arc fails.

---

## narration_timing_valid

Narration timing is defined and internally consistent.

Narration timing feeds pacing downstream. Undefined or contradictory timing fails.

---

## scene_order_valid

Scenes are ordered consistently with the story's three-act structure and forward time.

An ordering that violates the act structure or implies backward time (anticipating Part 4.1.8) fails.

---

## story_fidelity

The screenplay realizes the approved story and reopens none of its settled decisions.

Evidence records the mapping from scenes to story beats. A screenplay that changes the premise, protagonist, stakes, or arc fails — story meaning is immutable upstream intent.

---

## act_assignment_valid

Every scene is assigned to exactly one valid act.

Act assignment governs downstream act-based constraints. A scene with no act, or an invalid act, fails.

---

## no_article_leakage

The screenplay introduces no detail that is absent from the approved story.

The Screenplay Engine dramatizes the story, not the article. New facts with no basis in the approved story fail, preserving the traceability chain from article to story to screenplay.

---

# Advisory Checks

| Check                     | Owner  | Signals                                             |
| ------------------------- | ------ | -------------------------------------------------- |
| `dialogue_economy`        | Part 3 | Dialogue is economical rather than over-written.   |
| `scene_length_balance`    | Part 3 | Scene lengths are balanced across the acts.        |
| `narration_restraint`     | Part 3 | Narration supports rather than replaces the visual.|

---

# Verdict Function

```yaml
verdict_function: all_mandatory_pass
```

The gate passes only when every mandatory check is PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE.

---

# Upstream Verdict Dependencies

```yaml
upstream_verdicts:
  - story_quality_gate: PASS
```

The Screenplay Gate depends on the Story Gate PASS (7.1.7). A `story_fidelity` check references the approved story identity; if the upstream Story verdict is absent or not PASS, the dependent checks fail closed (7.1.7). The Screenplay Gate never re-derives story validity; it trusts the recorded Story verdict.

---

# The Gate Report

```json
{
  "gate_id": "screenplay_quality_gate",
  "stage": "screenplay_generation",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "failed_checks": ["story_fidelity"],
  "owning_sections": { "story_fidelity": "Part 3" },
  "upstream_verdicts": { "story_quality_gate": "PASS" }
}
```

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-811 — Reopening the Story

Wrong:

```text
Screenplay changes the protagonist → gate passes it as "improved"
```

Correct:

```text
story_fidelity FAIL → the story is immutable upstream intent
```

---

## AP-812 — Purposeless Scene

Wrong:

```text
scene with empty purpose → gate passes
```

Correct:

```text
every_scene_has_purpose FAIL → return to Screenplay Engine
```

---

## AP-813 — Re-Deriving Story Validity

Wrong:

```text
Screenplay Gate re-checks the story's dramatic arc from scratch
```

Correct:

```text
Screenplay Gate references the Story Gate PASS; it never re-derives it
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant SCG-701

The Screenplay Quality Gate guards the boundary between the Screenplay Engine and the Shot Planner.

---

## Invariant SCG-702

The gate passes only when every scene has a purpose, dialogue is well-formed, and progression is coherent.

---

## Invariant SCG-703

Every Screenplay Gate check is owned by Part 3.

---

## Invariant SCG-704

The gate enforces fidelity to the approved story and rejects any reopening of story meaning.

---

## Invariant SCG-705

The gate enforces no article leakage, preserving the article→story→screenplay trace.

---

## Invariant SCG-706

The gate is sequence-scope, evaluating the ordered scenes as a whole.

---

## Invariant SCG-707

The gate depends on the Story Gate PASS and never re-derives story validity.

---

## Invariant SCG-708

Advisory checks inform scoring but never block.

---

## Invariant SCG-709

A dependent check referencing an absent or non-PASS Story verdict fails closed.

---

## Invariant SCG-710

A Screenplay Gate PASS is the upstream dependency consumed by the Shot Gate.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-841 | The Screenplay Quality Gate guards the Screenplay→Shot boundary.                     |
| ADR-842 | A screenplay passes only with purposeful scenes, well-formed dialogue, and coherent progression. |
| ADR-843 | Screenplay Gate checks are owned by Part 3.                                          |
| ADR-844 | The gate enforces fidelity to the approved story and rejects reopening it.           |
| ADR-845 | The gate enforces no article leakage.                                                |
| ADR-846 | The gate is sequence-scope over the ordered scenes.                                  |
| ADR-847 | The gate depends on the Story Gate PASS and never re-derives story validity.         |
| ADR-848 | Advisory screenplay checks inform scoring but never block.                           |
| ADR-849 | A dependent check on an absent Story verdict fails closed.                           |
| ADR-850 | A Screenplay Gate PASS is consumed as an upstream dependency by the Shot Gate.        |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.3** is complete when:

* The Screenplay Quality Gate is defined as the Screenplay→Shot boundary gate.
* Its stage boundary, artifact, and output are explicit.
* Its sequence-scope, stage-exit, blocking, semantic type is declared.
* Its mandatory checks are enumerated with owners in Part 3 and detailed.
* Its advisory checks are enumerated and shown non-blocking.
* Its dependency on the Story Gate PASS and fail-closed handling of an absent verdict are defined.
* A representative report is provided.
* Anti-patterns for reopening the story, purposeless scenes, and re-derivation are documented.
* Invariants SCG-701 through SCG-710 and ADR-841 through ADR-850 are established.

---

# Part 7.2.4 — Shot Quality Gate

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Shot Quality Gate** as an instance of the Section 7.1 architecture.

The Shot Quality Gate was first specified in Part 4.1.12 as the per-shot pass/fail checkpoint of the visual planning control plane. This section re-expresses it as an instance of the unified gate architecture, without changing a single check.

The Shot Quality Gate is the canonical worked example of the architecture. Its eight boolean checks, its logical-AND verdict, and its fail-closed discipline were the model from which Section 7.1 was generalized. Here the relationship is closed: the gate defined in Part 4 is shown to be exactly the gate the architecture describes.

> **This section changes nothing about the Shot Quality Gate's behavior. It re-expresses it in the vocabulary of Section 7.1.**

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the principle established in Part 4.1.12.

> **A shot that cannot describe itself cannot be rendered. Every shot passes all eight mandatory checks, combined by logical AND, or it is rejected.**

The eight checks, their owners, and their fail-closed combination are unchanged. What Section 7.2.4 adds is the mapping of that behavior onto the architecture's anatomy, verdict function, and report.

---

# The Stage Boundary

```text
Approved Screenplay (passed Screenplay Gate)
        │
        ▼
Shot Planner (Part 4)  ──► shot-list.json
        │
        ▼
Shot Quality Gate  ◄── this section (== Part 4.1.12 Shot Quality Gate)
        │  PASS (per shot)
        ▼
Storyboard assembly
```

* **Input artifact:** one shot from `shot-list.json`.
* **Output on PASS:** the shot, eligible to enter the storyboard sequence.
* **Owner of checks:** Part 4 (subsections 4.1.2–4.1.9).

---

# Gate Type

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    element        # one shot
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: structural     # eight boolean well-formedness checks
```

The Shot Gate is an element, stage-exit, blocking, structural gate. It runs per shot; every shot must individually pass before the sequence-scope Storyboard Gate (7.2.5) evaluates their composition — exactly the ordering established in Part 4.1.12 and generalized in 7.1.7.

---

# Mandatory Checks

The Shot Gate performs the **eight** mandatory boolean checks defined in Part 4.1.12, unchanged.

| Check                     | Owner         | Enforces                                               |
| ------------------------- | ------------- | ----------------------------------------------------- |
| `purpose_exists`          | 4.1.3         | The shot has an explicit cinematic purpose (P-404).   |
| `camera_defined`          | 4.1.4         | Lens, angle, movement, and speed are defined.         |
| `blocking_defined`        | 4.1.5         | Observable character movement is described.           |
| `emotion_defined`         | 4.1.5         | Emotional transition, eye focus, breathing defined.   |
| `continuity_valid`        | 4.1.7 / 4.1.8 | Bible references resolve; time does not move backward. |
| `render_strategy_defined` | 4.1.9         | Exactly one render strategy is assigned (P-407).      |
| `single_action`           | 4.1.2 / 4.1.3 | Exactly one primary dramatic action (P-402).          |
| `single_camera_move`      | 4.1.4         | At most one camera movement (P-403).                  |

All eight are mandatory. Each must be PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE. One FAIL fails the shot.

---

# The Eight Booleans as Checks

Part 4.1.12 expressed the gate as eight booleans that must all be `true`.

```yaml
purpose_exists: true
camera_defined: true
blocking_defined: true
emotion_defined: true
continuity_valid: true
render_strategy_defined: true
single_action: true
single_camera_move: true
```

In the Section 7.1 vocabulary, each boolean is a mandatory check whose PASS corresponds to `true` and whose FAIL corresponds to `false`. The requirement that all eight be `true` is the `all_mandatory_pass` verdict function (7.1.5) — a logical AND across the eight mandatory checks.

The mapping is exact:

```text
Part 4.1.12:  all eight booleans == true
Section 7.1:  all_mandatory_pass over eight mandatory checks
```

There is no weighting, no scoring, and no threshold below eight — precisely as Part 4.1.12 stated.

---

# NOT_APPLICABLE for Non-Performance Shots

Some checks are `NOT_APPLICABLE` to some shots, and this is preserved from the check model (7.1.4).

A `title_card` shot has no character performance, so `emotion_defined` and `blocking_defined` may be `NOT_APPLICABLE` — the rule does not apply. Under `all_mandatory_pass`, a mandatory check that is `NOT_APPLICABLE` is acceptable and does not fail the gate. It is never silently treated as PASS; the report records `NOT_APPLICABLE` with justification (7.1.4).

This refines Part 4.1.12 with the architecture's three-valued check result, without weakening the eight-check requirement for shots to which the checks apply.

---

# Advisory Checks

| Check                  | Owner  | Signals                                          |
| ---------------------- | ------ | ------------------------------------------------ |
| `duration_in_range`    | 4.1.2  | The shot duration sits in the typical range.     |
| `purpose_type_fit`     | 4.1.3  | The shot type fits its declared purpose.         |

Advisory results inform the shot quality score (7.3) and appear in `advisory_failures`; they never flip the eight-check verdict.

---

# Verdict Function

```yaml
verdict_function: all_mandatory_pass
```

The Shot Gate uses `all_mandatory_pass` — the logical AND of Part 4.1.12 (ADR-622). A single mandatory `false`/FAIL fails the shot.

---

# Upstream Verdict Dependencies

```yaml
upstream_verdicts:
  - screenplay_quality_gate: PASS
```

The Shot Gate depends on the Screenplay Gate PASS. It never re-derives screenplay validity; it decomposes an approved screenplay (Part 4.1.1) and trusts the recorded Screenplay verdict.

---

# The Gate Report

The Shot Gate emits the standard report (7.1.8), equivalent to the `shot_gate_report` of Part 4.1.12.

```json
{
  "gate_id": "shot_quality_gate",
  "stage": "shot_planning",
  "artifact_identity": "sha256:shot-014-03...",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "failed_checks": ["emotion_defined"],
  "owning_sections": { "emotion_defined": "4.1.5" },
  "blocking": true
}
```

This is the Part 4.1.12 shot gate report expressed in the standard report shape. The failure routes to 4.1.5 for correction; the build is blocked (P-409).

---

# Failure Blocks the Build

The Shot Gate inherits the Part 4.1.12 rule, now a chain property (7.1.7).

> **Failure blocks rendering for the entire build; there is no partial rendering of passing shots.**

Nine of ten shots passing does not admit the nine. The build is blocked until all shots pass, exactly as Part 4.1.12 established and 7.1.5 generalized (no partial credit).

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-821 — Defaulting a Missing Value

Wrong:

```text
emotion_defined missing → substitute neutral default → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
emotion_defined missing → FAIL (fail-closed)
```

---

## AP-822 — Rendering the Shots That Passed

Wrong:

```text
9 of 10 shots pass → render the 9
```

Correct:

```text
build blocked until all 10 pass
```

---

## AP-823 — Re-Weighting the Eight

Wrong:

```text
seven of eight pass → "good enough" → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
all eight required; no threshold below eight
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant SHG-701

The Shot Quality Gate is the Part 4.1.12 gate expressed as an instance of Section 7.1, with unchanged behavior.

---

## Invariant SHG-702

The gate performs exactly the eight mandatory checks defined in Part 4.1.12.

---

## Invariant SHG-703

The eight checks are combined by `all_mandatory_pass` — a logical AND — with no threshold below eight.

---

## Invariant SHG-704

A mandatory check that is NOT_APPLICABLE is acceptable and never silently treated as PASS.

---

## Invariant SHG-705

Each check is owned by its Part 4 subsection, as tabulated in Part 4.1.12.

---

## Invariant SHG-706

The gate is element-scope and precedes the sequence-scope Storyboard Gate.

---

## Invariant SHG-707

The gate depends on the Screenplay Gate PASS and never re-derives screenplay validity.

---

## Invariant SHG-708

A single mandatory FAIL blocks the entire build; there is no partial rendering.

---

## Invariant SHG-709

Advisory shot checks inform scoring but never flip the eight-check verdict.

---

## Invariant SHG-710

The gate enforces Invariant P-409: no shot bypasses the gate before rendering.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-851 | The Shot Quality Gate is the Part 4.1.12 gate re-expressed as a Section 7.1 instance. |
| ADR-852 | The eight mandatory checks of Part 4.1.12 are preserved unchanged.                    |
| ADR-853 | The eight checks combine by `all_mandatory_pass`; no threshold below eight.           |
| ADR-854 | NOT_APPLICABLE refines the eight booleans without weakening them.                    |
| ADR-855 | Each check retains its Part 4 owning subsection.                                     |
| ADR-856 | The element Shot Gate precedes the sequence Storyboard Gate.                          |
| ADR-857 | The gate depends on the Screenplay Gate PASS.                                        |
| ADR-858 | A single FAIL blocks the whole build; no partial rendering.                          |
| ADR-859 | Advisory shot checks inform scoring but never block.                                 |
| ADR-860 | The gate enforces P-409; no shot reaches rendering unvalidated.                       |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.4** is complete when:

* The Shot Quality Gate is shown to be the Part 4.1.12 gate expressed as a Section 7.1 instance, unchanged in behavior.
* The eight mandatory checks are enumerated with their Part 4 owners.
* The mapping from the eight booleans to `all_mandatory_pass` is made exact.
* NOT_APPLICABLE handling for non-performance shots is defined without weakening the eight-check requirement.
* Advisory checks are enumerated and shown non-blocking.
* The dependency on the Screenplay Gate PASS is defined.
* The no-partial-rendering rule is preserved from Part 4.1.12.
* Anti-patterns for defaulting, partial rendering, and re-weighting are documented.
* Invariants SHG-701 through SHG-710 and ADR-851 through ADR-860 are established.

---

# Part 7.2.5 — Storyboard Quality Gate

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Storyboard Quality Gate** as an instance of the Section 7.1 architecture.

The Storyboard Quality Gate was first specified in Part 4.1.12 as the whole-sequence pass/fail checkpoint that runs after every shot has individually passed the Shot Gate. This section re-expresses it as a sequence-scope instance of the unified architecture, without changing its six checks.

Where the Shot Gate validates one shot, the Storyboard Gate validates the assembled sequence. A collection of individually valid shots can still fail as a sequence, and catching that failure mode is the Storyboard Gate's reason to exist.

> **This section changes nothing about the Storyboard Quality Gate's behavior. It re-expresses it in the vocabulary of Section 7.1.**

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the principle established in Part 4.1.12.

> **Individually valid shots can still fail as a sequence. The Storyboard Gate validates composition, continuity, pacing, render balance, concept ratio, and emotional rhythm across the whole sequence.**

The six checks and their owners are unchanged. Section 7.2.5 maps them onto the architecture's sequence scope and verdict function.

---

# The Stage Boundary

```text
Shots (each passed Shot Gate)
        │
        ▼
Storyboard Engine (Part 4)  ──► storyboard.json
        │
        ▼
Storyboard Quality Gate  ◄── this section (== Part 4.1.12 Storyboard Quality Gate)
        │  PASS
        ▼
Render execution (Part 5)
```

* **Input artifact:** the assembled storyboard sequence.
* **Output on PASS:** the storyboard, admitted to render execution.
* **Owner of checks:** Part 4 (subsections 4.1.6, 4.1.7, 4.1.8, 4.1.10, 4.1.11).

---

# Gate Type

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    sequence       # the ordered set of shots
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: semantic       # cross-shot coherence
```

The Storyboard Gate is a sequence, stage-exit, blocking, semantic gate. It runs once per storyboard, only after every shot has individually passed the element Shot Gate (7.1.7). A storyboard containing even one failing shot never reaches this gate — exactly as Part 4.1.12 established.

---

# Mandatory Checks

The Storyboard Gate performs the **six** mandatory checks defined in Part 4.1.12, unchanged.

| Check              | Owner  | Enforces                                                         |
| ------------------ | ------ | --------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `composition`      | 4.1.6  | Coherent composition, lighting, palette, focal subject, depth.  |
| `continuity`       | 4.1.7 / 4.1.8 | Character, location, and time continuity across the whole sequence. |
| `pacing`           | 4.1.6  | Shot durations and cut rhythm form a deliberate cadence.        |
| `render balance`   | 4.1.10 | The render-strategy mix respects the hybrid-rendering ratios (P-408). |
| `concept ratio`    | 4.1.11 | Concept-shot proportion stays within the configured restriction. |
| `emotional rhythm` | 4.1.6  | Emotional progression forms an intentional arc.                 |

All six are mandatory and sequence-level. Each must be PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE.

---

# Sequence-Level Semantics

The six checks are sequence-level, not shot-level, and this is the crux of the gate.

```text
Shot Gate:       validates each shot in isolation
Storyboard Gate: validates the shots' composition as a sequence
```

`continuity` here means continuity *across* shots — a sequence that is locally continuous within each shot but globally inconsistent fails. `render balance` is a whole-trailer property: the aggregate `runway_ratio` across all shots must respect the hybrid cap (Part 4.1.10), a value no single shot determines. This is why the gate is sequence-scope: the properties it checks are properties of the whole, invisible to any element gate.

---

# Advisory Checks

| Check                | Owner  | Signals                                          |
| -------------------- | ------ | ------------------------------------------------ |
| `palette_consistency`| 4.1.6  | The palette holds consistent across the sequence.|
| `grammar_adherence`  | 4.1.6  | The sequence follows the visual grammar arc.     |

Advisory results inform the storyboard quality score (7.3) and never flip the verdict.

---

# Verdict Function

```yaml
verdict_function: all_mandatory_pass
```

The gate passes only when all six mandatory checks are PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE — the logical AND of Part 4.1.12.

---

# Upstream Verdict Dependencies

```yaml
upstream_verdicts:
  - shot_quality_gate: PASS   # for every shot in the sequence
```

The Storyboard Gate depends on every shot's Shot Gate PASS. It never re-validates individual shots; it trusts their recorded verdicts and evaluates only what the sequence adds. If any shot's verdict is absent or not PASS, the Storyboard Gate does not run (7.1.7).

---

# The Gate Report

```json
{
  "gate_id": "storyboard_quality_gate",
  "stage": "storyboard_generation",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "failed_checks": ["render balance"],
  "owning_sections": { "render balance": "4.1.10" },
  "blocking": true
}
```

This is the Part 4.1.12 `storyboard_gate_report` in the standard report shape. A `render balance` failure routes to 4.1.10 for re-planning of render strategies until the trailer conforms.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-831 — Skipping the Sequence Gate

Wrong:

```text
every shot passes → render without the Storyboard Gate
```

Correct:

```text
run the Storyboard Gate; individually valid shots can still fail as a sequence
```

---

## AP-832 — Raising the Ratio to Pass

Wrong:

```text
render balance fails → raise the hybrid ratio to force a pass
```

Correct:

```text
render balance fails → rebalance strategies per 4.1.10; the cap is not raised in-build
```

---

## AP-833 — Re-Validating Shots

Wrong:

```text
Storyboard Gate re-runs the eight shot checks
```

Correct:

```text
Storyboard Gate trusts each Shot Gate PASS and checks only sequence properties
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant SBG-701

The Storyboard Quality Gate is the Part 4.1.12 sequence gate expressed as a Section 7.1 instance, unchanged.

---

## Invariant SBG-702

The gate performs exactly the six mandatory sequence-level checks of Part 4.1.12.

---

## Invariant SBG-703

The gate runs only after every shot has passed the Shot Gate.

---

## Invariant SBG-704

The six checks are sequence-level and detect defects invisible to the element Shot Gate.

---

## Invariant SBG-705

`render balance` enforces the whole-trailer hybrid-rendering cap (P-408).

---

## Invariant SBG-706

Each check retains its Part 4 owning subsection.

---

## Invariant SBG-707

The gate depends on every shot's Shot Gate PASS and re-validates no shot.

---

## Invariant SBG-708

Advisory storyboard checks inform scoring but never block.

---

## Invariant SBG-709

The gate is sequence-scope, stage-exit, blocking, semantic.

---

## Invariant SBG-710

A Storyboard Gate PASS is the upstream dependency consumed by the Render Gate.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-861 | The Storyboard Quality Gate is the Part 4.1.12 sequence gate as a Section 7.1 instance. |
| ADR-862 | The six mandatory sequence-level checks of Part 4.1.12 are preserved unchanged.       |
| ADR-863 | The gate runs only after every shot passes the Shot Gate.                            |
| ADR-864 | The six checks detect sequence-level defects invisible to element gates.             |
| ADR-865 | `render balance` enforces the whole-trailer hybrid cap.                              |
| ADR-866 | Each check retains its Part 4 owning subsection.                                     |
| ADR-867 | The gate depends on every shot's Shot Gate PASS and re-validates no shot.             |
| ADR-868 | Advisory storyboard checks inform scoring but never block.                           |
| ADR-869 | The gate is sequence, stage-exit, blocking, semantic.                                |
| ADR-870 | A Storyboard Gate PASS is consumed as an upstream dependency by the Render Gate.       |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.5** is complete when:

* The Storyboard Quality Gate is shown to be the Part 4.1.12 sequence gate as a Section 7.1 instance, unchanged.
* The six mandatory sequence-level checks are enumerated with their Part 4 owners.
* Sequence-level semantics are defined, distinguishing the gate from the element Shot Gate.
* The whole-trailer nature of `render balance` is established.
* Advisory checks are enumerated and shown non-blocking.
* The dependency on every shot's Shot Gate PASS and the prohibition on re-validation are defined.
* Anti-patterns for skipping the gate, raising the ratio, and re-validating shots are documented.
* Invariants SBG-701 through SBG-710 and ADR-861 through ADR-870 are established.

---

# Part 7.2.6 — Render Quality Gate

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Render Quality Gate**: the checkpoint between render execution (Part 5) and composition.

The Render Quality Gate answers exactly one question:

> **"Is this rendered asset a faithful, intact realization of its approved shot, or must it be rejected before composition?"**

Render execution is the platform's most expensive and least deterministic stage: it submits jobs to external providers such as Runway and receives generated assets back. The Render Gate confirms that each returned asset is present, intact, conformant, and a faithful realization of the shot and storyboard that specified it — before the composition stage builds a timeline on it.

This is the first gate that validates *produced* output rather than a *plan*. It is where the platform confirms that expensive, non-deterministic generation actually delivered what the deterministic plan required.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A rendered asset is admissible only when it is present, integrity-verified, conformant to the shot's declared duration, resolution, and strategy, and produced by a successful provider job. A missing, corrupt, or non-conformant asset is rejected, never composited.**

The Render Gate is fail-closed against the provider: a provider failure, a truncated download, or a corrupt file is a FAIL, never a pass. The platform trusts the plan; it verifies the render.

---

# The Stage Boundary

```text
Approved Storyboard (passed Storyboard Gate)
        │
        ▼
Render Execution (Part 5)  ──► rendered assets (per shot)
        │
        ▼
Render Quality Gate  ◄── this section
        │  PASS (per asset)
        ▼
Composition
```

* **Input artifact:** one rendered asset and its provenance (the shot and job that produced it).
* **Output on PASS:** the asset, eligible for composition.
* **Owner of checks:** Part 5 — Rendering Platform & Runway Integration; provenance rules from Part 6.

---

# Gate Type

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    element        # one rendered asset
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: structural     # presence, integrity, conformance
```

The Render Gate is an element, stage-exit, blocking, structural gate. It runs per rendered asset. Whole-timeline coherence is deferred to the sequence-scope Composition Gate (7.2.7), and render↔storyboard fidelity to the cross-stage gate (7.2.11).

---

# Mandatory Checks

| Check                    | Owner  | Enforces                                                        |
| ------------------------ | ------ | -------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `asset_present`          | Part 5 | The rendered asset exists and downloaded completely.          |
| `asset_integrity`        | Part 5 | The asset's content hash matches the recorded provenance.     |
| `provider_job_succeeded` | Part 5 | The provider job completed with a success status.             |
| `duration_conformance`   | Part 5 | The asset duration matches the shot's declared duration.      |
| `resolution_conformance` | Part 5 | The asset resolution matches the required output spec.        |
| `strategy_conformance`   | Part 5 | The asset was produced by the shot's assigned render strategy.|
| `no_corruption`          | Part 5 | The asset decodes without corruption across all frames.       |
| `provenance_bound`       | Part 6 | The asset is bound to the exact shot identity that specified it.|

Each mandatory check must return PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE for the gate to pass.

---

# Mandatory Check Detail

## asset_present

The rendered asset exists and its download completed.

A truncated or absent download is a FAIL. The platform never composites a partial asset; a missing asset is not an empty pass (7.1.5).

---

## asset_integrity

The asset's content hash matches the hash recorded when the provider job completed.

This detects corruption in transit and mismatched assets. A hash mismatch is a FAIL, and the asset is re-fetched or re-rendered, never trusted.

---

## provider_job_succeeded

The provider job that produced the asset reported success.

A failed, cancelled, or timed-out provider job cannot yield an admissible asset. A non-success job status is a FAIL, regardless of whether a file was returned.

---

## duration_conformance

The asset duration matches the shot's declared `duration_seconds` (Part 4.1.2) within the configured tolerance (7.1.11).

An asset that is materially shorter or longer than planned breaks pacing and composition. A non-conformant duration fails.

---

## resolution_conformance

The asset resolution matches the required output specification.

An under-resolution asset degrades the final trailer. A resolution below the required spec is a FAIL.

---

## strategy_conformance

The asset was produced by the render strategy the shot was assigned (Part 4.1.9).

A shot assigned `runway_video` must be realized by Runway, not silently substituted. A strategy mismatch is a FAIL, preserving the plan's cost and fidelity intent.

---

## no_corruption

The asset decodes cleanly across all frames, with no dropped, black, or corrupt frames.

Frame-level corruption is a FAIL. This is the check that catches a provider returning a nominally valid file that is visually broken.

---

## provenance_bound

The asset is bound to the exact shot identity that specified it.

An asset with no verifiable link to its originating shot cannot be placed correctly in the timeline. Unbound provenance is a FAIL.

---

# Advisory Checks

| Check                | Owner  | Signals                                             |
| -------------------- | ------ | -------------------------------------------------- |
| `visual_quality`     | Part 5 | A measured visual-quality score for the asset.     |
| `motion_smoothness`  | Part 5 | Generated motion is smooth rather than artifacted. |

Advisory results inform the render quality score (7.3); a low visual-quality score is recorded but does not, by itself, block. A blocking visual defect is caught by `no_corruption`, which is mandatory.

---

# Verdict Function

```yaml
verdict_function: all_mandatory_pass
```

The gate passes only when every mandatory check is PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE.

---

# Upstream Verdict Dependencies

```yaml
upstream_verdicts:
  - storyboard_quality_gate: PASS
```

The Render Gate depends on the Storyboard Gate PASS. It never re-validates the storyboard; it verifies that the render faithfully realized the already-approved storyboard. Whether the render *matches* the storyboard in detail is the cross-stage gate's responsibility (7.2.11); this gate confirms the asset is present, intact, and conformant.

---

# The Gate Report

```json
{
```
