```json
  "gate_id": "render_quality_gate",
  "stage": "render_execution",
  "artifact_identity": "sha256:asset-shot-014-03...",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "failed_checks": ["asset_integrity"],
  "owning_sections": { "asset_integrity": "Part 5" },
  "blocking": true
}
```

---

# Provider Failure Is Fail-Closed

A provider failure resolves to FAIL, never to a bypass.

```text
Provider job fails / times out / returns corrupt asset
        │
        ▼
Render Gate FAIL (fail-closed)
        │
        ▼
Retry render or re-plan; never composite the failed asset
```

The platform's dependence on an external, non-deterministic provider makes this the most important application of the fail-closed model. An asset the platform cannot verify is treated as unacceptable, exactly as an unevaluated check is (7.1.5).

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-841 — Compositing a Partial Download

Wrong:

```text
asset truncated → composite what arrived
```

Correct:

```text
asset_present FAIL → re-fetch or re-render
```

---

## AP-842 — Trusting Provider Success Without Integrity

Wrong:

```text
provider says success → skip hash check → composite
```

Correct:

```text
provider success AND asset_integrity PASS both required
```

---

## AP-843 — Silent Strategy Substitution

Wrong:

```text
Runway job failed → substitute a cheaper strategy silently → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
strategy_conformance FAIL, or a recorded re-plan; never a silent substitution
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant RQG-701

The Render Quality Gate guards the boundary between render execution and composition.

---

## Invariant RQG-702

An asset passes only when present, integrity-verified, conformant, and produced by a successful provider job.

---

## Invariant RQG-703

Every Render Gate check is owned by Part 5, with provenance binding owned by Part 6.

---

## Invariant RQG-704

A provider failure, truncated download, or corrupt asset resolves to FAIL.

---

## Invariant RQG-705

Duration, resolution, and strategy conformance are enforced against the approved shot spec.

---

## Invariant RQG-706

An asset is bound to the exact shot identity that specified it.

---

## Invariant RQG-707

The gate is element-scope; whole-timeline coherence is deferred to the Composition Gate.

---

## Invariant RQG-708

The gate depends on the Storyboard Gate PASS and re-validates no storyboard.

---

## Invariant RQG-709

Render↔storyboard fidelity is enforced by the cross-stage gate, not this gate.

---

## Invariant RQG-710

Advisory render checks inform scoring; blocking visual defects are caught by mandatory `no_corruption`.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-871 | The Render Quality Gate guards the render→composition boundary.                      |
| ADR-872 | An asset passes only when present, intact, conformant, and provider-successful.      |
| ADR-873 | Render Gate checks are owned by Part 5, provenance by Part 6.                        |
| ADR-874 | Provider failure and corruption are fail-closed to FAIL.                             |
| ADR-875 | Duration, resolution, and strategy conformance are enforced against the shot spec.    |
| ADR-876 | Each asset is bound to its originating shot identity.                                |
| ADR-877 | The gate is element-scope; timeline coherence is the Composition Gate's concern.      |
| ADR-878 | The gate depends on the Storyboard Gate PASS.                                        |
| ADR-879 | Render↔storyboard fidelity is a cross-stage gate concern.                            |
| ADR-880 | Silent strategy substitution is prohibited; substitutions are recorded re-plans.      |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.6** is complete when:

* The Render Quality Gate is defined as the render→composition boundary gate.
* Its stage boundary, per-asset input, and output are explicit.
* Its element, stage-exit, blocking, structural type is declared.
* Its mandatory checks — presence, integrity, provider success, conformance, corruption, provenance — are enumerated with owners and detailed.
* Its advisory checks are enumerated and shown non-blocking.
* Fail-closed handling of provider failure is established.
* The dependency on the Storyboard Gate PASS and the deferral of fidelity to 7.2.11 are defined.
* Anti-patterns for partial downloads, unverified success, and silent substitution are documented.
* Invariants RQG-701 through RQG-710 and ADR-871 through ADR-880 are established.

---

# Part 7.2.7 — Composition Quality Gate

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Composition Quality Gate**: the checkpoint between composition (FFmpeg timeline assembly, Part 5 / Part 6) and the narration & audio stage.

The Composition Quality Gate answers exactly one question:

> **"Is this assembled timeline complete, correctly ordered, and gap-free, or must it be rejected before audio is layered onto it?"**

Composition assembles the individual rendered assets into a single continuous timeline — placing each segment in order, applying transitions, and producing a coherent video. The Composition Gate confirms that the assembled timeline is complete and correct before narration and audio are added.

Where the Render Gate validates each asset in isolation, the Composition Gate validates the *assembly*: that every segment is present, in the right order, with no gaps, matching the shot plan's intended sequence and duration.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A composed timeline is admissible only when it contains every planned segment, in the planned order, with valid transitions and no gaps, and its total duration matches the plan. A timeline missing a segment or out of order is rejected, never advanced.**

The Composition Gate is the first sequence gate over *produced* output. It confirms that the whole is correctly assembled from parts each already validated by the Render Gate.

---

# The Stage Boundary

```text
Rendered assets (each passed Render Gate)
        │
        ▼
Composition (Part 5 / Part 6)  ──► assembled timeline
        │
        ▼
Composition Quality Gate  ◄── this section
        │  PASS
        ▼
Narration & Audio (Part 3 / Part 5)
```

* **Input artifact:** the assembled timeline.
* **Output on PASS:** the timeline, admitted to narration and audio.
* **Owner of checks:** Part 5 (composition) and Part 6 (timeline assembly and ordering).

---

# Gate Type

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    sequence       # the assembled timeline
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: structural
```

The Composition Gate is a sequence, stage-exit, blocking, structural gate. It validates the timeline as a whole, only after every constituent asset has passed the element Render Gate (7.1.7).

---

# Mandatory Checks

| Check                     | Owner  | Enforces                                                       |
| ------------------------- | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `all_segments_present`    | Part 6 | Every planned segment appears in the timeline.                |
| `segment_order_matches_plan`| Part 6| Segments are ordered exactly as the shot plan specifies.     |
| `no_timeline_gaps`        | Part 5 | The timeline is continuous with no gaps or overlaps.          |
| `transitions_valid`       | Part 5 | Every transition is one of the permitted, correctly applied.  |
| `total_duration_matches`  | Part 6 | Total timeline duration matches the planned duration.         |
| `segment_boundaries_intact`| Part 5| Segment boundaries align to frame boundaries without drift.   |
| `resolution_uniform`      | Part 5 | All segments share the required uniform resolution.           |

Each mandatory check must return PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE.

---

# Mandatory Check Detail

## all_segments_present

Every segment the shot plan calls for appears in the assembled timeline.

A missing segment leaves a hole in the trailer. Evidence records the planned segment set and the observed set; any missing segment is a FAIL.

---

## segment_order_matches_plan

Segments appear in exactly the order the shot plan specifies.

Order carries narrative meaning (the visual grammar arc, Part 4.1.6). A reordered timeline is a FAIL, even if every segment is present.

---

## no_timeline_gaps

The timeline is continuous — no black gaps between segments and no unintended overlaps.

A gap is a visible defect. Evidence records any discontinuity; a gap or overlap is a FAIL.

---

## transitions_valid

Every transition between segments is a permitted transition, correctly applied.

An undefined or malformed transition is a FAIL. Transition *smoothness* is advisory; transition *validity* is mandatory.

---

## total_duration_matches

The total timeline duration matches the planned total within tolerance.

A timeline materially longer or shorter than planned indicates a missing, duplicated, or mis-durationed segment. A non-matching total is a FAIL.

---

## segment_boundaries_intact

Segment boundaries align to frame boundaries with no drift accumulation.

Sub-frame drift accumulates into audio-sync failures downstream. Boundary drift beyond tolerance is a FAIL.

---

## resolution_uniform

All segments share the single required output resolution.

A timeline mixing resolutions produces a visibly inconsistent trailer. Any non-uniform segment is a FAIL.

---

# Advisory Checks

| Check                   | Owner  | Signals                                             |
| ----------------------- | ------ | -------------------------------------------------- |
| `transition_smoothness` | Part 5 | Transitions are smooth rather than abrupt.         |
| `pacing_realized`       | Part 5 | The realized cut rhythm matches the planned pacing.|

Advisory results inform the composition quality score (7.3) and never block.

---

# Verdict Function

```yaml
verdict_function: all_mandatory_pass
```

---

# Upstream Verdict Dependencies

```yaml
upstream_verdicts:
  - render_quality_gate: PASS   # for every segment's asset
```

The Composition Gate depends on every constituent asset's Render Gate PASS. It never re-validates individual assets; it validates only what the assembly adds — presence, order, continuity, and total duration.

---

# The Gate Report

```json
{
  "gate_id": "composition_quality_gate",
  "stage": "composition",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "failed_checks": ["segment_order_matches_plan"],
  "owning_sections": { "segment_order_matches_plan": "Part 6" },
  "blocking": true
}
```

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-851 — Advancing a Gapped Timeline

Wrong:

```text
one segment missing → add audio to the gapped timeline
```

Correct:

```text
all_segments_present FAIL → complete the timeline first
```

---

## AP-852 — Tolerating Reorder

Wrong:

```text
segments present but reordered → "close enough" → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
segment_order_matches_plan FAIL → order carries meaning
```

---

## AP-853 — Re-Validating Assets

Wrong:

```text
Composition Gate re-checks each asset's integrity
```

Correct:

```text
Composition Gate trusts each Render Gate PASS; it checks the assembly
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant CQG-701

The Composition Quality Gate guards the boundary between composition and narration/audio.

---

## Invariant CQG-702

A timeline passes only when complete, correctly ordered, gap-free, and duration-matched.

---

## Invariant CQG-703

Composition Gate checks are owned by Part 5 and Part 6.

---

## Invariant CQG-704

Segment order must match the shot plan exactly; reordering is a FAIL.

---

## Invariant CQG-705

Timeline gaps, overlaps, and boundary drift beyond tolerance are FAILs.

---

## Invariant CQG-706

The gate is sequence-scope and runs only after every asset passes the Render Gate.

---

## Invariant CQG-707

The gate depends on every segment's Render Gate PASS and re-validates no asset.

---

## Invariant CQG-708

Transition validity is mandatory; transition smoothness is advisory.

---

## Invariant CQG-709

Total timeline duration must match the planned duration within tolerance.

---

## Invariant CQG-710

A Composition Gate PASS is the upstream dependency consumed by the Narration & Audio Gate.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-881 | The Composition Quality Gate guards the composition→narration boundary.             |
| ADR-882 | A timeline passes only when complete, ordered, gap-free, and duration-matched.       |
| ADR-883 | Composition Gate checks are owned by Part 5 and Part 6.                              |
| ADR-884 | Segment order must match the shot plan exactly.                                      |
| ADR-885 | Gaps, overlaps, and boundary drift are FAILs.                                        |
| ADR-886 | The gate is sequence-scope, running after all Render Gate passes.                    |
| ADR-887 | The gate depends on every segment's Render Gate PASS.                                |
| ADR-888 | Transition validity is mandatory; smoothness is advisory.                           |
| ADR-889 | Total duration must match the plan within tolerance.                                |
| ADR-890 | A Composition Gate PASS is consumed as an upstream dependency by the Narration Gate.  |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.7** is complete when:

* The Composition Quality Gate is defined as the composition→narration boundary gate.
* Its stage boundary, timeline input, and output are explicit.
* Its sequence, stage-exit, blocking, structural type is declared.
* Its mandatory checks — presence, order, gaps, transitions, duration, boundaries, resolution — are enumerated with owners and detailed.
* Its advisory checks are enumerated and shown non-blocking.
* The dependency on every asset's Render Gate PASS is defined, with no re-validation.
* Anti-patterns for gapped timelines, reorder tolerance, and asset re-validation are documented.
* Invariants CQG-701 through CQG-710 and ADR-881 through ADR-890 are established.

---

# Part 7.2.8 — Narration & Audio Quality Gate

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Narration & Audio Quality Gate**: the checkpoint between the narration & audio stage and packaging.

The Narration & Audio Quality Gate answers exactly one question:

> **"Is the audio track complete, correctly synchronized, and correctly leveled against the composed timeline, or must it be rejected before packaging?"**

The narration & audio stage layers narration, music, and sound onto the composed timeline. The gate confirms that the audio is present, synchronized to the video, correctly leveled, and consistent with the screenplay's narration timing (Part 3) before the trailer is packaged.

Audio defects — a missing narration line, a sync drift, a clipped level — are as visible to an audience as visual defects, and this gate catches them at the audio stage rather than at publication.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **An audio track is admissible only when every planned narration segment is present, synchronized to the timeline within tolerance, correctly leveled, and consistent with the approved narration timing. Missing, drifted, or clipped audio is rejected.**

The gate enforces both fidelity to the screenplay's narration plan (Part 3) and technical audio correctness against the composed timeline (Part 5).

---

# The Stage Boundary

```text
Composed timeline (passed Composition Gate)
        │
        ▼
Narration & Audio (Part 3 / Part 5)  ──► timeline + audio track
        │
        ▼
Narration & Audio Quality Gate  ◄── this section
        │  PASS
        ▼
Packaging (Part 6)
```

* **Input artifact:** the timeline with its assembled audio track.
* **Output on PASS:** the audio-complete trailer, admitted to packaging.
* **Owner of checks:** Part 3 (narration timing) and Part 5 (audio technical).

---

# Gate Type

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    sequence       # the full audio track over the timeline
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: structural
```

The Narration & Audio Gate is a sequence, stage-exit, blocking, structural gate. It validates the whole audio track against the whole timeline.

---

# Mandatory Checks

| Check                        | Owner  | Enforces                                                       |
| ---------------------------- | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `all_narration_present`      | Part 3 | Every planned narration segment is present.                   |
| `narration_timing_matches`   | Part 3 | Narration aligns to the approved narration timing.            |
| `audio_video_sync`           | Part 5 | Audio is synchronized to video within tolerance.              |
| `levels_within_spec`         | Part 5 | Audio levels sit within the required loudness spec.           |
| `no_clipping`                | Part 5 | No audio clipping or distortion is present.                   |
| `no_dropouts`                | Part 5 | No unintended audio dropouts or silence gaps.                 |
| `language_correct`           | Part 3 | The narration language matches the target specification.      |

Each mandatory check must return PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE. A trailer with no narration by design resolves narration checks as NOT_APPLICABLE (7.1.4), never as silent PASS.

---

# Mandatory Check Detail

## all_narration_present

Every narration segment the screenplay specifies is present in the audio track.

A missing narration line leaves a planned beat silent. Evidence records the planned versus present narration set; any missing segment is a FAIL.

---

## narration_timing_matches

Narration aligns to the approved narration timing from the screenplay (Part 3).

Narration that lands early or late against its intended moment is a FAIL. This enforces fidelity to the screenplay's narration plan validated at the Screenplay Gate.

---

## audio_video_sync

Audio is synchronized to the video within the configured tolerance.

Sync drift is among the most perceptible defects. Drift beyond tolerance is a FAIL. This check depends on the composition's boundary integrity (7.2.7).

---

## levels_within_spec

Audio loudness sits within the required spec (integrated loudness and true-peak).

Levels outside spec cause the trailer to be too quiet, too loud, or rejected by a publication target. Out-of-spec levels are a FAIL.

---

## no_clipping

No audio clipping or distortion is present.

Clipping is an unrecoverable defect. Any detected clipping is a FAIL.

---

## no_dropouts

No unintended dropouts, silence gaps, or truncations are present.

An accidental silence reads as a technical fault. Any unintended dropout is a FAIL.

---

## language_correct

The narration language matches the target language specification.

A trailer narrated in the wrong language is unusable for its target. A language mismatch is a FAIL.

---

# Advisory Checks

| Check                | Owner  | Signals                                             |
| -------------------- | ------ | -------------------------------------------------- |
| `narration_clarity`  | Part 5 | A measured narration intelligibility score.        |
| `music_balance`      | Part 5 | Music sits in balance with narration.              |

Advisory results inform the audio quality score (7.3) and never block.

---

# Verdict Function

```yaml
verdict_function: all_mandatory_pass
```

---

# Upstream Verdict Dependencies

```yaml
upstream_verdicts:
  - composition_quality_gate: PASS
  - screenplay_quality_gate: PASS   # for narration timing fidelity
```

The gate depends on the Composition Gate PASS (the timeline it synchronizes against) and references the Screenplay Gate PASS (the approved narration timing). It re-derives neither; it verifies the audio against both recorded verdicts.

---

# The Gate Report

```json
{
  "gate_id": "narration_audio_quality_gate",
  "stage": "narration_audio",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "failed_checks": ["audio_video_sync"],
  "owning_sections": { "audio_video_sync": "Part 5" },
  "blocking": true
}
```

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-861 — Packaging a De-Synced Trailer

Wrong:

```text
audio drifts 300ms → package anyway
```

Correct:

```text
audio_video_sync FAIL → re-sync before packaging
```

---

## AP-862 — Silent Missing Narration

Wrong:

```text
one narration line absent → treat as intentional silence → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
all_narration_present FAIL, unless narration is NOT_APPLICABLE by design with justification
```

---

## AP-863 — Ignoring Loudness Spec

Wrong:

```text
levels above spec → "sounds fine" → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
levels_within_spec FAIL → conform to the loudness spec
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant NQG-701

The Narration & Audio Quality Gate guards the boundary between narration/audio and packaging.

---

## Invariant NQG-702

The audio passes only when complete, synchronized, correctly leveled, and timing-consistent.

---

## Invariant NQG-703

Narration checks are owned by Part 3; audio-technical checks by Part 5.

---

## Invariant NQG-704

Every planned narration segment is present, or resolved NOT_APPLICABLE with justification.

---

## Invariant NQG-705

Audio-video sync drift beyond tolerance is a FAIL.

---

## Invariant NQG-706

Loudness out of spec, clipping, and dropouts are FAILs.

---

## Invariant NQG-707

The gate is sequence-scope over the full audio track.

---

## Invariant NQG-708

The gate depends on the Composition Gate PASS and the Screenplay Gate PASS.

---

## Invariant NQG-709

Advisory audio checks inform scoring but never block.

---

## Invariant NQG-710

A Narration & Audio Gate PASS is the upstream dependency consumed by the Packaging Gate.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-891 | The Narration & Audio Gate guards the narration→packaging boundary.                  |
| ADR-892 | Audio passes only when complete, synced, leveled, and timing-consistent.             |
| ADR-893 | Narration checks are owned by Part 3, audio-technical by Part 5.                     |
| ADR-894 | Every planned narration segment is present or justified NOT_APPLICABLE.              |
| ADR-895 | Sync drift beyond tolerance is a FAIL.                                               |
| ADR-896 | Out-of-spec loudness, clipping, and dropouts are FAILs.                              |
| ADR-897 | The gate is sequence-scope over the audio track.                                    |
| ADR-898 | The gate depends on the Composition and Screenplay Gate passes.                      |
| ADR-899 | Advisory audio checks inform scoring but never block.                               |
| ADR-900 | A Narration & Audio Gate PASS is consumed as an upstream dependency by Packaging.     |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.8** is complete when:

* The Narration & Audio Quality Gate is defined as the narration→packaging boundary gate.
* Its stage boundary, input, and output are explicit.
* Its sequence, stage-exit, blocking, structural type is declared.
* Its mandatory checks — presence, timing, sync, levels, clipping, dropouts, language — are enumerated with owners and detailed.
* NOT_APPLICABLE handling for narration-free trailers is defined.
* Its advisory checks are enumerated and shown non-blocking.
* The dependencies on the Composition and Screenplay Gate passes are defined.
* Anti-patterns for de-sync, silent missing narration, and loudness are documented.
* Invariants NQG-701 through NQG-710 and ADR-891 through ADR-900 are established.

---

# Part 7.2.9 — Metadata & Packaging Quality Gate

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Metadata & Packaging Quality Gate**: the checkpoint between packaging (Part 6) and publication.

The Metadata & Packaging Quality Gate answers exactly one question:

> **"Is this package complete, correctly formatted, and fully described by its metadata, or must it be rejected before publication?"**

Packaging assembles the finished trailer, its metadata, and its delivery artifacts into a publishable package. The gate confirms that the package is structurally complete, its metadata is present and valid, and its format conforms to the publication target's requirements — before the package reaches the Publication Gate.

This gate catches the defects that would cause a publication to fail or a published trailer to be malformed: a missing thumbnail, an incomplete metadata field, a container in the wrong format.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A package is admissible only when every required artifact is present, every required metadata field is valid, and the container format conforms to the target specification. An incomplete or malformed package is rejected, never published.**

The gate is the last structural checkpoint before publication. It ensures the Publication Gate (7.2.10) evaluates a well-formed package and can focus on rights, safety, and approval rather than structural completeness.

---

# The Stage Boundary

```text
Audio-complete trailer (passed Narration & Audio Gate)
        │
        ▼
Packaging (Part 6)  ──► publishable package (trailer + metadata + artifacts)
        │
        ▼
Metadata & Packaging Quality Gate  ◄── this section
        │  PASS
        ▼
Publication (Part 6 / Part 7.4)
```

* **Input artifact:** the assembled publishable package.
* **Output on PASS:** the package, admitted to publication.
* **Owner of checks:** Part 6 — packaging and metadata.

---

# Gate Type

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    sequence       # the whole package
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: structural
```

The Metadata & Packaging Gate is a sequence, stage-exit, blocking, structural gate over the whole package.

---

# Mandatory Checks

| Check                    | Owner  | Enforces                                                       |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `all_artifacts_present`  | Part 6 | Every required package artifact is present.                   |
| `metadata_complete`      | Part 6 | Every required metadata field is present.                     |
| `metadata_valid`         | Part 6 | Every metadata field is well-formed and within constraints.   |
| `container_format_valid` | Part 6 | The container format conforms to the target specification.    |
| `thumbnail_present`      | Part 6 | The required thumbnail/poster artifact is present and valid.  |
| `checksums_valid`        | Part 6 | Every artifact's checksum matches its manifest entry.         |
| `manifest_consistent`    | Part 6 | The package manifest matches the actual package contents.     |

Each mandatory check must return PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE.

---

# Mandatory Check Detail

## all_artifacts_present

Every artifact the package specification requires — the trailer, thumbnail, captions, and delivery files — is present.

A missing artifact makes the package incomplete. Evidence records the required versus present artifact set; any absence is a FAIL.

---

## metadata_complete

Every required metadata field — title, description, attribution, target, rights references — is present.

An incomplete metadata record produces a malformed publication. Any missing required field is a FAIL.

---

## metadata_valid

Every metadata field is well-formed and within its constraints (length, format, allowed values).

A present-but-malformed field is as bad as a missing one. Malformed metadata is a FAIL.

---

## container_format_valid

The trailer container format conforms to the publication target's specification.

A container in the wrong format is rejected by the target. A non-conformant container is a FAIL.

---

## thumbnail_present

The required thumbnail or poster artifact is present, correctly sized, and valid.

A missing or malformed thumbnail degrades the publication. Its absence or invalidity is a FAIL.

---

## checksums_valid

Every artifact's checksum matches the value recorded in the package manifest.

A checksum mismatch indicates corruption or substitution. Any mismatch is a FAIL, consistent with the content-addressed integrity discipline of Part 6.2.

---

## manifest_consistent

The package manifest describes exactly the package's actual contents — no missing entries, no phantom entries.

An inconsistent manifest breaks downstream automation. Any inconsistency is a FAIL.

---

# Advisory Checks

| Check                  | Owner  | Signals                                             |
| ---------------------- | ------ | -------------------------------------------------- |
| `metadata_richness`    | Part 6 | Optional descriptive metadata is populated.        |
| `caption_quality`      | Part 6 | Caption formatting and coverage quality.           |

Advisory results inform the packaging quality score (7.3) and never block.

---

# Verdict Function

```yaml
verdict_function: all_mandatory_pass
```

---

# Upstream Verdict Dependencies

```yaml
upstream_verdicts:
  - narration_audio_quality_gate: PASS
```

The gate depends on the Narration & Audio Gate PASS (the audio-complete trailer it packages). It re-validates neither audio nor video; it validates the package built around them.

---

# The Gate Report

```json
{
  "gate_id": "metadata_packaging_quality_gate",
  "stage": "packaging",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "failed_checks": ["metadata_complete"],
  "owning_sections": { "metadata_complete": "Part 6" },
  "blocking": true
}
```

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-871 — Publishing With Incomplete Metadata

Wrong:

```text
description field empty → publish and "fill in later"
```

Correct:

```text
metadata_complete FAIL → complete metadata before publication
```

---

## AP-872 — Trusting the Manifest Without Checksums

Wrong:

```text
manifest lists the artifact → assume it is intact → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
checksums_valid required; a manifest entry is not proof of integrity
```

---

## AP-873 — Wrong Container Format

Wrong:

```text
container format differs from target → "the target may accept it" → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
container_format_valid FAIL → conform to the target specification
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant MQG-701

The Metadata & Packaging Quality Gate guards the boundary between packaging and publication.

---

## Invariant MQG-702

A package passes only when complete, metadata-valid, and format-conformant.

---

## Invariant MQG-703

Packaging Gate checks are owned by Part 6.

---

## Invariant MQG-704

Every required artifact and every required metadata field must be present.

---

## Invariant MQG-705

Every artifact checksum must match its manifest entry.

---

## Invariant MQG-706

The package manifest must be consistent with actual package contents.

---

## Invariant MQG-707

The container format must conform to the publication target specification.

---

## Invariant MQG-708

The gate is sequence-scope over the whole package.

---

## Invariant MQG-709

The gate depends on the Narration & Audio Gate PASS and re-validates no audio or video.

---

## Invariant MQG-710

A Packaging Gate PASS is the upstream dependency consumed by the Publication Gate.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-901 | The Metadata & Packaging Gate guards the packaging→publication boundary.            |
| ADR-902 | A package passes only when complete, metadata-valid, and format-conformant.          |
| ADR-903 | Packaging Gate checks are owned by Part 6.                                           |
| ADR-904 | Every required artifact and metadata field must be present.                          |
| ADR-905 | Every artifact checksum must match its manifest entry.                               |
| ADR-906 | The manifest must be consistent with actual package contents.                        |
| ADR-907 | The container format must conform to the publication target.                         |
| ADR-908 | The gate is sequence-scope over the whole package.                                  |
| ADR-909 | The gate depends on the Narration & Audio Gate PASS.                                 |
| ADR-910 | A Packaging Gate PASS is consumed as an upstream dependency by the Publication Gate.  |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.9** is complete when:

* The Metadata & Packaging Quality Gate is defined as the packaging→publication boundary gate.
* Its stage boundary, package input, and output are explicit.
* Its sequence, stage-exit, blocking, structural type is declared.
* Its mandatory checks — artifacts, metadata completeness/validity, format, thumbnail, checksums, manifest — are enumerated with owners and detailed.
* Its advisory checks are enumerated and shown non-blocking.
* The dependency on the Narration & Audio Gate PASS is defined.
* Anti-patterns for incomplete metadata, unverified manifests, and wrong format are documented.
* Invariants MQG-701 through MQG-710 and ADR-901 through ADR-910 are established.

---

# Part 7.2.10 — Publication Quality Gate

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Publication Quality Gate**: the final checkpoint between a finished package and the outside world.

The Publication Quality Gate answers exactly one question:

> **"Is this trailer cleared, safe, approved, and correctly targeted for release, or must it be withheld?"**

Publication is irreversible in a way no earlier stage is: once a trailer is public, it has reached an audience and cannot be un-seen. The Publication Gate is therefore the strictest gate in the platform. It confirms that publication rights are cleared, that safety obligations are met, that the required human editorial approval exists, and that the publish target is correct — before anything is released.

This gate carries the platform's **non-waivable checks** (7.1.10). A rights or safety failure here halts publication absolutely; no waiver, deadline, or authority can release it.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A trailer is publishable only when rights are cleared, safety is validated, required human approval is recorded, and the target is correct. Rights and safety are non-waivable: their failure withholds publication absolutely.**

The Publication Gate is where enforcement authority meets editorial authority (Part 7.4). The gate mechanically confirms the *presence* of the required human approval; it never substitutes for the human judgment itself.

---

# The Stage Boundary

```text
Publishable package (passed Packaging Gate)
        │
        ▼
Publication (Part 6 / Part 7.4)
        │
        ▼
Publication Quality Gate  ◄── this section
        │  PASS
        ▼
Released Trailer
```

* **Input artifact:** the complete publishable package plus its approval and rights records.
* **Output on PASS:** authorization to release.
* **Owner of checks:** Part 6 (publication mechanics), Part 7.4 (approval), and governance (Part 7.1.10) for non-waivable status.

---

# Gate Type

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    sequence           # the complete package + approvals
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: human-approval     # includes a recorded human decision
```

The Publication Gate is a sequence, stage-exit, blocking, human-approval gate. It is the only stage-exit gate whose judgment type is human-approval: it enforces the presence of a recorded editorial decision in addition to structural and rights checks.

---

# Mandatory Checks

| Check                          | Owner        | Enforces                                                     | Waivable |
| ------------------------------ | ------------ | ----------------------------------------------------------- | -------- |
| `publication_rights_cleared`   | Part 6       | All publication rights are cleared and recorded.            | **No**   |
| `child_safety_validated`       | Governance   | Child-safety obligations are validated.                     | **No**   |
| `content_safety_validated`     | Governance   | Content-safety obligations are validated.                   | **No**   |
| `editorial_approval_recorded`  | Part 7.4     | Required human editorial approval is recorded and current.  | No       |
| `approval_scope_matches`       | Part 7.4     | The approval scope matches this exact artifact identity.    | No       |
| `publish_target_valid`         | Part 6       | The publication target is valid and authorized.             | Yes      |
| `no_upstream_waivers_open`     | Part 7.1.10  | No unresolved blocking waiver remains open on the chain.    | No       |

Each mandatory check must return PASS. The `Waivable` column records that rights and safety checks are **non-waivable** (7.1.10): no waiver can release a FAIL on them.

---

# Mandatory Check Detail

## publication_rights_cleared

All rights required to publish — to the source article, to any depicted material, to music and assets — are cleared and recorded.

Publishing without cleared rights exposes the platform to legal and ethical failure. Uncleared rights are a FAIL, and the check is **non-waivable**.

---

## child_safety_validated

The trailer meets the platform's child-safety obligations.

This is the platform's highest-priority safety guarantee. A child-safety FAIL withholds publication absolutely. The check is **non-waivable** and is enforced regardless of authority, deadline, or profile.

---

## content_safety_validated

The trailer meets the platform's content-safety obligations.

Content that violates safety policy is withheld. The check is **non-waivable**.

---

## editorial_approval_recorded

The required human editorial approval exists, is current, and is recorded (Part 7.4).

The gate confirms the *presence* of the approval; it does not make the approval. A missing or stale approval is a FAIL. The gate never self-approves.

---

## approval_scope_matches

The recorded approval applies to the exact artifact identity being published.

An approval granted for a prior version does not cover a changed trailer (7.1.5, verdict binding). A scope mismatch is a FAIL — a trailer altered after approval must be re-approved.

---

## publish_target_valid

The publication target is valid, authorized, and correctly configured.

Publishing to the wrong target is a release defect. An invalid or unauthorized target is a FAIL. This check is waivable only by governance for a corrected, re-validated target.

---

## no_upstream_waivers_open

No unresolved blocking waiver remains open anywhere on the gate chain.

A waiver recorded upstream (7.1.10) must be resolved or explicitly accepted by governance before publication. An open, unresolved blocking waiver is a FAIL, ensuring nothing is published while a known exception is still pending.

---

# Human Approval Is Presence, Not Judgment

The Publication Gate mechanizes the presence of approval; the human owns its substance.

```text
Editorial Authority (Part 7.4) → makes the approval decision
Publication Gate               → checks the decision is recorded, current, scoped
```

The gate never decides whether the trailer is *good enough* to publish; that is the editorial authority's judgment, recorded as an approval. The gate decides only whether that recorded approval *exists and applies*. This preserves the separation of enforcement from editorial judgment (7.1.1, non-scope).

---

# Non-Waivable Enforcement

Rights and safety checks cannot be released by any waiver.

```text
child_safety_validated FAIL
        │
        ▼
Publication withheld absolutely
        │
        ▼
No waiver, authority, deadline, or profile can release it
```

This is the concrete instance of the non-waivable checks defined in 7.1.10. The Publication Gate is where the platform's hard floor is enforced: certain failures are simply not releasable. A waiver against a non-waivable check is itself invalid and rejected.

---

# Advisory Checks

| Check                  | Owner  | Signals                                             |
| ---------------------- | ------ | -------------------------------------------------- |
| `metadata_seo_quality` | Part 6 | Discoverability metadata quality for the target.    |
| `release_timing_fit`   | Part 6 | The release timing fits the planned schedule.       |

Advisory results inform the publication readiness score (7.3) and never block. No safety or rights concern is ever advisory.

---

# Verdict Function

```yaml
verdict_function: all_mandatory_pass
```

The gate passes only when every mandatory check is PASS. Given the presence of non-waivable checks, even a governance waiver cannot convert this gate's FAIL on a non-waivable check.

---

# Upstream Verdict Dependencies

```yaml
upstream_verdicts:
  - metadata_packaging_quality_gate: PASS
  - render_storyboard_coherence_gate: PASS   # cross-stage fidelity (7.2.11)
```

The Publication Gate depends on the Packaging Gate PASS and on the cross-stage render↔storyboard coherence PASS (7.2.11). Reaching the Publication Gate proves the entire upstream chain passed (7.1.7, non-bypassable); the Publication Gate adds rights, safety, approval, and target on top.

---

# The Gate Report

```json
{
  "gate_id": "publication_quality_gate",
  "stage": "publication",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "failed_checks": ["editorial_approval_recorded"],
  "owning_sections": { "editorial_approval_recorded": "7.4" },
  "non_waivable_failures": [],
  "blocking": true
}
```

The report adds a `non_waivable_failures` field. A non-empty `non_waivable_failures` means publication is withheld absolutely and no waiver path exists.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-881 — Self-Approval

Wrong:

```text
Publication Gate marks the trailer approved on the author's behalf
```

Correct:

```text
editorial_approval_recorded checks a human decision made in Part 7.4; the gate never self-approves
```

---

## AP-882 — Waiving Safety

Wrong:

```text
child_safety_validated FAIL → governance waives it under deadline
```

Correct:

```text
child_safety_validated is non-waivable; publication is withheld absolutely
```

---

## AP-883 — Stale Approval

Wrong:

```text
trailer changed after approval → publish under the old approval
```

Correct:

```text
approval_scope_matches FAIL → re-approve the changed artifact identity
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant PQG-701

The Publication Quality Gate is the final, strictest gate before release.

---

## Invariant PQG-702

A trailer publishes only with rights cleared, safety validated, approval recorded, and a valid target.

---

## Invariant PQG-703

`publication_rights_cleared`, `child_safety_validated`, and `content_safety_validated` are non-waivable.

---

## Invariant PQG-704

A non-waivable FAIL withholds publication absolutely; no waiver, authority, deadline, or profile can release it.

---

## Invariant PQG-705

The gate confirms the presence of human editorial approval and never self-approves.

---

## Invariant PQG-706

Approval scope must match the exact artifact identity being published.

---

## Invariant PQG-707

No open, unresolved blocking waiver on the chain may remain at publication.

---

## Invariant PQG-708

The gate is sequence-scope, stage-exit, blocking, human-approval.

---

## Invariant PQG-709

Reaching the Publication Gate proves the entire upstream chain, including cross-stage coherence, passed.

---

## Invariant PQG-710

No safety or rights concern is ever expressed as an advisory check.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-911 | The Publication Quality Gate is the final, strictest gate before release.            |
| ADR-912 | Publication requires rights, safety, recorded approval, and a valid target.           |
| ADR-913 | Rights and safety checks are non-waivable.                                          |
| ADR-914 | A non-waivable FAIL withholds publication absolutely.                                |
| ADR-915 | The gate confirms approval presence and never self-approves.                         |
| ADR-916 | Approval scope must match the exact artifact identity.                               |
| ADR-917 | No unresolved blocking waiver may remain open at publication.                        |
| ADR-918 | The gate is sequence, stage-exit, blocking, human-approval.                          |
| ADR-919 | The gate depends on the Packaging and cross-stage coherence passes.                  |
| ADR-920 | Safety and rights are never advisory.                                               |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.10** is complete when:

* The Publication Quality Gate is defined as the final, strictest gate before release.
* Its stage boundary, package-plus-approvals input, and release authorization output are explicit.
* Its human-approval judgment type is declared.
* Its mandatory checks — rights, child/content safety, approval, scope, target, open-waiver — are enumerated with owners, detail, and waivability.
* Non-waivable enforcement of rights and safety is established and tied to 7.1.10.
* The distinction between approval presence and editorial judgment is defined.
* The dependency on the Packaging and cross-stage coherence passes is defined.
* Anti-patterns for self-approval, waiving safety, and stale approval are documented.
* Invariants PQG-701 through PQG-710 and ADR-911 through ADR-920 are established.

---

# Part 7.2.11 — Cross-Stage Coherence Gates

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Cross-Stage Coherence Gates**: the family of gates that verify a transformation preserved meaning across a stage boundary.

A single-stage gate validates the output of one stage against that stage's rules. A cross-stage coherence gate validates that the output of one stage faithfully realizes the *approved output of an earlier stage*. It answers:

> **"Does what was produced still match what was approved?"**

The most important cross-stage gate confirms that rendered assets match the approved storyboard: that the expensive, non-deterministic render actually produced what the deterministic plan specified. Cross-stage gates are the platform's defense against drift — the slow divergence between plan and product that no single-stage gate can see.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A transformation is coherent only when the produced artifact faithfully realizes the approved source artifact. Drift between what was approved and what was produced is rejected, regardless of whether each artifact is individually valid.**

A rendered asset can pass the Render Gate (present, intact, conformant) and still not depict the approved shot. A composed timeline can pass the Composition Gate (complete, ordered) and still not follow the approved shot plan's intent. Cross-stage gates catch exactly this class of defect: individually valid, jointly incoherent.

---

# The Cross-Stage Gate Family

The platform defines the following cross-stage coherence gates.

| Gate                                | Verifies                                              | Between            |
| ----------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------- | ------------------ |
| `render_storyboard_coherence_gate`  | Rendered assets realize the approved storyboard.     | Storyboard ↔ Render |
| `composition_shotplan_coherence_gate`| The timeline realizes the approved shot plan order.  | Shot Plan ↔ Composition |
| `published_approved_coherence_gate` | The published trailer matches the approved artifact. | Approval ↔ Publication |

Each is a cross-stage-scope gate (7.1.6). Each runs at the boundary where a transformation must be verified, after both the source and produced artifacts have passed their own single-stage gates.

---

# Gate Type

```yaml
gate_type:
  scope:    cross-stage
  trigger:  stage-exit
  blocking: blocking
  judgment: semantic
```

Cross-stage coherence gates are cross-stage, stage-exit, blocking, semantic gates. They span the outputs of two stages and judge the fidelity of the transformation between them.

---

# The Render–Storyboard Coherence Gate

The canonical cross-stage gate verifies that rendered assets realize the approved storyboard.

```text
Approved Storyboard (Storyboard Gate PASS)
        │
        ├───────────────► specifies each shot's visual intent
        │
Rendered Assets (Render Gate PASS)
        │
        ▼
render_storyboard_coherence_gate  ◄── this gate
        │  PASS
        ▼
Composition
```

## Mandatory Checks

| Check                        | Owner         | Enforces                                                     |
| ---------------------------- | ------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------- |
| `every_shot_rendered`        | Part 5 / 7    | Every approved shot has a corresponding rendered asset.     |
| `subject_matches`            | Part 4 / 5    | The rendered subject matches the shot's focal subject.      |
| `composition_matches_intent` | Part 4 / 5    | The rendered framing matches the storyboard's visual intent.|
| `continuity_preserved`       | Part 4 / 5    | Character and location continuity are preserved in render.  |
| `no_prohibited_content`      | Part 4.1.11   | No concept rendered as forbidden literal text.              |
| `strategy_realized`          | Part 4 / 5    | Each shot realized by its assigned render strategy.         |

A rendered asset that is individually valid but does not depict the approved shot fails `subject_matches` or `composition_matches_intent`, even though it passed the Render Gate.

---

# Why Single-Stage Gates Are Insufficient

Drift is invisible to single-stage gates by construction.

```text
Render Gate:      "is this asset present, intact, conformant?"   → YES
Storyboard Gate:  "is this storyboard coherent?"                 → YES
Missing question: "does this asset depict THIS storyboard?"      → ???
```

Neither single-stage gate asks whether the asset matches the plan, because neither sees both. The cross-stage gate exists precisely to ask the question that spans the boundary. Without it, a render that is technically perfect but depicts the wrong content would pass every single-stage gate and reach publication.

---

# Cross-Stage Gates Consume, Never Re-Derive

A cross-stage gate depends on both single-stage gates and re-validates neither.

```yaml
upstream_verdicts:
  - storyboard_quality_gate: PASS
  - render_quality_gate: PASS   # for every asset
```

The `render_storyboard_coherence_gate` trusts that the storyboard is valid (Storyboard Gate) and that each asset is intact (Render Gate). It adds only the fidelity judgment: does the intact asset realize the valid storyboard. It re-checks neither storyboard validity nor asset integrity (7.1.7, no re-derivation).

---

# The Published–Approved Coherence Gate

The final cross-stage gate confirms the published trailer matches the approved artifact.

```text
Approved artifact identity (from editorial approval, 7.4)
        │
        ▼
published_approved_coherence_gate
        │  compares published identity to approved identity
        ▼
PASS only if identical
```

This gate is the ultimate guard against publishing something other than what was approved. It confirms the published artifact identity equals the approved artifact identity (7.1.5, verdict binding). Any divergence — a re-encode, a substitution, a late edit — fails, because approval binds to an exact identity.

---

# The Gate Report

```json
{
  "gate_id": "render_storyboard_coherence_gate",
  "stage": "render_storyboard_boundary",
  "verdict": "FAIL",
  "failed_checks": ["composition_matches_intent"],
  "owning_sections": { "composition_matches_intent": "4.1.6 / Part 5" },
  "upstream_verdicts": { "storyboard_quality_gate": "PASS", "render_quality_gate": "PASS" },
  "blocking": true
}
```

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-891 — Assuming Fidelity From Validity

Wrong:

```text
Render Gate PASS and Storyboard Gate PASS → assume the render matches the storyboard
```

Correct:

```text
render_storyboard_coherence_gate explicitly checks fidelity across the boundary
```

---

## AP-892 — Re-Validating in the Cross-Stage Gate

Wrong:

```text
Coherence gate re-checks storyboard coherence and asset integrity
```

Correct:

```text
Coherence gate trusts both single-stage passes and checks only fidelity
```

---

## AP-893 — Publishing a Divergent Identity

Wrong:

```text
approved identity ≠ published identity → publish anyway
```

Correct:

```text
published_approved_coherence_gate FAIL → publish only the approved identity
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant XSG-701

Cross-stage coherence gates verify that a produced artifact faithfully realizes an approved source artifact.

---

## Invariant XSG-702

A cross-stage gate is cross-stage-scope, stage-exit, blocking, and semantic.

---

## Invariant XSG-703

The render–storyboard coherence gate confirms every approved shot is rendered and depicts its approved intent.

---

## Invariant XSG-704

Drift between approved and produced artifacts is rejected even when each artifact is individually valid.

---

## Invariant XSG-705

A cross-stage gate depends on both single-stage passes and re-derives neither.

---

## Invariant XSG-706

The render–storyboard coherence gate enforces that no forbidden literal concept text appears (Part 4.1.11).

---

## Invariant XSG-707

The published–approved coherence gate confirms the published identity equals the approved identity.

---

## Invariant XSG-708

Cross-stage gates run after both source and produced artifacts pass their single-stage gates.

---

## Invariant XSG-709

A cross-stage FAIL blocks advancement exactly as a single-stage FAIL does.

---

## Invariant XSG-710

The render–storyboard coherence PASS is an upstream dependency of the Publication Gate.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-921 | Cross-stage coherence gates verify fidelity of a transformation across a boundary.   |
| ADR-922 | Cross-stage gates are cross-stage-scope, stage-exit, blocking, semantic.             |
| ADR-923 | The render–storyboard gate confirms rendered assets realize the approved storyboard. |
| ADR-924 | Drift between approved and produced is rejected even when each is individually valid.|
| ADR-925 | Cross-stage gates consume both single-stage passes and re-derive neither.            |
| ADR-926 | The render–storyboard gate enforces the no-forbidden-text rule of Part 4.1.11.       |
| ADR-927 | The published–approved gate confirms published identity equals approved identity.    |
| ADR-928 | Cross-stage gates run after both source and produced single-stage gates pass.        |
| ADR-929 | A cross-stage FAIL blocks advancement like any blocking gate.                        |
| ADR-930 | The render–storyboard coherence PASS is an upstream dependency of Publication.        |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.2.11** is complete when:

* Cross-stage coherence gates are defined as verifying fidelity of a transformation across a boundary.
* The cross-stage gate family — render↔storyboard, composition↔shot-plan, published↔approved — is enumerated.
* The cross-stage-scope, stage-exit, blocking, semantic type is declared.
* The render–storyboard coherence gate's mandatory checks are enumerated with owners.
* It is established why single-stage gates cannot detect drift.
* The consume-not-re-derive dependency on both single-stage passes is defined.
* The published–approved identity-equality gate is defined.
* Anti-patterns for assuming fidelity, re-validation, and divergent identity are documented.
* Invariants XSG-701 through XSG-710 and ADR-921 through ADR-930 are established.

```text
Story ─► Screenplay ─► Shot ─► Storyboard ─► [render↔storyboard] ─► Render ─►
```

Reaching any gate proves every upstream gate passed. Reaching publication proves the entire chain — every single-stage gate and every cross-stage coherence gate — returned PASS.

Every check is owned; no stage gate authors a rule (Principle 3).

Every gate is an instance of the Section 7.1 architecture, every check is owned by a defining section, and the gates compose into a complete, non-bypassable chain from the insight article to the released trailer.
