# 7.3 Quality Metrics, Scoring & Enforcement

# Part 7.3.1 — Purpose & Measurement Philosophy

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **measurement philosophy** of the Quality Gates: how the platform measures quality continuously, and the strict boundary between measurement and the mandatory admissibility floor.

Sections 7.1 and 7.2 defined gates as binary admissibility conditions. This section adds the continuous dimension: quality *scores*, computed from advisory signals, that let the platform observe trends, detect regressions, and enforce quality thresholds — without ever weakening the pass/fail floor.

A gate answers "is this admissible?" A score answers "how good is this?" The two questions are complementary and must never be confused. This section establishes that scores measure and thresholds enforce, but neither ever rescues a mandatory failure or replaces a mandatory check.

---

# Governing Principle

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **Scoring measures quality above the mandatory floor; it never lowers it. A high score never rescues a mandatory FAIL, and a score threshold is an additional gate, never a substitute for the mandatory checks.**

The relationship is strictly additive. The mandatory checks (7.1.4) establish an absolute floor of admissibility. Scoring adds a *further* condition on top of that floor for gates that use the `threshold_score` verdict function (7.1.5). A score can only make a gate stricter; it can never make it more lenient.

This is the measurement-layer expression of Principle 1 (quality is an admissibility condition) and Principle 9 (quality outranks throughput): the score is a lens for observing and raising quality, never a knob for relaxing it.

---

# Measurement vs Enforcement

The platform distinguishes measurement from enforcement.

```text
Measurement  → compute a quality score from advisory signals   (observe)
Enforcement  → block when the score falls below a threshold     (act)
```

Measurement is always safe: computing a score never changes a verdict. Enforcement is where a score acquires teeth — but only through the `threshold_score` verdict function (7.1.5), and only *in addition to* the mandatory checks.

A gate may measure without enforcing (advisory-influence gates, 7.1.6). A gate that enforces a score always also enforces its mandatory floor first.

---

# Where Scores Come From

Every quality score is derived from advisory checks and metrics already produced by the gates.

```text
Advisory checks (7.1.4)  ──► advisory results
Gate metrics    (7.1.8)  ──► measured values
        │
        ▼
Quality Score (7.3.3)
```

Scores are not a new source of judgment. They are a *reduction* of signals the gates already produce — the advisory check results and the measured metric values recorded in gate reports. A score introduces no rule the gates do not already evaluate; it aggregates existing advisory evidence into a single measured value.

This keeps scoring consistent with Principle 3 (enforce, do not author): scoring authors no rule, it reduces existing advisory evidence.

---

# The Three Measurement Guarantees

Quality measurement obeys three guarantees.

## Derived

Every score is a pure function of recorded advisory results and metrics. No score is authored, estimated, or entered by hand. Recomputing a score from the same evidence yields the same value.

---

## Subordinate

Every score is subordinate to the mandatory floor. A score is computed and enforced only *after* the mandatory checks pass. A gate whose mandatory checks fail has no meaningful score to consider — the verdict is already FAIL.

---

## Deterministic

Every score is deterministic. Given identical advisory evidence and identical scoring configuration, the score is identical. Scores are reproducible and auditable exactly as verdicts are (7.1.5).

---

# The Measurement Boundary

Scoring is bounded by two rules.

```text
Rule 1: A score never converts a mandatory FAIL into a PASS.
Rule 2: A score threshold never lowers below the mandatory floor.
```

Rule 1 protects the verdict: the mandatory checks are evaluated first, and if any fails, the gate fails regardless of score. Rule 2 protects the floor: a `threshold_score` gate passes only when *both* the mandatory checks pass *and* the score meets the threshold — the threshold can only add strictness.

Together these rules guarantee that scoring is a one-way ratchet toward higher quality: it can raise the bar, never lower it.

---

# Why Measure At All

If mandatory checks establish admissibility, why measure quality above them?

Three reasons.

* **Trend visibility.** A score reveals whether quality is rising or falling across builds, before a trend becomes a mandatory failure. Regression detection (7.3.5) depends on it.
* **Prioritized attention.** A score directs reviewers to the artifacts most in need of attention among many that all technically pass.
* **Graduated enforcement.** A `threshold_score` gate lets the platform require not merely admissibility but a minimum quality level for production builds, without hard-coding that level as a mandatory check.

Measurement gives the platform a continuous signal in a space that binary gates alone leave invisible: the range of quality *among* admissible artifacts.

---

# Scoring Never Replaces a Check

A score is never a substitute for a mandatory check.

```text
Wrong:  replace continuity_valid (mandatory) with a "continuity score >= 0.9"
Correct: keep continuity_valid mandatory; add a continuity quality score as advisory
```

A property that must hold absolutely is a mandatory check, evaluated as PASS/FAIL. A property that is a matter of degree is measured by a score. The platform never demotes an absolute requirement into a scored one, because a score admits partial satisfaction and an absolute requirement does not.

This is the boundary that keeps scoring honest: it measures degree where degree is meaningful, and it never dilutes a binary requirement into a gradient.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-901 — The Rescuing Score

Wrong:

```text
mandatory check FAILs, overall score 0.95 → gate PASSes
```

Correct:

```text
mandatory check FAILs → gate FAILs regardless of score
```

---

## AP-902 — The Demoted Requirement

Wrong:

```text
continuity_valid becomes "continuity score >= 0.9"
```

Correct:

```text
continuity_valid stays mandatory; a continuity score is added as advisory measurement
```

---

## AP-903 — The Authored Score

Wrong:

```text
reviewer types in a quality score of 0.8
```

Correct:

```text
score is computed from recorded advisory results and metrics
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant QMP-701

Quality scoring measures quality above the mandatory floor and never lowers it.

---

## Invariant QMP-702

A score never converts a mandatory FAIL into a PASS.

---

## Invariant QMP-703

A score threshold is an additional gate condition, never a substitute for mandatory checks.

---

## Invariant QMP-704

Every score is derived purely from recorded advisory results and metrics.

---

## Invariant QMP-705

Every score is subordinate to the mandatory floor and considered only after mandatory checks pass.

---

## Invariant QMP-706

Every score is deterministic given identical evidence and scoring configuration.

---

## Invariant QMP-707

Scoring authors no rule; it reduces existing advisory evidence.

---

## Invariant QMP-708

A score threshold never lowers the bar below the mandatory floor.

---

## Invariant QMP-709

An absolute requirement is a mandatory check, never a scored gradient.

---

## Invariant QMP-710

Measurement is always safe: computing a score never changes a verdict.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-938 | Scoring measures quality above the mandatory floor and never lowers it.              |
| ADR-939 | A high score never rescues a mandatory FAIL.                                         |
| ADR-940 | A score threshold is an additional condition, never a substitute for mandatory checks. |
| ADR-941 | Every score is derived from recorded advisory results and metrics.                   |
| ADR-942 | Scoring is subordinate to the mandatory floor.                                       |
| ADR-943 | Every score is deterministic and reproducible.                                       |
| ADR-944 | Scoring authors no rule; it reduces existing advisory evidence.                      |
| ADR-945 | An absolute requirement stays a mandatory check, never a scored gradient.            |
| ADR-946 | Measurement never changes a verdict; only enforcement, via threshold_score, acts.    |
| ADR-947 | Scores exist to give trend visibility, prioritized attention, and graduated enforcement. |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.3.1** is complete when:

* The measurement philosophy is defined, distinguishing measurement from enforcement.
* The strict subordination of scoring to the mandatory floor is established.
* The derivation of scores from advisory checks and metrics is defined.
* The three measurement guarantees — derived, subordinate, deterministic — are stated.
* The two measurement boundary rules are established.
* The rationale for measuring above the floor is given.
* The prohibition on demoting a mandatory check into a scored one is defined.
* Anti-patterns for rescuing scores, demoted requirements, and authored scores are documented.
* Invariants QMP-701 through QMP-710 and ADR-938 through ADR-947 are established.

---

# Part 7.3.2 — Quality Metric Model

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Quality Metric** — the atomic unit of quality measurement — and the model every metric obeys.

Section 7.3.1 established that scores are derived from metrics and advisory results. This section defines what a metric is: its identity, its source, its computation, and its value.

A metric is a single measured fact about an artifact or a gate evaluation. Everything the scoring system computes is built from metrics, exactly as everything a gate concludes is built from checks (7.1.4). This section defines the metric precisely enough that a score built on it is trustworthy.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A metric is a derived, deterministic measurement of one quantity. It is computed from recorded evidence, carries its provenance, and never authors judgment.**

Two commitments follow.

A metric is **derived**: it is a pure function of recorded evidence — gate check results, artifact fields, or other metrics. No metric is entered by hand.

A metric is **single-valued**: it measures exactly one quantity. A metric that measures two quantities is two metrics. Singularity is what lets a metric be composed into a score transparently.

---

# The Anatomy of a Metric

Every metric is composed of five parts.

```text
Metric
  ├── metric_id   (unique identity)
  ├── source      (the evidence it is computed from)
  ├── computation (the deterministic function)
  ├── value       (the measured result)
  └── range       (the valid value range)
```

* **metric_id** — the unique name of the metric.
* **source** — the recorded evidence the metric reads.
* **computation** — the deterministic function producing the value.
* **value** — the measured result.
* **range** — the valid range the value falls within.

A metric missing any part is malformed.

---

# The Metric Schema

Every metric is represented by the following canonical schema.

```json
{
  "metric_id": "storyboard_pacing_variance",
  "source": ["storyboard_quality_gate:advisory:pacing_variance"],
  "computation": "normalized_variance",
  "value": 0.18,
  "range": { "min": 0.0, "max": 1.0 },
  "direction": "lower_is_better"
}
```

The schema records the metric identity, the evidence it derives from, the computation applied, the measured value, the valid range, and the direction of goodness. The `direction` field states whether higher or lower values indicate better quality, so the scoring layer (7.3.3) can combine metrics correctly.

---

# Metric Categories

Metrics fall into a closed set of categories.

| Category      | Measures                                          | Example                          |
| ------------- | ------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------- |
| `structural`  | Well-formedness quality above the mandatory floor | field completeness ratio         |
| `fidelity`    | Faithfulness of a transformation                  | render-to-storyboard match score |
| `aesthetic`   | Measured visual/audio quality                     | visual quality, motion smoothness|
| `efficiency`  | Cost and resource quality                         | runway_ratio, cache hit ratio    |
| `narrative`   | Story and pacing quality                          | emotional arc intensity          |

Every metric declares its category. Categories let the scoring layer weight related metrics coherently and let dashboards (7.3.6) group them.

---

# Metric Direction

Every metric declares a direction of goodness.

```yaml
direction: higher_is_better    # e.g. visual_quality
direction: lower_is_better     # e.g. runway_ratio, pacing_variance
direction: target_band         # e.g. average_duration within a range
```

* `higher_is_better` — a larger value is better.
* `lower_is_better` — a smaller value is better.
* `target_band` — a value within a target band is best; deviation in either direction is worse.

Direction is what lets metrics of different natures be normalized into a comparable contribution (7.3.3). A metric with no declared direction cannot be scored.

---

# Metric Provenance

Every metric carries its provenance.

```json
"source": ["storyboard_quality_gate:advisory:pacing_variance"]
```

The `source` records exactly which recorded evidence the metric derives from — a gate, a check, an artifact field. Provenance makes a metric auditable: a reviewer can trace a metric's value back to the raw evidence that produced it, exactly as a check result traces to its evidence (7.1.4).

A metric whose source is unrecorded is not auditable, and the platform does not accept unauditable metrics.

---

# Metric Determinism

A metric is deterministic.

Given identical source evidence, a metric computes an identical value. Because gate evidence is deterministic (7.1.4) and metric computation is a pure function, a metric is reproducible across runs and machines. This is what allows a metric — and the score built on it — to be cached with the artifact identity (Part 6.2) and reproduced during audit.

---

# Metrics Are Recorded, Not Just Computed

Every metric is recorded in the gate report and the build quality record.

A computed metric that is not recorded cannot inform a trend (7.3.5) or a dashboard (7.3.6). Metrics are persisted with their artifact identity, so that a build's full quality picture — every metric, every value — is reconstructable after the fact. Metrics are first-class recorded data, exactly as gate reports are (7.1.8).

---

# The Metric Registry

Metrics are declared in a registry.

```text
metric_id
        │
        ▼
Metric Registry
        │
        ▼
category, source, computation, range, direction
```

The registry is the single source of truth for which metrics exist and how each is computed. A metric not in the registry is never computed or scored. This mirrors the Gate Registry (7.1.6): declared, discoverable, and closed.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-911 — The Hand-Entered Metric

Wrong:

```text
reviewer records visual_quality = 0.7 by judgment
```

Correct:

```text
visual_quality is computed from recorded render evidence
```

---

## AP-912 — The Directionless Metric

Wrong:

```text
metric value 0.4 with no direction of goodness
```

Correct:

```text
metric declares higher_is_better, lower_is_better, or target_band
```

---

## AP-913 — The Multi-Quantity Metric

Wrong:

```text
one metric bundles pacing and palette quality
```

Correct:

```text
two metrics: pacing_variance and palette_consistency
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant QMM-701

A metric measures exactly one quantity and is derived from recorded evidence.

---

## Invariant QMM-702

Every metric declares its identity, source, computation, value, and range.

---

## Invariant QMM-703

Every metric declares a category from the closed set.

---

## Invariant QMM-704

Every metric declares a direction of goodness.

---

## Invariant QMM-705

Every metric carries provenance tracing to the evidence it derives from.

---

## Invariant QMM-706

A metric is deterministic given identical source evidence.

---

## Invariant QMM-707

No metric is authored, estimated, or hand-entered.

---

## Invariant QMM-708

Every computed metric is recorded with its artifact identity.

---

## Invariant QMM-709

A metric not in the Metric Registry is never computed or scored.

---

## Invariant QMM-710

A metric with no declared direction cannot be scored.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-948 | A metric is the atomic unit of measurement and measures exactly one quantity.        |
| ADR-949 | Every metric is derived from recorded evidence, never hand-entered.                  |
| ADR-950 | Every metric declares identity, source, computation, value, and range.               |
| ADR-951 | Every metric declares a category from a closed set.                                 |
| ADR-952 | Every metric declares a direction of goodness.                                      |
| ADR-953 | Every metric carries provenance to the evidence it derives from.                     |
| ADR-954 | Every metric is deterministic and reproducible.                                     |
| ADR-955 | Every computed metric is recorded with its artifact identity.                        |
| ADR-956 | Metrics are declared in a registry; unregistered metrics are never computed.          |
| ADR-957 | A metric with no direction cannot be scored.                                         |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.3.2** is complete when:

* The five-part anatomy of a metric is defined.
* The canonical metric schema is specified with source, computation, range, and direction.
* The closed set of metric categories is defined.
* Metric direction of goodness is defined with three modes.
* Metric provenance, determinism, and recording are established.
* The Metric Registry is defined as the single source of truth.
* Anti-patterns for hand-entered, directionless, and multi-quantity metrics are documented.
* Invariants QMM-701 through QMM-710 and ADR-948 through ADR-957 are established.

---

# Part 7.3.3 — Quality Score Computation

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines how metrics are combined into a **Quality Score**, and the rules that keep the computation deterministic, auditable, and subordinate to the mandatory floor.

Section 7.3.2 defined the metric. This section defines the reduction from many metrics to one score, and how that score participates in the `threshold_score` verdict function (7.1.5).

A score is a single number that summarizes the measured quality of an artifact above its mandatory floor. This section defines exactly how that number is computed, so that a quality score carries the same reproducible, defensible meaning everywhere it is used.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A quality score is a deterministic, weighted reduction of normalized metrics. It summarizes quality above the mandatory floor; it is computed only after the mandatory checks pass, and it never alters them.**

Two commitments follow.

A score is **computed, not judged**: it is a pure function of normalized metric values and declared weights. There is no discretionary input.

A score is **floor-subordinate**: it is meaningful only for an artifact that has already passed its mandatory checks. For a mandatory-failed artifact, the verdict is already FAIL and the score is moot.

---

# The Score Computation Pipeline

A quality score is computed in four steps.

```text
Metrics (7.3.2)
        │
        ▼
1. Normalize    each metric to [0, 1] using its direction and range
        │
        ▼
2. Weight       apply the configured weight to each normalized metric
        │
        ▼
3. Aggregate    sum the weighted contributions
        │
        ▼
4. Bound        clamp the result to [0, 1]
        │
        ▼
Quality Score ∈ [0, 1]
```

Each step is deterministic. The same metrics under the same configuration always produce the same score.

---

# Step 1 — Normalization

Each metric is normalized to the interval [0, 1], where 1 is best.

```text
higher_is_better:  normalized = (value - min) / (max - min)
lower_is_better:   normalized = (max - value) / (max - min)
target_band:       normalized = 1 - (distance_from_band / max_distance)
```

Normalization uses the metric's declared direction and range (7.3.2). After normalization, every metric contributes on a common scale where 1 is best and 0 is worst, regardless of its native units or direction. A metric outside its declared range is clamped to the range before normalizing.

---

# Step 2 — Weighting

Each normalized metric is multiplied by its configured weight.

```yaml
weights:
  visual_quality: 0.30
  pacing_variance: 0.20
  palette_consistency: 0.15
  motion_smoothness: 0.20
  narration_clarity: 0.15
```

Weights are declared in the scoring configuration (7.1.11), are versioned, and are frozen for the build. Weights express the relative importance of each metric to the overall quality of the artifact. Weights sum to 1 across the metrics that contribute to a score.

---

# Step 3 — Aggregation

The weighted contributions are summed.

```text
score = Σ (normalized_metric × weight)
```

Because each normalized metric is in [0, 1] and the weights sum to 1, the aggregate is naturally in [0, 1]. The aggregation is a weighted mean of the normalized metrics — a single, interpretable number where 1 is perfect measured quality and 0 is worst.

---

# Step 4 — Bounding

The aggregate is clamped to [0, 1].

```text
score = clamp(aggregate, 0.0, 1.0)
```

Bounding guards against configuration errors (weights not summing to exactly 1) producing a score outside the valid interval. The bounded score is the final quality score.

---

# The Score Is Subordinate to the Floor

A quality score is computed only after the mandatory checks pass.

```text
Mandatory checks (7.1.4)
        │
        ├── any FAIL → verdict FAIL; score is not the deciding factor
        │
        └── all PASS → compute score → threshold_score verdict
```

For an artifact whose mandatory checks fail, the verdict is FAIL regardless of any score. The score becomes relevant only for artifacts that have cleared the mandatory floor, where the `threshold_score` function (7.1.5) adds the requirement that the score also meet the configured threshold.

The score never rescues a mandatory FAIL (QMP-702), and it never lowers the floor (QMP-708).

---

# The threshold_score Verdict, Precisely

For a gate using `threshold_score`:

```text
PASS ⟺ (every mandatory check is PASS or NOT_APPLICABLE)
       AND (quality_score >= configured_threshold)
```

Both conditions are required. The mandatory checks are a hard AND (as in every gate); the score threshold is an *additional* hard condition. A gate with a perfect score but a failed mandatory check is FAIL. A gate with all mandatory checks passing but a below-threshold score is also FAIL. The score can only make the gate stricter.

---

# Score Composition Across Gates

Per-gate scores compose into a build quality score.

```text
Per-check advisory results
        │
        ▼
Per-metric values (7.3.2)
        │
        ▼
Per-gate quality score (this section)
        │
        ▼
Per-stage quality score
        │
        ▼
Build quality score (7.3.6)
```

Each level is a weighted reduction of the level below, and each preserves drill-down (7.1.8): a build quality score can always be decomposed to the per-gate scores, the metrics, and the advisory evidence that produced it. Aggregation adds structure; it never loses provenance.

---

# Score Determinism and Recording

A quality score is deterministic and recorded.

Given identical metrics and identical frozen scoring configuration, the score is byte-identical. The score is recorded in the gate report (7.1.8) alongside the metrics and the configuration version that produced it, so the score is fully reproducible and auditable.

A score whose configuration is unknown is not reproducible; the platform records the configuration with every score.

---

# Worked Example

A gate with three contributing metrics.

```text
Metric              value   direction         normalized   weight   contribution
visual_quality      0.82    higher_is_better  0.82         0.50     0.410
pacing_variance     0.18    lower_is_better   0.82         0.30     0.246
palette_consistency 0.90    higher_is_better  0.90         0.20     0.180
                                                                    ───────
                                              quality_score        0.836
```

With a configured threshold of `0.80`, and assuming every mandatory check passed, the gate returns PASS: the mandatory floor is clear and `0.836 >= 0.80`. Had a single mandatory check failed, the gate would be FAIL regardless of the `0.836` score.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-921 — Scoring Before the Floor

Wrong:

```text
compute score first → if high, skip mandatory checks
```

Correct:

```text
mandatory checks first → compute score only for artifacts that clear the floor
```

---

## AP-922 — Unnormalized Aggregation

Wrong:

```text
sum raw metric values of different units into a "score"
```

Correct:

```text
normalize each metric to [0,1] by its direction and range, then weight and sum
```

---

## AP-923 — Unrecorded Configuration

Wrong:

```text
record the score but not the weights/threshold that produced it
```

Correct:

```text
record the score with its scoring configuration version
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant QSC-701

A quality score is a deterministic, weighted reduction of normalized metrics bounded to [0, 1].

---

## Invariant QSC-702

Each metric is normalized to [0, 1] using its declared direction and range before weighting.

---

## Invariant QSC-703

Weights are declared in frozen scoring configuration and sum to 1 across contributing metrics.

---

## Invariant QSC-704

A quality score is computed only after the mandatory checks pass.

---

## Invariant QSC-705

Under `threshold_score`, PASS requires both all mandatory checks passing and the score meeting the threshold.

---

## Invariant QSC-706

A score never rescues a mandatory FAIL and never lowers the mandatory floor.

---

## Invariant QSC-707

Per-gate scores compose into stage and build scores while preserving drill-down.

---

## Invariant QSC-708

A quality score is deterministic given identical metrics and frozen configuration.

---

## Invariant QSC-709

Every score is recorded with the scoring configuration version that produced it.

---

## Invariant QSC-710

A score computed from unnormalized or directionless metrics is invalid.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-958 | A quality score is a deterministic, weighted reduction of normalized metrics.        |
| ADR-959 | Metrics are normalized to [0,1] by direction and range before weighting.             |
| ADR-960 | Weights are frozen configuration and sum to 1 across contributing metrics.            |
| ADR-961 | A score is computed only after the mandatory checks pass.                            |
| ADR-962 | Under threshold_score, PASS requires mandatory checks passing AND score ≥ threshold.  |
| ADR-963 | A score never rescues a mandatory FAIL and never lowers the floor.                    |
| ADR-964 | Per-gate scores compose into stage and build scores with full drill-down.            |
| ADR-965 | A quality score is deterministic and reproducible.                                   |
| ADR-966 | Every score is recorded with its scoring configuration version.                      |
| ADR-967 | Scores are computed from normalized, directional metrics only.                       |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.3.3** is complete when:

* The four-step score computation pipeline — normalize, weight, aggregate, bound — is defined.
* Normalization by direction and range is specified.
* Weighting from frozen configuration summing to 1 is defined.
* The subordination of the score to the mandatory floor is established.
* The `threshold_score` verdict is stated precisely as a conjunction of floor and threshold.
* Score composition across gates preserving drill-down is defined.
* Score determinism and configuration recording are established.
* A worked example is provided.
* Anti-patterns for scoring-before-floor, unnormalized aggregation, and unrecorded configuration are documented.
* Invariants QSC-701 through QSC-710 and ADR-958 through ADR-967 are established.

---

# Part 7.3.4 — Thresholds, Tolerances & Score Profiles

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **thresholds**, **tolerances**, and **score profiles** that govern how quality scores are enforced, and the rules that keep them immutable within a build and subordinate to the mandatory floor.

Section 7.3.3 defined how a score is computed. This section defines the bars a score is measured against: the minimum score a `threshold_score` gate requires, the tolerances that permit measured deviation, and how these vary by build profile without ever weakening the mandatory floor.

A score is only actionable against a threshold. This section defines those thresholds as versioned, frozen configuration — the same discipline the gate configuration architecture (7.1.11) applies to mandatory limits.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **Score thresholds and tolerances are declarative, versioned, and frozen for a build. They may rise with build stringency but never lower the mandatory floor, and they are never tuned in-build to rescue a failing artifact.**

Thresholds are the enforcement bars for scores. They obey exactly the configuration discipline of 7.1.11: declared, hierarchical, resolved once, frozen, and profile-varying only above the mandatory floor.

---

# Score Thresholds

A score threshold is the minimum quality score a `threshold_score` gate requires.

```yaml
score_threshold:
  gate: storyboard_quality_gate
  minimum_score: 0.85
  profile: production
```

A gate using `threshold_score` (7.1.5) passes only when its quality score meets or exceeds `minimum_score` — in addition to every mandatory check passing (7.3.3). The threshold is an additional gate condition; it can only add strictness.

A threshold is never set below the level at which a mandatory check would already have failed. The threshold operates strictly in the space above the mandatory floor.

---

# Tolerances

A tolerance is a permitted deviation for a continuous measured value.

```yaml
tolerances:
  duration_seconds: 0.25          # asset duration may deviate 0.25s from plan
  audio_sync_ms: 40               # audio may drift up to 40ms
  loudness_lufs: 1.0              # loudness may deviate 1.0 LUFS from target
```

A tolerance defines the band within which a measured value is considered conformant. A value within tolerance passes the relevant check; a value outside tolerance fails it.

Tolerances belong to the mandatory checks they parameterize — a duration outside tolerance fails `duration_conformance` (7.2.6), a hard mandatory FAIL. A tolerance is never widened in-build to admit a non-conformant value; that would be an in-build mandatory relaxation, which is prohibited (7.1.11).

---

# Score Profiles

Score thresholds vary by build profile, above the mandatory floor.

| Profile       | Score posture                                        |
| ------------- | ---------------------------------------------------- |
| `development` | Low or no score threshold; fast iteration.           |
| `preview`     | Moderate score threshold; structural validation.     |
| `production`  | High score threshold; shippable quality.             |
| `benchmark`   | Fixed score threshold; reproducible measurement.     |

A profile may raise or relax a *score* threshold, but it never changes a *mandatory* check or a mandatory tolerance. A development build may set a low score threshold to iterate quickly; a production build sets a high one. Both enforce the identical mandatory floor (7.1.11, GC-705).

---

# The Mandatory Floor Is Threshold-Invariant

No score threshold or tolerance profile relaxes a mandatory check.

```text
mandatory checks + mandatory tolerances → identical across all profiles
score thresholds                        → may vary by profile, above the floor
advisory tolerances                     → may vary by profile
```

A production build and a development build differ in score strictness, never in mandatory admissibility. This preserves the guarantee that a PASS means the same mandatory thing everywhere, while allowing the *scored* quality bar to scale with the build's purpose.

A configuration that lowered a mandatory tolerance under any profile to pass an artifact is invalid and rejected (7.1.11).

---

# Threshold Resolution and Freezing

Score thresholds and tolerances are resolved once and frozen, exactly as gate configuration (7.1.11).

```text
Build starts
        │
        ▼
Resolve score thresholds and tolerances (defaults → profile → build)
        │
        ▼
Validate (no mandatory relaxation)
        │
        ▼
Freeze into the Build Score Configuration Snapshot
```

Every gate reads its score threshold and tolerances from the frozen snapshot. No threshold or tolerance changes after freezing. An artifact that fails a frozen threshold is corrected, or the build proceeds under a recorded waiver (7.1.10) if the threshold is waivable — the threshold is never lowered in place.

---

# Threshold Versioning and Recording

Thresholds and tolerances are versioned and recorded.

A change to a threshold or tolerance produces a new configuration version; the prior version is retained. A build records the score configuration version it ran under, and every gate report records the threshold it evaluated against, so a scored verdict is fully reproducible (7.3.3).

A scored verdict whose threshold is unknown is not reproducible; the platform records the threshold with every scored verdict.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-931 — In-Build Threshold Lowering

Wrong:

```text
score 0.82 fails threshold 0.85 → lower threshold to 0.80 mid-build
```

Correct:

```text
threshold is frozen; improve the artifact, or record a waiver if permitted
```

---

## AP-932 — Widening a Mandatory Tolerance

Wrong:

```text
audio drifts 60ms past 40ms tolerance → widen tolerance to 60ms to pass
```

Correct:

```text
mandatory tolerance is frozen; re-sync the audio
```

---

## AP-933 — Profile Relaxing the Floor

Wrong:

```text
development profile disables a mandatory duration_conformance tolerance
```

Correct:

```text
mandatory floor is profile-invariant; only score thresholds and advisory tolerances vary
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant QTT-701

A score threshold is the minimum quality score a `threshold_score` gate requires, above the mandatory floor.

---

## Invariant QTT-702

A tolerance defines a permitted deviation band for a continuous measured value.

---

## Invariant QTT-703

Score thresholds and tolerances are declarative, versioned configuration.

---

## Invariant QTT-704

Score thresholds and tolerances are resolved once and frozen for the build.

---

## Invariant QTT-705

No score threshold or tolerance profile relaxes a mandatory check or a mandatory tolerance.

---

## Invariant QTT-706

Score thresholds may vary by build profile only above the mandatory floor.

---

## Invariant QTT-707

A mandatory tolerance is never widened in-build to admit a non-conformant value.

---

## Invariant QTT-708

A score threshold is never lowered in-build to rescue a failing artifact.

---

## Invariant QTT-709

Thresholds and tolerances are versioned; a scored verdict records the threshold it evaluated against.

---

## Invariant QTT-710

A configuration that relaxes a mandatory tolerance under any profile is invalid and rejected.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-968 | Score thresholds enforce a minimum quality score above the mandatory floor.          |
| ADR-969 | Tolerances define permitted deviation bands for continuous values.                   |
| ADR-970 | Thresholds and tolerances are declarative, versioned configuration.                  |
| ADR-971 | Thresholds and tolerances are resolved once and frozen for the build.                |
| ADR-972 | No profile relaxes a mandatory check or mandatory tolerance.                          |
| ADR-973 | Score thresholds vary by profile only above the mandatory floor.                     |
| ADR-974 | Mandatory tolerances are never widened in-build.                                     |
| ADR-975 | Score thresholds are never lowered in-build to rescue an artifact.                   |
| ADR-976 | Thresholds are versioned and recorded with every scored verdict.                     |
| ADR-977 | A configuration relaxing a mandatory tolerance under any profile is rejected.         |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.3.4** is complete when:

* Score thresholds are defined as the minimum score a `threshold_score` gate requires above the floor.
* Tolerances are defined as permitted deviation bands and tied to their mandatory checks.
* Score profiles are defined and the mandatory floor is established as threshold-invariant.
* Threshold and tolerance resolution and freezing are defined, mirroring 7.1.11.
* Threshold versioning and recording with scored verdicts are established.
* Anti-patterns for in-build lowering, tolerance widening, and floor relaxation are documented.
* Invariants QTT-701 through QTT-710 and ADR-968 through ADR-977 are established.

---

# Part 7.3.5 — Regression Detection

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines **regression detection**: how the platform compares quality across builds to detect a decline before it becomes a failure.

Sections 7.3.1 through 7.3.4 measured and scored the quality of a single build. This section adds the temporal dimension: comparing a build's quality metrics and scores against a baseline to detect regression — a statistically meaningful decline in a metric that still technically passes.

A regression is a warning, not yet a failure. A metric that drops from 0.92 to 0.83 may still clear its threshold, but the trend is the early signal of an emerging defect. Regression detection surfaces that signal while the decline is still cheap to reverse — the cost-of-defect curve (7.1.2) applied across time rather than across stages.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A quality decline against a baseline is detected and surfaced even when the current build still passes. Regression detection is deterministic, baseline-relative, and advisory by default — it warns, and it escalates to blocking only where configured.**

Two commitments follow.

Regression detection is **baseline-relative**: it compares a build against a defined baseline, not against an absolute standard. A decline is meaningful relative to where quality was.

Regression detection is **advisory by default**: a detected regression is recorded and surfaced, but does not by itself block a build unless a gate is configured to treat that regression as blocking.

---

# The Baseline

Regression is measured against a defined baseline.

```yaml
baseline:
  type: last_passing_production   # last_passing_production | pinned_build | rolling_average
  build_ref: build-2026-07-13-004
  metrics_snapshot: { ... }
```

The baseline is a recorded set of metric values and scores from a reference build. The platform supports three baseline types:

* `last_passing_production` — the most recent production build that passed.
* `pinned_build` — a specific build pinned as the quality reference.
* `rolling_average` — a moving average over recent passing builds.

The baseline is explicit and recorded, so a regression verdict is reproducible: the same current build against the same baseline yields the same regression result.

---

# Regression Computation

A regression is a decline in a metric beyond a configured sensitivity.

```text
delta = baseline_value_normalized − current_value_normalized

regression ⟺ delta > regression_sensitivity
```

The comparison uses normalized metric values (7.3.3), so metrics of different natures are compared on a common scale. A decline larger than the configured `regression_sensitivity` is flagged as a regression. A decline within sensitivity is noise, not a regression.

Regression is computed per metric and per score, deterministically, from recorded values.

---

# Regression Is Detected Even on a Passing Build

A build can pass every gate and still exhibit a regression.

```text
Current build: all gates PASS, storyboard score 0.83
Baseline:       storyboard score 0.92
Delta:          0.09 > sensitivity 0.05
        │
        ▼
Regression detected and surfaced (build still PASSes)
```

This is the point of regression detection: it catches quality erosion that has not yet crossed a threshold into failure. The build passes because 0.83 clears its threshold, but the 0.09 drop against baseline is recorded as a regression and surfaced to reviewers and the dashboard (7.3.6).

---

# Advisory by Default, Blocking by Configuration

A regression is advisory unless a gate is configured to treat it as blocking.

```text
Default:     regression → recorded + surfaced, non-blocking
Configured:  regression on a critical metric → escalates to a blocking check
```

By default a regression informs; it does not block. A gate may, by configuration, promote a regression on a designated critical metric to a blocking check — for example, a fidelity regression on a production build. When promoted, the regression becomes a mandatory check that fails closed like any other (7.1.5). The promotion is declared in configuration and versioned; it is never applied ad hoc.

---

# Regression Direction Respects Metric Direction

Regression respects each metric's declared direction (7.3.2).

```text
higher_is_better metric:  regression = a decrease beyond sensitivity
lower_is_better metric:   regression = an increase beyond sensitivity
target_band metric:       regression = increased deviation from the band
```

A rising `runway_ratio` (lower_is_better) is a regression; a rising `visual_quality` (higher_is_better) is an improvement. Because normalization already maps every metric to "1 is best" (7.3.3), a regression is uniformly a decline in normalized value — but the recorded delta references the metric's native direction for interpretability.

---

# Regression Report

Regression detection emits a report.

```yaml
regression_report:
  build_id:
  baseline_ref:
  regressions:
    - metric: storyboard_quality_score
      baseline: 0.92
      current: 0.83
      delta: 0.09
      sensitivity: 0.05
      blocking: false
  improvements:
    - metric: runway_ratio
      baseline: 0.48
      current: 0.41
      delta: -0.07
  verdict_impact: none
```

The report records every regression and every improvement against baseline, whether each regression is blocking, and its impact on the build verdict. It records improvements as well as regressions, so the quality trend is visible in both directions.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-941 — Ignoring a Passing Regression

Wrong:

```text
build passes → ignore the 0.09 quality drop against baseline
```

Correct:

```text
regression surfaced even though the build passes
```

---

## AP-942 — Absolute-Only Comparison

Wrong:

```text
compare current score only to its threshold, never to the baseline
```

Correct:

```text
compare to threshold (enforcement) AND to baseline (regression)
```

---

## AP-943 — Ad Hoc Blocking Escalation

Wrong:

```text
operator decides mid-build to block on a regression
```

Correct:

```text
blocking escalation is declared in versioned configuration, not decided ad hoc
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant QRD-701

Regression detection compares a build against a defined, recorded baseline.

---

## Invariant QRD-702

The baseline is one of last-passing-production, pinned-build, or rolling-average, and is recorded.

---

## Invariant QRD-703

A regression is a decline in a normalized metric beyond a configured sensitivity.

---

## Invariant QRD-704

Regression is detected and surfaced even when the current build passes every gate.

---

## Invariant QRD-705

A regression is advisory by default and blocking only where declared in versioned configuration.

---

## Invariant QRD-706

A promoted blocking regression fails closed like any mandatory check.

---

## Invariant QRD-707

Regression respects each metric's declared direction of goodness.

---

## Invariant QRD-708

Regression detection is deterministic given the same current build and baseline.

---

## Invariant QRD-709

The regression report records regressions, improvements, and their verdict impact.

---

## Invariant QRD-710

Blocking escalation of a regression is never decided ad hoc in-build.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-978 | Regression detection compares a build against a defined, recorded baseline.          |
| ADR-979 | Baselines are last-passing-production, pinned-build, or rolling-average.              |
| ADR-980 | A regression is a normalized decline beyond a configured sensitivity.                 |
| ADR-981 | Regressions are detected even on builds that pass every gate.                         |
| ADR-982 | Regressions are advisory by default and blocking only where configured.               |
| ADR-983 | A promoted blocking regression fails closed like any mandatory check.                |
| ADR-984 | Regression respects each metric's declared direction.                                |
| ADR-985 | Regression detection is deterministic.                                               |
| ADR-986 | The regression report records regressions, improvements, and verdict impact.          |
| ADR-987 | Blocking escalation of a regression is declared in versioned configuration, not ad hoc. |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.3.5** is complete when:

* Regression detection is defined as baseline-relative comparison across builds.
* The three baseline types are defined and required to be recorded.
* Regression computation from normalized deltas against a sensitivity is specified.
* Detection of regressions on passing builds is established.
* Advisory-by-default with configured blocking escalation is defined and fails closed when promoted.
* Regression's respect for metric direction is defined.
* The regression report recording regressions and improvements is specified.
* Anti-patterns for ignoring passing regressions, absolute-only comparison, and ad hoc escalation are documented.
* Invariants QRD-701 through QRD-710 and ADR-978 through ADR-987 are established.

---

# Part 7.3.6 — Quality Dashboard & Reporting

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **Build Quality Report** and the **Quality Dashboard**: how per-gate metrics, scores, and regressions are aggregated into a build-level picture and surfaced to operators, without losing traceability to the underlying evidence.

Sections 7.3.2 through 7.3.5 produced metrics, scores, and regressions per gate. This section aggregates them into a single, drill-downable quality view for a build, and defines how that view is presented.

A dashboard is only useful if it is faithful: every number it shows must trace to the evidence that produced it. This section defines the aggregation as structure-adding and provenance-preserving, never as summary that discards attribution.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **The Build Quality Report aggregates every gate's metrics, scores, and regressions into one view, and every aggregated number drills down to the check-level evidence that produced it. Aggregation adds structure; it never discards provenance.**

The dashboard is a rendering of the Build Quality Report. It is observation, never enforcement: viewing a dashboard changes no verdict.

---

# The Build Quality Report

The Build Quality Report is the aggregate quality record of a build.

```json
{
  "build_id": "build-2026-07-20-001",
  "build_quality_score": 0.87,
  "verdict": "PASS",
  "gates": [
    { "gate": "story_quality_gate",      "verdict": "PASS", "score": 0.91 },
    { "gate": "shot_quality_gate",       "verdict": "PASS", "score": 0.88 },
    { "gate": "storyboard_quality_gate", "verdict": "PASS", "score": 0.83, "regression": true }
  ],
  "regressions": [
    { "metric": "storyboard_quality_score", "baseline": 0.92, "current": 0.83, "blocking": false }
  ],
  "config_versions": { "gate": "2.0", "score": "2.0" },
  "chain_report_ref": "chain-build-2026-07-20-001"
}
```

The report records the build's aggregate quality score, its overall verdict, each gate's verdict and score, any regressions, the configuration versions, and a reference to the chain report (7.1.7). It is the single quality artifact for the build.

---

# Aggregation Preserves Drill-Down

Every aggregated number decomposes to its underlying evidence.

```text
Build Quality Score
        │  drills down to
        ▼
Per-gate scores
        │  drills down to
        ▼
Per-metric values
        │  drills down to
        ▼
Advisory check results + evidence
```

The build quality score can always be decomposed to the per-gate scores, the metrics, and the advisory evidence that produced it (7.1.8). No level of aggregation loses the levels below it. A reviewer seeing a low build score can drill straight to the specific check evidence responsible.

Aggregation that lost drill-down would produce a number no one could explain, and the platform does not accept unexplainable numbers.

---

# The Quality Dashboard

The Quality Dashboard is a rendering of the Build Quality Report.

The dashboard presents, for a build or across builds:

* the build quality score and verdict;
* per-gate verdicts and scores;
* regressions and improvements against baseline;
* trends across recent builds;
* drill-down from any number to its underlying evidence.

The dashboard is a view, not an authority. It renders recorded data (7.1.8, GR-710) and never computes a new verdict. Interacting with the dashboard — filtering, drilling down, comparing — changes no build's verdict.

---

# The Dashboard Is Observation, Not Enforcement

Viewing the dashboard never changes a verdict.

```text
Dashboard  → renders recorded verdicts, scores, regressions   (observe)
Gates      → produce verdicts                                 (enforce)
```

Enforcement lives exclusively in the gates (7.3.7). The dashboard surfaces what the gates decided; it never decides. This separation keeps the dashboard safe to expose widely: it is a window onto quality, not a control over it.

---

# Trend Presentation

The dashboard presents quality trends across builds.

```text
build quality score

  1.0 │        ●───●
      │   ●───●        ●
      │              ●───●  ← regression surfaced here
  0.0 │
      └──────────────────────► builds over time
```

Trends make regressions visible before they become failures, applying the temporal cost-of-defect logic of 7.3.5. A downward trend that has not yet crossed a threshold is the earliest actionable quality signal, and the dashboard is where it becomes visible.

---

# Dashboard Data Is Recorded, Not Live-Computed

The dashboard renders recorded report data, not freshly recomputed judgments.

Every number the dashboard shows was computed by a gate, recorded in a report, and retained (7.1.8). The dashboard reads these records; it does not re-run gates or re-derive scores. This guarantees the dashboard shows exactly what the gates decided, reproducibly, and that the dashboard cannot disagree with the reports it renders.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-951 — The Un-Drillable Summary

Wrong:

```text
dashboard shows a build score of 0.7 with no way to see why
```

Correct:

```text
every number drills down to its gate, metric, and check evidence
```

---

## AP-952 — The Enforcing Dashboard

Wrong:

```text
operator marks a build failed from the dashboard
```

Correct:

```text
dashboard observes; only gates enforce
```

---

## AP-953 — Live Re-Computation

Wrong:

```text
dashboard re-runs gates to display "current" quality
```

Correct:

```text
dashboard renders recorded report data
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant QDB-701

The Build Quality Report aggregates every gate's verdicts, scores, and regressions for a build.

---

## Invariant QDB-702

Every aggregated number drills down to the check-level evidence that produced it.

---

## Invariant QDB-703

Aggregation adds structure and never discards provenance.

---

## Invariant QDB-704

The Quality Dashboard is a rendering of the Build Quality Report.

---

## Invariant QDB-705

The dashboard is observation only; viewing it changes no verdict.

---

## Invariant QDB-706

Enforcement lives exclusively in the gates, never in the dashboard.

---

## Invariant QDB-707

The dashboard renders recorded report data and never re-runs gates or re-derives scores.

---

## Invariant QDB-708

The Build Quality Report records configuration versions and references the chain report.

---

## Invariant QDB-709

The dashboard presents trends that surface regressions before they become failures.

---

## Invariant QDB-710

The dashboard cannot disagree with the reports it renders.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-988 | The Build Quality Report aggregates gate verdicts, scores, and regressions.          |
| ADR-989 | Every aggregated number drills down to check-level evidence.                         |
| ADR-990 | Aggregation preserves provenance and never discards it.                              |
| ADR-991 | The Quality Dashboard renders the Build Quality Report.                              |
| ADR-992 | The dashboard is observation only and changes no verdict.                            |
| ADR-993 | Enforcement lives in the gates, never in the dashboard.                              |
| ADR-994 | The dashboard renders recorded data and never re-runs gates.                         |
| ADR-995 | The Build Quality Report records config versions and the chain report reference.      |
| ADR-996 | The dashboard presents trends that surface regressions early.                        |
| ADR-997 | The dashboard cannot disagree with the reports it renders.                           |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.3.6** is complete when:

* The Build Quality Report is specified as the aggregate quality record of a build.
* Drill-down from any aggregated number to check-level evidence is established.
* The Quality Dashboard is defined as a rendering of the report.
* The dashboard is established as observation only, never enforcement.
* Trend presentation surfacing early regressions is defined.
* The dashboard is shown to render recorded data, never re-computing verdicts.
* Anti-patterns for un-drillable summaries, enforcing dashboards, and live re-computation are documented.
* Invariants QDB-701 through QDB-710 and ADR-988 through ADR-997 are established.

# Part 7.3.7 — Enforcement & Blocking Model

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section defines the **enforcement model** of quality scores: precisely how and where a score acquires the power to block a build, and the strict limits on that power.

Sections 7.3.1 through 7.3.6 measured, scored, tracked, and surfaced quality. This section defines the one place a score becomes enforcement: the `threshold_score` verdict function (7.1.5) and configured blocking regressions (7.3.5). It also defines the limits that keep scored enforcement subordinate to the mandatory floor.

Enforcement is where measurement acquires consequence. This section makes that consequence precise, bounded, and always secondary to the mandatory checks.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **A score blocks a build only through a declared `threshold_score` gate or a configured blocking regression, always in addition to the mandatory floor. Scored enforcement is fail-closed, governed, and never able to lower or bypass a mandatory check.**

Enforcement obeys the same fail-closed and governance discipline as the mandatory checks. A scored gate is stricter than a mandatory-only gate, never more lenient.

---

# The Two Enforcement Paths

A score can block a build through exactly two paths.

```text
Path 1: threshold_score gate    → score < threshold AND mandatory checks pass → FAIL
Path 2: blocking regression     → configured critical regression detected     → FAIL
```

Both paths are declared in versioned configuration. There is no third path. A score never blocks a build ad hoc, and a gate not configured for scored enforcement is never blocked by a score.

---

# Path 1 — The threshold_score Gate

A `threshold_score` gate blocks when the score falls below its threshold, on top of the mandatory floor.

```text
mandatory checks all PASS?
   │ no  → FAIL (mandatory, score irrelevant)
   │ yes
   ▼
score >= threshold?
   │ no  → FAIL (scored)
   │ yes → PASS
```

The mandatory checks are evaluated first and are decisive on failure. Only for an artifact that clears the mandatory floor does the score threshold apply. A scored FAIL is therefore always an artifact that was mandatory-admissible but did not meet the required quality level.

---

# Path 2 — The Blocking Regression

A configured blocking regression blocks when a critical metric regresses beyond sensitivity.

```text
critical metric regresses beyond sensitivity?
   │ yes AND configured blocking → FAIL (regression)
   │ otherwise                   → recorded, non-blocking
```

A blocking regression is a promoted regression check (7.3.5, QRD-705). It fails closed like any mandatory check once promoted. Promotion is declared in versioned configuration; it is never applied in-build ad hoc.

---

# Scored Enforcement Is Fail-Closed

A scored enforcement failure is fail-closed exactly as a mandatory failure.

```text
score cannot be computed (missing metric)        → FAIL
scoring configuration unresolvable               → FAIL
threshold cannot be resolved                     → FAIL
```

An undeterminable score is treated as a failure, never as a pass. This applies the fail-closed model (7.1.5) to scored enforcement: absence and error resolve to FAIL, so a scored gate cannot be bypassed by inducing a scoring error.

---

# Scored Enforcement Cannot Lower the Floor

Scored enforcement only ever adds strictness.

```text
mandatory-only gate:   PASS ⟺ mandatory checks pass
threshold_score gate:  PASS ⟺ mandatory checks pass AND score >= threshold
```

The `threshold_score` gate's pass condition is a strict superset of the mandatory-only condition's requirements. Every artifact that fails the mandatory-only gate also fails the scored gate; some artifacts that pass the mandatory-only gate fail the scored gate. Scored enforcement can only make a gate harder to pass, never easier (QMP-703, QMP-708).

---

# Scored Enforcement Is Governed

A scored blocking failure is subject to the same governance as any gate failure.

A scored FAIL is a FAIL: it blocks the build, records a report, and may be waived only by the Waiver Authority (7.1.10) if the scored check is waivable. A score threshold may be waived by governance for a specific artifact with justification and expiry; a mandatory check underlying the gate remains non-waivable if so designated. Waiving a score threshold never waives the mandatory floor beneath it.

---

# Enforcement Recording

Every scored enforcement decision is recorded.

A scored FAIL records, in the gate report (7.1.8), the score, the threshold, the metrics that produced the score, and the configuration version. A blocking regression records the metric, the baseline, the delta, and the sensitivity. Every scored enforcement decision is as traceable and reproducible as a mandatory decision.

---

# Anti-Patterns

## AP-961 — Scored Bypass of the Floor

Wrong:

```text
high score → skip a failing mandatory check → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
mandatory checks decisive; score applies only above the floor
```

---

## AP-962 — Ad Hoc Score Blocking

Wrong:

```text
operator blocks a build on a low score with no threshold_score gate configured
```

Correct:

```text
score blocks only through a declared threshold_score gate or configured blocking regression
```

---

## AP-963 — Scoring-Error Bypass

Wrong:

```text
score cannot be computed → skip the scored gate → PASS
```

Correct:

```text
uncomputable score → FAIL (fail-closed)
```

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant QEN-701

A score blocks a build only through a declared `threshold_score` gate or a configured blocking regression.

---

## Invariant QEN-702

Scored enforcement always applies in addition to the mandatory floor, never instead of it.

---

## Invariant QEN-703

A `threshold_score` gate evaluates mandatory checks first; a mandatory FAIL is decisive.

---

## Invariant QEN-704

A blocking regression is a promoted regression check declared in versioned configuration.

---

## Invariant QEN-705

Scored enforcement is fail-closed: an uncomputable score or unresolvable threshold resolves to FAIL.

---

## Invariant QEN-706

The `threshold_score` pass condition is a strict superset of the mandatory-only condition; scoring only adds strictness.

---

## Invariant QEN-707

A scored FAIL is a FAIL: it blocks, reports, and is waivable only per governance.

---

## Invariant QEN-708

Waiving a score threshold never waives the mandatory floor beneath it.

---

## Invariant QEN-709

Every scored enforcement decision records the score, threshold, metrics, and configuration version.

---

## Invariant QEN-710

A score never blocks a build ad hoc; enforcement is always declared in versioned configuration.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR     | Decision                                                                            |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-998  | A score blocks only through a declared threshold_score gate or configured blocking regression. |
| ADR-999  | Scored enforcement always applies in addition to the mandatory floor.               |
| ADR-1000 | A threshold_score gate evaluates mandatory checks first; a mandatory FAIL is decisive. |
| ADR-1001 | A blocking regression is a promoted regression check in versioned configuration.     |
| ADR-1002 | Scored enforcement is fail-closed on uncomputable scores.                           |
| ADR-1003 | The threshold_score pass condition is a strict superset; scoring only adds strictness.|
| ADR-1004 | A scored FAIL blocks, reports, and is waivable only per governance.                  |
| ADR-1005 | Waiving a score threshold never waives the mandatory floor.                         |
| ADR-1006 | Every scored enforcement decision is recorded and reproducible.                      |
| ADR-1007 | Scores never block ad hoc; enforcement is declared in versioned configuration.        |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.3.7** is complete when:

* The two enforcement paths — `threshold_score` gate and configured blocking regression — are defined as the only ways a score blocks.
* The `threshold_score` evaluation order, mandatory-first, is specified.
* The blocking regression path is defined as a promoted, versioned-configuration check.
* Scored enforcement is established as fail-closed.
* Scored enforcement is shown to only add strictness, never lower the floor.
* Governance and recording of scored enforcement are established.
* Anti-patterns for scored bypass, ad hoc blocking, and scoring-error bypass are documented.
* Invariants QEN-701 through QEN-710 and ADR-998 through ADR-1007 are established.

# Part 7.3.8 — Section Acceptance & Transition

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section closes **Section 7.3 — Quality Metrics, Scoring & Enforcement** and defines the transition to Section 7.4.

Sections 7.3.1 through 7.3.7 defined how the platform measures quality, computes scores, sets thresholds, detects regressions, surfaces a dashboard, and enforces scores. This section confirms the measurement layer is complete and coherent, and hands forward to human approval.

---

# Section 7.3 Overview

Section 7.3 established the measurement and scoring layer.

```text
7.3.1 → Purpose & Measurement Philosophy
7.3.2 → Quality Metric Model
7.3.3 → Quality Score Computation
7.3.4 → Thresholds, Tolerances & Score Profiles
7.3.5 → Regression Detection
7.3.6 → Quality Dashboard & Reporting
7.3.7 → Enforcement & Blocking Model
7.3.8 → Section Acceptance & Transition
```

Together these define a measurement layer that observes and enforces quality above the mandatory floor, without ever weakening it.

---

# The Central Guarantee

Section 7.3 rests on one guarantee, restated for emphasis.

> **Scoring measures and enforces quality above the mandatory floor. It never rescues a mandatory FAIL, never lowers a mandatory check, and never blocks a build except through declared, versioned configuration.**

Every subsection of 7.3 is subordinate to this guarantee. Metrics measure, scores summarize, thresholds enforce, regressions warn, dashboards observe, and enforcement acts — all strictly above the mandatory floor established in 7.1 and 7.2.

---

# Consolidated Section Invariants

## Invariant SAT73-701

Quality measurement and scoring operate strictly above the mandatory floor.

---

## Invariant SAT73-702

Every metric and score is derived, deterministic, and recorded with its provenance and configuration.

---

## Invariant SAT73-703

A score never rescues a mandatory FAIL and never lowers a mandatory check.

---

## Invariant SAT73-704

Regressions are detected against a recorded baseline and surfaced even on passing builds.

---

## Invariant SAT73-705

The dashboard observes and never enforces; enforcement lives in the gates.

---

## Invariant SAT73-706

A score blocks only through a declared `threshold_score` gate or configured blocking regression, and is fail-closed.

---

## Invariant SAT73-707

Every scored enforcement decision is governed, recorded, and reproducible.

---

## Invariant SAT73-708

The measurement layer never weakens the admissibility guarantees of Sections 7.1 and 7.2.

```text
        │

```

Section 7.3 defined how the platform *measures* quality mechanically. Section 7.4 defines where *human judgment* enters: the editorial approvals that the Publication Gate (7.2.10) requires, the approval state model, and the audit trail that records who approved what.

Section 7.4 builds on the `human-approval` judgment type (7.1.6), the governance and waiver model (7.1.10), and the scores and dashboards of 7.3 that inform human reviewers. It may not weaken any mandatory check or scored enforcement defined earlier.

Throughout, scoring measures and enforces quality above the floor and never weakens it.

Mechanical measurement is established. Human approval follows in Section 7.4.
