# Part 7.5.3 — Traceability Matrix

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section presents the **traceability matrix** that maps Part 7's quality gates to the sections whose rules they enforce, across the whole specification.

Part 7 enforces rules it does not author (Guarantee G7-03). This section makes the enforcement-to-authorship mapping explicit and complete, so that every check in every gate can be traced to the section that owns its rule, and every owning section can be traced to the gates that enforce it.

Traceability is what makes the quality architecture auditable end to end. This matrix is the index.

---

# Design Philosophy

The platform adopts the following principle.

> **Every check traces to an owning section, and every owning section traces to the gates that enforce it. The mapping is complete and bidirectional: no check is ownerless, and no rule critical to quality is unenforced.**

The matrix is the concrete artifact of Guarantee G7-03 (enforce, not author) and Guarantee G7-06 (traceability). It closes the loop between the sections that define rules and the gates that enforce them.

---

# Gate-to-Owner Matrix

Each gate's checks trace to the sections that own their rules.

| Gate                     | Enforces rules owned by                              |
| ------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------- |
| Story Quality Gate       | Part 2 (Story Engine)                                |
| Screenplay Quality Gate  | Part 3 (Screenplay Engine)                           |
| Shot Quality Gate        | Part 4.1.2–4.1.9                                     |
| Storyboard Quality Gate  | Part 4.1.6, 4.1.7, 4.1.8, 4.1.10, 4.1.11             |
| Render Quality Gate      | Part 5 (Rendering Platform), Part 6 (provenance)     |
| Composition Quality Gate | Part 5, Part 6                                       |
| Narration & Audio Gate   | Part 3 (narration), Part 5 (audio)                   |
| Packaging Quality Gate   | Part 6 (packaging & metadata)                        |
| Publication Quality Gate | Part 6, Part 7.4 (approval), Governance (non-waivable)|
| Cross-Stage Coherence    | Part 4, Part 5, Part 7                               |

Every gate enforces rules owned elsewhere. No gate authors a rule.

---

# Owner-to-Gate Matrix

Each defining section traces to the gates that enforce its rules.

| Owning section          | Enforced by                                          |
| ----------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------- |
| Part 2 (Story)          | Story Quality Gate                                   |
| Part 3 (Screenplay)     | Screenplay Gate, Narration & Audio Gate              |
| Part 4 (Shot/Storyboard)| Shot Gate, Storyboard Gate, Cross-Stage Coherence    |
| Part 5 (Rendering)      | Render Gate, Composition Gate, Narration & Audio Gate |
| Part 6 (Execution)      | Render, Composition, Packaging, Publication Gates    |
| Part 7.4 (Approval)     | Publication Gate, editorial gates                    |
| Governance (7.1.10)     | Publication Gate (non-waivable checks)               |

The reverse mapping confirms that every quality-critical section's rules are enforced by at least one gate. No owned quality rule is left unenforced.

---

# Cross-Reference to Prior Gate Definitions

Part 7 unifies gates defined earlier in the specification.

| Prior definition            | Unified as                          |
| --------------------------- | ----------------------------------- |
| Part 4.1.12 Shot Gate       | 7.2.4 (instance of 7.1)             |
| Part 4.1.12 Storyboard Gate | 7.2.5 (instance of 7.1)             |
| Part 4.1.1 Storyboard Approval | 7.4.3 (editorial gate)            |
| Part 6.3.24 Quality Gates   | generalized by 7.1                  |
| Part 6.1 Human Approval Before High-Cost | 7.4.3 (Storyboard Approval) |
| Part 6.2 verdict caching    | 7.1.1 (verdict bound to identity)   |

Part 7 does not contradict any prior gate definition; it generalizes them into instances of one architecture. Where a prior Part defined a gate locally, Part 7 re-expresses it as an instance without changing its behavior.

---

# Guarantee-to-Section Traceability

Each of the ten guarantees (7.5.2) traces to the sections that establish it.

| Guarantee                    | Established in                     |
| ---------------------------- | ---------------------------------- |
| G7-01 Determinism            | 7.1.5, 7.3.3                       |
| G7-02 Fail-Closed            | 7.1.5                              |
| G7-03 Enforce, Not Author    | 7.1.1, 7.2.1                       |
| G7-04 Single Model           | 7.1.3                             |
| G7-05 Complete Coverage      | 7.2.1, 7.2.11                     |
| G7-06 Traceability           | 7.1.8, 7.3.6, 7.4.6               |
| G7-07 Mandatory Floor        | 7.3.1, 7.3.7, 7.4.1              |
| G7-08 Non-Waivable Floor     | 7.1.10, 7.2.10                    |
| G7-09 Separation of Duties   | 7.1.10, 7.4.1                     |
| G7-10 Immutability In-Build  | 7.1.11, 7.3.4                     |

Every guarantee is anchored in specific subsections, so the platform's quality claim (7.5.2) is fully traceable to its establishing sections.

---

# Traceability Is Bidirectional and Complete

The matrix satisfies two completeness properties.

* **No ownerless check.** Every check in every gate names an owning section (7.1.4). The gate-to-owner matrix has no gap.
* **No unenforced quality rule.** Every quality-critical rule owned by a section is enforced by at least one gate. The owner-to-gate matrix has no gap.

Together these make the enforcement web complete: rules flow from owners to gates, verdicts flow from gates to reports, and every link is traceable in both directions.

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant P7T-701

Every check traces to an owning section, and every owning section traces to the gates that enforce it.

---

## Invariant P7T-702

The gate-to-owner matrix has no gap: no check is ownerless.

---

## Invariant P7T-703

The owner-to-gate matrix has no gap: no quality-critical rule is unenforced.

---

## Invariant P7T-704

Part 7 generalizes prior gate definitions without contradicting them.

---

## Invariant P7T-705

The Shot and Storyboard gates of Part 4.1.12 are re-expressed unchanged as instances of Part 7.1.

---

## Invariant P7T-706

Each of the ten platform quality guarantees traces to its establishing subsections.

---

## Invariant P7T-707

Traceability is bidirectional: from owners to gates and from gates to owners.

---

## Invariant P7T-708

The enforcement web is complete: rules flow to gates, verdicts flow to reports, every link traceable.

---

| ADR-1103 | No quality-critical rule is unenforced; the owner-to-gate matrix has no gap.          |
| ADR-1104 | Part 7 generalizes prior gate definitions without contradicting them.                 |

| ADR-1106 | Each of the ten guarantees traces to its establishing subsections.                    |

| ADR-1108 | The enforcement web is complete and fully traceable.                                 |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

* The gate-to-owner matrix is presented and shown to have no gap.
* The owner-to-gate matrix is presented and shown to have no gap.
* The cross-reference unifying prior gate definitions is presented.

# Part 7.5.4 — Part 7 Acceptance Criteria

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section states the **acceptance criteria for Part 7 as a whole**: the conditions under which the Quality Gates specification is complete and the platform's quality control is established.

Each subsection of Part 7 carried its own acceptance criteria. This section states the whole-of-Part-7 criteria — the authoritative definition of "done" for the entire quality architecture.

---

# Part 7 Acceptance Criteria

Part 7 is complete when all of the following hold.

* A single, reusable Quality Gate architecture is defined: anatomy, checks, verdict semantics, classification, composition, reporting, lifecycle, governance, and configuration (7.1).
* Every gate is deterministic and fail-closed, returns exactly {PASS, FAIL} with an immutable report, and enforces only rules owned by upstream sections (7.1).
* Every pipeline stage boundary is guarded by exactly one stage-exit gate, each an instance of the architecture (7.2).
* The Shot and Storyboard gates of Part 4.1.12 are re-expressed as instances of the architecture, unchanged in behavior (7.2.4, 7.2.5).
* Cross-stage coherence gates guard every drift-prone transformation, including render↔storyboard and published↔approved (7.2.11).
* The Publication Gate carries non-waivable rights and safety checks that no waiver can release (7.2.10).
* Quality is measured above the mandatory floor by deterministic metrics and scores that never rescue a mandatory FAIL or lower the floor (7.3).
* Regression is detected against a baseline and surfaced even on passing builds (7.3.5).
* Quality is surfaced through a drill-downable dashboard that observes but never enforces (7.3.6).
* A score blocks only through a declared `threshold_score` gate or configured blocking regression, always fail-closed and additive to the floor (7.3.7).
* Human approval is required at high-consequence boundaries, is identity-bound, scoped, revocable, and never releases a mandatory or non-waivable check (7.4).
* Every approval decision is recorded in an append-only audit log, making a published trailer's editorial history fully reconstructable (7.4.6).
* The ten platform quality guarantees hold for every gate at every boundary (7.5.2).
* Every check traces to an owning section and every quality rule traces to an enforcing gate, bidirectionally and completely (7.5.3).

When every criterion holds, Part 7 is closed and the platform's quality control is established end to end.

---

# The Part 7 Acceptance Statement

> **The platform's quality is controlled by a single, uniform gate architecture instantiated at every boundary, measured above a mandatory floor that scoring and approval can only strengthen, topped with human judgment where consequence demands it, and made fully traceable and auditable end to end.**

This statement is the whole of what Part 7 delivers. Each acceptance criterion above is a testable condition that upholds it.

---

# Acceptance Criteria Traceability

Each Part 7 acceptance criterion maps to its owning section.

| Criterion theme               | Owning section  |
| ----------------------------- | --------------- |
| Reusable gate architecture    | 7.1             |
| Deterministic, fail-closed    | 7.1.5           |
| Every boundary gated          | 7.2.1           |
| Prior gates re-expressed      | 7.2.4, 7.2.5    |
| Cross-stage coherence         | 7.2.11          |
| Non-waivable floor            | 7.2.10, 7.1.10  |
| Measurement above the floor   | 7.3             |
| Regression detection          | 7.3.5           |
| Observability, not enforcement| 7.3.6           |
| Scored enforcement            | 7.3.7           |
| Human approval                | 7.4             |
| Approval audit                | 7.4.6           |
| Consolidated guarantees       | 7.5.2           |
| Traceability                  | 7.5.3           |

Every criterion is anchored, so Part 7's completeness is itself traceable.

---

# Architectural Invariants

Part 7 is complete only when every whole-of-Part-7 acceptance criterion holds.

---

Each acceptance criterion is a testable condition anchored in an owning section.

---

The Part 7 acceptance statement is upheld by the conjunction of the acceptance criteria.

---

---

---

---

---

## Invariant P7A-708

Part 7 is closed only when the platform's quality control is established end to end.

# Part 7.5.5 — Transition to Part 8

## Insynergy Cinematic Thought Leadership Platform

### Master Specification v2.1

---

# Purpose

This section closes **Part 7 — Quality Gates** and defines the transition to Part 8.

Part 7 defined the platform's quality control: what a gate is, where gates run, how quality is measured, and where human judgment enters. This section states what Part 7 hands to Part 8 and what Part 8 may and may not do with it.

---

# Part 7 Closure

Part 7 defined the quality control architecture in full.

```text
7.1  → Quality Gate Architecture
7.2  → Pipeline Stage Quality Gates
7.3  → Quality Metrics, Scoring & Enforcement
7.4  → Human Approval & Editorial Gates
7.5  → Acceptance & Transition
```

The platform now has a uniform, complete, measured, and accountable quality control system. Every stage boundary is gated, every gate is an instance of one architecture, quality is measured above a mandatory floor, and human judgment is recorded and audited where consequence demands it.

---

# What Part 7 Hands Forward

Part 7 hands Part 8 a defined set of quality gates and their contracts.

```text
Part 7
Quality Gates (definitions, verdicts, reports, approvals)
        │
        ▼
Downstream Contract
        │
        ▼
Part 8
GitHub Actions & CI/CD Orchestration
```

Part 7 delivers to Part 8:

* the gate definitions and the gate chain (7.1, 7.2);
* the verdict and report contracts the CI/CD system must honor (7.1.5, 7.1.8);
* the human-approval dependencies the pipeline must wait on (7.4.4);
* the governance and audit obligations the automation must record (7.1.10, 7.4.6).

---

# Part 8 Executes the Gates; It Does Not Redefine Them

Part 8 orchestrates the gates in a CI/CD environment; it does not change them.

Part 8 defines how the platform runs on GitHub Actions or an equivalent runner: how gates are invoked as CI steps, how verdicts halt or advance a workflow, how human approvals are surfaced as CI approvals, and how reports and audit logs are persisted as CI artifacts.

Part 8 may not:

* redefine gate anatomy, verdict semantics, or the fail-closed model;
* weaken a mandatory or non-waivable check to fit a CI constraint;
* substitute a CI success signal for a gate verdict;
* bypass a human-approval dependency through automation.

Part 8 is the execution substrate for Part 7's gates. It honors the verdicts; it never overrides them, exactly as the Orchestrator does within a build (7.1.1).

---

# The Boundary Is a Formal Contract

The handoff from Part 7 to Part 8 is a formal contract.

```text
Part 7 produces:  gate definitions, verdict contract, report contract, approval dependencies
Part 8 consumes:  and orchestrates them in CI/CD, honoring every verdict
```

Part 8 consumes Part 7's contracts and runs them in an automated environment. The contract is that Part 8 executes gates faithfully — invoking each gate, honoring each verdict, waiting on each approval, and persisting each report and audit entry — without altering any gate's behavior.

A CI/CD system that could pass a build whose gate returned FAIL would violate this contract and the fail-closed guarantee (G7-02). Part 8 runs the gates; it does not get a vote on their verdicts.

---

# Architectural Invariants

## Invariant P7X-701

Part 7 hands Part 8 a complete set of gate definitions, verdict and report contracts, and approval dependencies.

---

## Invariant P7X-702

Part 8 executes the gates in a CI/CD environment and never redefines them.

---

## Invariant P7X-703

Part 8 never weakens a mandatory or non-waivable check to fit a CI constraint.

---

## Invariant P7X-704

Part 8 never substitutes a CI success signal for a gate verdict.

---

## Invariant P7X-705

Part 8 never bypasses a human-approval dependency through automation.

---

## Invariant P7X-706

Part 8 honors every gate verdict and never overrides one.

---

## Invariant P7X-707

Part 8 persists gate reports and audit entries as durable CI artifacts.

---

## Invariant P7X-708

The Part 7 to Part 8 handoff is a formal contract, not an informal process note.

---

# Architectural Decision Records

| ADR      | Decision                                                                            |
| -------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ADR-1117 | Part 7 hands Part 8 complete gate definitions, verdict/report contracts, and approvals. |
| ADR-1118 | Part 8 executes the gates in CI/CD and never redefines or weakens them.               |
| ADR-1119 | Part 8 honors every gate verdict and never substitutes a CI signal for it.            |
| ADR-1120 | The Part 7 to Part 8 handoff is a formal contract.                                   |

---

# Acceptance Criteria

Section **7.5.5** is complete when:

* Part 7 is formally closed across its five sections.
* What Part 7 hands to Part 8 is enumerated.
* Part 8's role as executor, not redefiner, of the gates is established.
* The prohibitions on Part 8 weakening, substituting, or bypassing gates are defined.
* The handoff is established as a formal contract.
* Invariants P7X-701 through P7X-708 and ADR-1117 through ADR-1120 are established.

---

# Transition to Part 8

Part 7 ends where automation begins.

```text
Part 7
Quality Gates
        │
        ▼
Part 8
GitHub Actions & CI/CD Orchestration
```

Part 8 runs the platform's pipeline — and its quality gates — on a CI/CD substrate. It invokes each gate as an automated step, halts on FAIL, advances on PASS, surfaces human approvals as CI approvals, and persists every report and audit entry. It honors the gates defined in Part 7 exactly; it does not reopen gate anatomy, verdict semantics, the mandatory floor, or the non-waivable floor.

Part 7 is complete. CI/CD orchestration begins in Part 8.

---

# Part 7 Completion Statement

Part **7 — Quality Gates** is complete.

It defines the platform's quality control end to end: a single, reusable gate architecture (7.1); a gate at every pipeline boundary plus cross-stage coherence gates (7.2); deterministic quality measurement, scoring, regression detection, and enforcement strictly above a mandatory floor (7.3); and human approval at high-consequence boundaries, identity-bound and fully audited (7.4). The whole is consolidated into ten platform quality guarantees, a complete bidirectional traceability matrix, and a formal handoff to Part 8 (7.5).

Every trailer the platform releases has passed every mandatory check at every boundary, met every required quality threshold, satisfied every cross-stage coherence check, cleared every non-waivable rights and safety check, carried every required human approval on its exact identity, and left a complete, immutable, deterministic audit trail of all of it.

The Quality Gates are established. CI/CD orchestration follows in Part 8.
